1935.08.01

The Subei Embankment is Completed: The Rising Waters of Weishan Lake Flood Southward to Pêi East. Representatives from Shandong Return to Heze After Inspection. Both the Yun and Yi Rivers are Rising.

T'ungshan Dispatch: Following the rapid rise of the Weishan Lake waters, they are now flooding southward from the north bank, having reached Pêi East. Within days, they are expected to flood the south bank. The Weishan Lake Embankment has been fully completed. After inspection, representatives from Shandong believe that the Subei Embankment is located on the west bank of Weishan Lake and is unrelated to the Yellow River's entry into the Grand Canal, resolving the misunderstanding. (31st Dispatch)

(Hsüchow) Shao Han-yüan, Wang Kung-yü, Yü Shu-fang, and Shandong representatives Sun Tse-jang and others, after inspecting the Weishan Lake Embankment in Pêi yesterday, returned to Hsüchow that night. Shao stated that the water coming from the north is very strong, and the floodwaters have reached Pêi East, and will soon flood Weishan Lake. A large part of the south bank embankment has been completed. Representatives from Shandong have had their misunderstandings about the construction of the Subei Embankment resolved. During discussions with Sun and others in Pêi, it was agreed that the construction of a dam in Linp'u, western Shandong, to block the upstream source is urgently needed. Sun and others returned to Hoze this afternoon. Shao is scheduled to go to Linchia Dam with Wang Kung-yü and Yü Shu-fang tomorrow for inspection. The reconstruction of the dam has been completed, and after inspection, a request will be made to the province to install a sluice gate for opening and closing. Construction of the Chingshan Embankment outside of Linchia Dam has begun. The embankment is seven li long and is expected to be completed in one week. (31st Dispatch)

(Nanking) The Yellow River is rapidly flowing into Weishan Lake, endangering the Kiangsu Embankment. In addition to ordering the Yellow River Commission to send personnel for investigation, the Economic Commission will convene a meeting within days with the governors of Kiangsu and Shandong, the heads of the Huai River and Yellow River Commissions, and various engineers to discuss a thorough reorganization plan. (31st Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Ch'ingkiangp'u) The water in the Grand Canal rose one inch today. The Yi River is still rising rapidly. The Huai-P'i Section Works Office has divided the central Grand Canal into four flood prevention sections and assigned personnel responsible for flood control. Director Feng Tan accompanied Ku Chi-chih, a technician from the Construction Bureau, to P'i and Su this morning to inspect the water conditions at Liu Lao Chien and the Ten Village River, then proceeded to Hsüchow to inspect the Subei Embankment project and the water level of Weishan Lake. (31st Central News Agency Dispatch)

The Water Level of the Han River Continues to Recede; The Dikes are Completely Out of Danger.

(Hankow) The river water receded 5.5 inches on the 31st, with a water mark of 46.75, a relatively rapid rate of recession. The dikes are completely out of danger. (31st Dispatch)

(Hankow) According to records from the Chiang Han Customs water mark, at 4:00 PM on the 31st, the water level in Changsha was 18.7, Yochow was 42.9, and Hankow was 47.0, a decrease of 4 inches compared to the same time on the 30th. (31st Central News Agency Dispatch)

The Yungting River Rose Three Feet in Half a Day. The River Authority Cables Each Section to Take Strict Precautions.

(Tientsin) Before 7:00 AM on the 31st, the water level at Huilung Temple on the Yungting River was 9 feet. After 7:00 AM, it suddenly rose 2 feet, increasing to 11 feet, and continuing to rise to 12 feet, a rise of 3 feet in half a day. The water was muddy yellow and extremely turbulent. The Director of the River Authority recabled all sections to take strict precautions. According to a telegram from Huailai County upstream, there was a flash flood, expected to arrive in two days. The water level at Huilung Temple is expected to increase to 18 feet. In addition to ordering employees to protect the dikes, the Authority has sent a special telegram to the provincial government requesting an emergency allocation of 11,000 yuan for flood prevention and 30,000 yuan for rescue expenses. (31st Dispatch)

(Peiping) After a sharp rise to 11.5 feet last night, the water in the Yungting River was quite rapid. Fortunately, by 2:00 PM today, it had fallen 1.5 feet, with the current water level at 10 feet. (31st Dispatch)

The North Grand Canal Flooded; Dozens of Villages Were Submerged.

(Tientsin) The North Grand Canal flooded, with the water suddenly rising more than 3 feet on the 30th. The water overflowed on both banks. Dozens of nearby villages were flooded. The Yangts'un T'ien Ch'i Temple, the Ch'ingchen Mosque, and the Peichuang Temple were all submerged to varying degrees, from two to three feet. Crops were all submerged. The Lungfeng River, affected by the floodwaters from the North Grand Canal, also rose significantly. The Lungfeng Control Sluice on the river has not been completed, and the riverbed has been silted up for a long time, preventing it from being used as a dike, causing the floodwaters to be trapped. On the night of the 30th, the water also overflowed. More than a thousand acres of fertile land were submerged in thirty villages along the river, including Huangchuang, Lao Mi Tien, San Li T'un, and Tungchou. The water level is still rising. (31st Dispatch)

The Luan River Raged, Washing Away Both East and West Banks.

(Tientsin) There were two days of heavy rain in Locheng County. By the 30th, flash floods had washed through, and the Locheng River continued to rise by three feet on the 30th, with white waves surging skyward and the river being unusually turbulent. Due to the rapid flow of water, a newly built section of the rear bank made of stones was washed away. There was a breach of about 16 feet on the east bank and a breach of 21 feet on the west bank. Officials and citizens are gathering to try to close the breaches. (31st Dispatch)

(Peiping) The Locheng River continued to rise by three feet, and the unfinished levee collapsed and was washed away. (31st Dispatch)

The Anhwei Provincial Government Cables the Executive Yüan Requesting to Swiftly Block the Yellow River Breach.

(Anking) The Provincial Government sent a telegram to the Executive Yüan and the National Economic Council requesting that the breach in the Yellow River be swiftly blocked and that attention be paid to the embankment on the south bank. (31st Dispatch)

The Rain Has Stopped in Eastern Tientsin; The Waters of Each River Have Receded Slightly.

(Tientsin) The heavy rain in eastern Tientsin stopped on the 30th. The water levels of each river have receded slightly, and the danger has been averted. However, a large number of wheat seedlings and cotton plants have been washed away, making the autumn harvest hopeless. Local authorities in each county have sent telegrams to report to the provincial government. The Tangshan Public Security Bureau, in collaboration with the security forces, is repairing roads and waterways. If it does not rain, traffic can be restored in three days. (31st Dispatch)

The Yangtze River Flood is Severe; The Central Government Has Decided to Allocate One Million Yuan for Relief; Distributed to the Four Provinces of Hunan, Hupeh, Kiangsi, and Anhwei for Disaster Relief; The Disaster Relief Preparations Fund Custody Committee is Established; K'ung and Hsü Met Yesterday to Discuss Disaster Relief Measures.

(Nanking) Of the two million yuan allocated for disaster relief preparedness in the second budget reserve for this year, the original plan was to allocate just over ten thousand yuan per month, so that two million yuan would be fully allocated within a year. Now, because the Yangtze River flood is so severe, it has been decided to allocate one million yuan at once, to be distributed to the four provinces of Hunan, Hupeh, Kiangsi, and Anhwei for disaster relief. As for the counties in the four provinces that have been affected, according to reports from the Accounting Committee, there are seven counties in southern Hunan, fifty counties and the city of Hankow in Hupeh, forty-eight counties in Kiangsi, and thirteen counties in Anhwei. The Accounting Committee received a telegram from Kiangsi Province stating that forty-nine counties in Kiangsi Province have been affected by the flood, with 2,881,700 mu of farmland submerged. There are now 1,857,300 disaster victims awaiting relief. (31st Dispatch)

(Nanking) The inaugural meeting of the Disaster Relief Preparations Fund Custody Committee was held at Shen time on the 31st, followed by the first committee meeting. Those in attendance were Hsü Shih-ying, K'ung Hsiang-hsi (represented by Tsou Lin), Wang Chen, Chu Ch'ing-lan (represented by Wang Chen), K'ung Hsiang-jung (represented by Chu Yung). Hsü reported on: 1. The process of establishing the Disaster Relief Preparations Fund Bill; 2. The number of committee members present and reading related telegrams; 3. The positions and names of appointed personnel; 4. An order from the Executive Yüan for the Ministry of Health to organize mobile medical teams to go to the disaster areas for diagnosis, treatment, and epidemic prevention, with an initial allocation of 40,000 yuan from the disaster relief preparations fund; 5. The situation of urging various provinces to organize disaster relief preparations fund custody committees. Proposals: 1. Formulating the working rules of this committee. Resolution: Amended and approved. 2. Specifying the dates for meetings of this committee and the standing committee. Resolution: Committee meetings are scheduled to be held on the last Thursday afternoon of each month, and the dates for standing committee meetings will not be specified for the time being and may be convened at any time. 3. Urging various provincial governments to form disaster relief preparations fund custody committees. According to the report from this committee chair, A. Hupeh, Hunan, Kiangsi, and Anhwei are hurrying to organize. Kiangsi Province has submitted a list of committee members and submitted it to the Executive Yüan for approval. B. The Yüan ordered Chekiang, Chahar, Shantung, and Suiyuan Provinces, as well as Tientsin City, to reply by telegram, and each department is being notified to comply. C. The remaining provinces and cities are being urged for inquiries. Resolution: Please ask the Ministry of Interior and the Disaster Relief Committee to jointly urge the provinces and cities to establish committees by a specific date. 4. Chairman Hsü's report on inspecting the disaster situation in the provinces along the river and presenting the political Yüan's disaster relief plan. Resolution: It will be followed up after receiving the order from the Executive Yüan and submitting it to this committee. As for the personnel of the committee, it was decided that the chief secretary will be Huang, with the style name Po-tu, the secretary and director of the General Affairs Section will be Hu Mai, with the style name Chung-shu, and the secretary and director of the Custody Section will be Chou Yi-k'uei, with the style name Hsü-sheng. They will begin work this month and report to the Executive Yüan for the record. (31st Dispatch)

(Nanking) Hsü Shih-ying went to the Executive Yüan at 5:00 PM on the 31st to visit Acting President K'ung Hsien-hsi to discuss ways to relieve the flood in the four provinces of Hunan, Hupeh, Kiangsi, and Anhwei. Hsü said that the situation of the flood in the provinces along the river was dire and pitiful, and that the vitality of the people had been exhausted, and relief could not be delayed. Of the four provinces he had visited, Hupeh was the most severely affected, followed by Hunan and Kiangsi, and Anhwei was the least affected. The disaster relief measures he had presented included both short-term and long-term relief. The fundamental solution lies in reorganizing, and he is currently drafting a fundamental solution that includes all water conservancy issues of the Yangtze, Huai, Yellow, and Han Rivers, as well as those that should be repaired and reorganized. The draft will be completed in two days and submitted to the central government for adoption. Due to the severity of this disaster, in addition to government allocations for relief, all parties must also contribute. Philanthropists and the municipal government in Shanghai have launched a fundraising campaign. He is scheduled to take the Chiang An ship to Shanghai on the 2nd to report the disaster situation to all parties and plan for fundraising. He will not stay in Shanghai for long and plans to go to P'ing and Yü to inspect the Yellow River's water situation and disaster situation. He will first go to K'ai, inspect along the Yellow River, and return via Shantung. The departure date must be determined after arriving in Shanghai. Whether or not he will go to Chihli will be determined after considering the situation. (31st Dispatch)

The National Economic Council Received a Report Regarding the Breach of the Yellow River Embankment.

(Nanking) The Water Conservancy Department of the National Economic Council recently received a report stating that the flow of the Yellow River has increased from over 40 cubic meters to over 5,000 cubic meters. At the same time, a section of the embankment between the Fifth and Sixth breaches suddenly collapsed, covering a large area and creating a serious situation. It is said that although the water volume is currently increasing, the riverbed is very shallow and the water force is not turbulent. If the autumn flood arrives, it will be even more dangerous. Efforts are currently being made to construct and maintain the embankment. (31st Central News Agency Dispatch)

Chairman Chiang Ordered Each Province to Recruit Labor to Dredge Rivers and Build Embankments.

(Hankow) Chiang telegraphed the provincial governments along the river, stating that this year's major flood has caused disaster, and he has already telegraphed all armies to donate funds for relief. However, the way to govern and bring peace is still to dredge rivers and build embankments, which is a matter of urgency. During this flood, the recruitment of labor should be prepared according to the regulations of the Executive Headquarters for dredging rivers and building embankments. Refugees should also be recruited for work relief, treating both the symptoms and the root causes, as a permanent solution. (31st Dispatch)

The Shantung River Affairs Bureau Plans to Block the Breaches in the Embankment.

(Tsinan) The River Bureau telegraphed the provincial government reporting that the breaches in the embankment are being severely eroded. The head of the eastern embankment has not collapsed. Chang Lien-chia will return to Tsinan to discuss blocking and building measures. (31st Dispatch)

(Tsinan) The San-yu River rose again today. The River Bureau ordered the counties along the embankment to fill and reinforce it. (31st Dispatch)

(Tsinan) Chang Yüeh inspected the refugee camps in T'ai and Yen Counties and returned to Tsinan today. (31st Dispatch)

(Tsinan) The San-yu Yellow River in Shantung Province has risen today. The water level at Lokou has risen 4.3 centimeters to 29.23 meters. (31st Dispatch)

(Tsinan) The Magistrate of Chin Hsiang County telegraphed that the lake water has increased, and the embankments built along the lake are in danger and are being urgently blocked. (31st Dispatch)

The Water Level at Hsia-Kuan Rose Slightly.

(Nanking) Due to the arrival of the flood season, the water level at Hsia-Kuan on the 31st continued to increase. According to records from the Public Works Bureau, the maximum water level at noon reached 53.84 meters, an increase of 1 centimeter compared to the afternoon of the 30th. By 5:00 PM, it was 53.73 meters, a slight decrease. (31st Dispatch)

The Yung River Has Been Rising Rapidly for Days, Flooding the Riverside Streets.

(Hong Kong) The Yung River has been rising rapidly for days. From the 25th to the 29th, it rose more than 30 feet. The riverside streets have all been flooded. (31st Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Amoy) There was a violent storm with wind and rain all night on the 30th. The rain stopped after daybreak on the 31st, but the wind did not diminish. After the planes from Shanghai and Kwangtung passed through Amoy, the sky darkened again in the afternoon, and the wind and rain intensified, not stopping at 9:00 or 10:00 PM. The ships in the inner harbor, as well as the trains to Changchow and Chuanchow in Amoy, were still stopped. The water in Changchow rose again. The water depth along the Chiu-lung River and the Kiangtung Bridge was 2 feet. Small boats between Amoy and Kulangsu were taking risks to ferry passengers, charging 2 jiao per person. The temperature dropped to 77 degrees in the evening. (31st Dispatch)

(Amoy) According to a telephone call from Changchow, there was heavy rain on the 30th and 31st. On the 31st, the water in the Chiu-lung River rose by more than 10 feet. It reached the shore at 3:00 PM and rose to the Ma-p'ing Street at 5:00 PM. The water was turbulent at night, even more severe than the previous time. Heavy rain continued after 8:00 PM. Traffic was cut off everywhere, creating a second flood disaster. The Amoy-Amoy power lines were repaired on the evening of the 31st, but the Chuanchow-Amoy lines had not yet been restored to their original state. (31st Dispatch)

(Foochow) The typhoon in this city had subsided by the afternoon of the 30th. The wind completely stopped by the morning of the 31st. Many houses collapsed on the city walls. (31st Central News Agency Dispatch) (Nanking) According to a message from the Central Meteorological Observatory, the typhoon had entered the area between Kweilin and Wuchow by the afternoon of the 31st. The wind force decreased and changed direction to the southwest, and it will disappear within days in Yunnan and Kweichow. (31st Central News Agency Dispatch)

The National Economic Council Issued Two Major Demerits Against Yang Szu-lien.

(Nanking) During the tense flood control situation in Hankow caused by the major flood, Yang Szu-lien, Director of the Chiang Han Public Works Bureau, requested sick leave and went directly to the hospital, which drew criticism from all sides. The National Economic Council sent personnel to investigate and found that although he had been telegraphed to work diligently despite his illness, he still delayed, resulting in the abandonment of bureau affairs. Although Wuhan did not suffer a major disaster, it is difficult to absolve him of the blame for negligence. On the 21st, an order was issued to give the bureau director two major demerits as a warning, but during the major flood season, he is still responsible for earning merit to offset his demerits, supervising his subordinates, and strictly defending the area. It must also be thoroughly investigated and punished whether civil servants have been negligent in their duties. (31st Dispatch)

The German Reporter Müller Arrived in Changyuan After Being Released.

(Peiping) Ch'in Te-ch'un received a telephone report from Changyuan stating that the German reporter Müller, who was kidnapped by bandits in Paoch'ang, had been released by the bandits and arrived in Changyuan at 3:30 PM on the 31st. He is scheduled to return to P'ing on the 1st for rest and recuperation. After receiving the telegram, Ch'in immediately notified the German Embassy and reported to both the Military and Political Affairs Committees. (31st Dispatch)

(Peiping) Regarding the kidnapping of British and German reporters Jones and Müller, there were rumors yesterday that Müller had left the bandits' lair and would arrive in Changyuan today, but as of this afternoon, there has been no official report. Relevant parties are still trying their best to rescue them. After the British and German reporters were kidnapped, the P'ing Military Branch sent a telegram this afternoon to the Chahar Provincial Government, asking them to take responsibility for a swift rescue. Ch'in Te-ch'un inquired about the rescue situation with Chen Ying in Changyuan by long-distance telephone this afternoon and also asked Hsiao to inquire about whether the German reporter was out of danger. Hsiao was originally scheduled to leave Changyuan for P'ing this morning, but because he had to handle the rescue in Chahar, he changed his departure to tomorrow morning. (31st Dispatch)

(Peiping) Rumors have it that after the German reporter Miller was kidnapped by bandits, the bandits saw that he was unusually weak and feared for his life if he stayed in the bandits' lair for too long. Therefore, they released him yesterday morning. After regaining his freedom, Miller rushed to Paoch'ang and reported to the German China Automobile Company in Changyuan by long-distance telephone, saying that he had escaped danger and arrived in Paoch'ang and would be able to go to Changyuan from Paoch'ang today. However, as of this afternoon, neither the Chinese nor foreign parties have received an accurate report of Miller's whereabouts. (31st Dispatch)

(Peiping) Mr. Sa, a counselor at the British Embassy, visited Wang K'e-min at the Political Reorganization Committee at 10:00 AM today, asking the Chinese government to quickly find a way to rescue Jones. Wang promised to telegram the Chahar Provincial authorities to do their best to rescue him. After Mr. Sa visited Wang, he told people that the news that the German reporter Miller had left the bandits' lair was only seen in the newspapers, and the details were still unknown. But in any case, Jones is still not out of danger. Mr. Sa, a military officer at the British Embassy, is currently traveling in the Lei-tien Ranch in Outer Mongolia. This morning, he telegraphed P'ing, saying that he would rush from Lei-tien to Changyuan to assist the Chinese government in finding a way to rescue him. (31st Dispatch)

(Peiping) Japanese Military Attaché Takahashi stated that the kidnapping location of the British and German reporters was on the border of Chahar Province, 50 li east of Paoch'ang. If the Japanese side needs to contribute to the rescue, the Japanese side will do its best to assist so that the reporters can escape danger as soon as possible. (31st Dispatch)

(Peiping) Feng Chih-an came to P'ing from Changyuan at 6:00 PM on the 31st. According to him, the German reporter has been released, but the British reporter is still not out of danger. The Chahar Provincial Government is intensifying its rescue efforts. The Magistrate of Paoch'ang County reported that there were no Chinese security teams at the kidnapping location. No formal contact has yet been made, so the conditions demanded by the bandits are not very clear. Hsiao Chen-ying still has matters to deal with in Chahar, and it is uncertain whether he will be able to return to P'ing on the 1st. (31st Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Peiping) According to news from Chinese sources in Changyuan, the commander of the Paoch'ang militia has contacted the bandit leader who kidnapped Jones. It is said that the bandit leader is demanding a ransom of 50,000 yuan. Dr. Müller, who escaped danger yesterday, has not yet made any statements today. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

(Peiping) According to Japanese Deputy Military Attaché Takahashi stationed in P'ing today, the Kwantung Army has ordered the Japanese army in Jehol and the Japanese Military Affairs Group in Changyuan to assist the Chinese authorities in rescuing Mr. Jones. It is said that several teams of Japanese soldiers have been ordered to go and search. It is now known that before Jones left P'ing, the British Embassy advised him not to go to Dolon Nor via Inner Mongolia. According to news from Changyuan by telephone, Dr. Müller took a car to Changyuan after being released by the bandits, but has not yet arrived. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

(Peiping) The British reporter Jones is still not out of danger. The Chahar Provincial Government has dispatched Platoon Leader Chang of the Paoch'ang Security Team to negotiate with the bandit leader in person. However, the bandits are demanding a ransom of 50,000 yuan, and it is still unknown whether he can escape danger safely. (31st Dispatch)

The Riotous Bandits Attacked Tungchow; The Luho Middle School Was Unsuccessful.

(Peiping) At around 3:00 AM this morning, there were sudden gunshots in the Tungchow area, saying that a dozen or so riotous bandits attempted to attack the Luho Middle School. Because the school was heavily guarded, they were unsuccessful. Although the residents were alarmed for a time, they have returned to normal. According to another telephone call from Tungchow, at around 3:00 AM this morning, gunshots suddenly rang out quite densely at the North Gate, West Gate, and South Gate of Tungchow. Residents were extremely frightened by the sudden attack by the riotous bandits. By the time the garrison from Nanyuan arrived, the bandits were gone. It is said that the bandits' target was the Luho Middle School, but the school had its own self-defense police, so the bandits were unsuccessful and retreated to the northeast. According to the Luho Middle School police and the railway workers in Tung County, there were very few bandits. Because the Luho Middle School police fought back very hard, the gunshots were very dense. The security of Tung County has returned to normal this morning. (31st Dispatch)

(Tientsin) According to a telephone call from Tung County, a large group of bandits suddenly appeared outside the South Gate of Tung County early on the 30th, attempting to surround Luho Middle School and rob it. A fierce battle broke out with the school's guards. For a time, gunshots rang out loudly, and residents were startled awake from their dreams, fleeing in panic. Later, with the joint attack of the security team and the militia, the bandit forces could not resist and fled into the green gauze tents. Order was not restored until 10:00 AM. (31st Dispatch)

The Bandits in Ch'ien-an Sacked the Town of T'ai-p'ing-chai.

(Tientsin) T'ai-p'ing-chai in the southeast of Ch'ien-an County was broken through by Yang, a bandit leader, leading 1,500 men. On the 27th, the bandits entered the town, looting and massacring over 600 households. No merchants or residents were spared. Chi Shu-fan, the Director of the Public Security Bureau, led the police to resist, but they were outnumbered. The bandits disarmed them. Chi and more than 20 police officers were abducted by the bandits and their whereabouts are unknown. The bandits occupied the town overnight, and on the 28th, they kidnapped over 300 men and women and withdrew, then returned at night and occupied the town. The Ch'ien-an Security Team has mobilized a large force to suppress them. (31st Dispatch)

Peace in the City of Peiping; Martial Law May Be Lifted Within Days.

(Peiping) The order in the city of Peiping has been stable for half a month, and the people's hearts are at ease. Martial Law Commander Wang Shu-ch'ang, in view of the fact that long-term martial law has a great impact on various businesses, and residents of the city also feel inconvenienced, specially asked the authorities this morning whether martial law could be lifted. After consideration, it was decided to hand it over to the Martial Law Command to handle it according to the situation. After receiving the order, Wang immediately convened Shao Wen-k'ai, the commander of the Gendarmerie, and Chu Jui-lin, the acting director of the Public Security Bureau, at the command this afternoon to discuss everything. It is said that as a result of the discussion, it has been planned to lift martial law starting tomorrow. If it cannot be realized temporarily, the duration of martial law must be shortened at the very least. (31st Dispatch)

Ho and Hsü Discussed Measures to Suppress the Remnant Bandits.

Hsü Yüan-ch'üan telegraphed that the remnant bandits in Lungch'eng had been defeated, and the puppet commander was killed on the spot. Ho Ch'eng-chün flew from Hsüan to Shihnan on the 31st to meet Hsü Yüan-ch'üan to discuss measures to suppress the remnant bandits in detail. (31st Dispatch)

Yin Ju-keng Passed Through Tientsin Yesterday to Go to Yü-kuan.

(Tientsin) Yin Ju-keng passed through Tientsin early on the 31st to go to Yü-kuan to take office as the Director of the Special Public Security Bureau of Shanhaikwan concurrently. It is said that Su Yü-ch'i is still reluctant to take on the position of Commissioner of Chi-Mi, and Wang K'e-min specially sent Ku Ju-keng to persuade him. (31st Dispatch)

(Peiping) Yin Ju-keng left P'ing for Tientsin this morning with his secretary Ch'ih Shang-t'ung to visit Sakai, the Chief of Staff of the Japanese Garrison in Tientsin, to discuss matters. Ch'ih will return to P'ing tomorrow to prepare for the handover of the Chi-Mi area. Yin has dispatched another secretary, Wang Lü-ts'ai, to Tangshan tomorrow morning to discuss the handover procedures with Tao Shang-ming, the former Commissioner of the Ao-Yü area. Yin himself may go to Tangshan from Tientsin within a day or two. (31st Dispatch)

The Central Political Conference Decided to Submit the Publishing Law Issue for Review.

(Nanking) The Central Political Conference held its 468th meeting on the morning of the 31st. Over 30 people attended, including Yeh Ch'u-ts'ang, Chu Cheng, K'ung Hsiang-hsi, Ch'en Li-fu, Chou Ch'i-kang, Hung Lu-tung, Chu Chia-hua, and Ho Ying-ch'in. The meeting was chaired by Yeh Ch'u-ts'ang. The following important cases were resolved: (1) Ratification of the National Government's appointment of Wang Yü-chün as a member of the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission. (2) Approval of a subsidy of 70,000 yuan for the 6th National Games. (3) Approval of several budget estimates. (31st Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanking) The press has repeatedly sent representatives to the central government to petition for the Publishing Law and put forward five points of opinion, asking for amendments. On the morning of the 31st, representatives from the Nanking Press Association, including Chin Ch'eng-fu, Chao Min-heng, and Ch'en Ming-te, went to the Central Political Conference to petition again. T'ang Yu-jen met them and promised to submit it to the meeting for discussion. The representatives considered the reply satisfactory and left. According to further inquiries from responsible parties, the Central Political Conference has decided to submit the five points of opinion put forward by the press regarding the Publishing Law for review. (31st Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanking) K'ung Chao-k'ai, Chao Min-heng, and over ten other reporters stationed in Nanking from various newspapers in P'ing, Tientsin, Shanghai, and Hankow, went to the Central Party Headquarters together at 8:00 AM on the 31st to petition the Central Political Conference again for the revision of the Publishing Law. Secretary-General T'ang Yu-jen met them. After the representatives stated that the content of the law placed excessive restrictions on the press, it would be difficult to be effective if only remedial measures were sought in the implementation regulations. They requested a re-determination of principles and submission to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration in order to implement the purpose of supporting public opinion. T'ang said that the Central Political Conference fully understands your intentions and will take into account the opinions of the press in various places. It would be good if remedial measures could be found in the implementing regulations, but if the implementing regulations cannot provide remedies, further discussions will be held on reconsideration. (31st Dispatch)

Chang Hsüeh-liang Returned to Wuchang.

(Hankow) After Chang Hsüeh-liang inspected the army in Shensi on behalf of Chiang, and went to Loyang to attend the graduation ceremony of the senior class of the military academy, he returned to Sian. On the 31st, he completed his official duties and returned to Wuchang from Sian. (31st Dispatch)

(Hankow) Mao Ping-wen arrived in Hankow from Kiangsi on the 31st to visit Chang and report on defense matters. (31st Dispatch)

Current Commentary

Anglo-American Naval Race After the Abolition of the Ratio System

— Latitude

Today, British foreign policy is thoroughly clear to the world. Britain has always feigned a gentlemanly demeanor and strenuously defended its foreign policy, claiming to seek collective security, to maintain European peace, and, with regard to the Far East, to seek Anglo-American cooperation to maintain peace and tranquility in the Pacific. Previously, figures such as General Smuts of South Africa and Marquis Rhodes had all vigorously promoted Anglo-American cooperation and appealed for peace in the Far East. More recently, even Eden, the Minister without Portfolio in the current cabinet, stated that "obtaining the close cooperation of the United States is the special purpose of the British government." We hear such loud pronouncements and are led to believe that the British government under Conservative Party control is truly a strong supporter of peace in the Far East. However, in reality, the talk of collective security, maintaining European peace, and Far Eastern cooperation are all empty promises that will not be honored. The Anglo-Saxons are, after all, a pragmatic people. When their diplomats were working for peace in Europe, the world generally believed that British foreign policy had abandoned its narrow isolationism. But before long, Britain suddenly broke free from the constraints of the London Agreement and the Stresa Conference, and concluded a naval agreement with Germany, effectively abolishing the naval clauses of the Treaty of Versailles. Britain's move directly abandoned its claim to collective security and returned to the "splendid isolation" advocated by Lord Beaverbrook. Indirectly, it also dealt a major blow to naval limitations. This is a clear fact. This policy, in Britain's view, is naturally cause for self-satisfaction, but internationally, it is enough to stir up dangerous waves. Now, before one wave subsides, another rises. British First Lord of the Admiralty Monsell has announced in the British House of Commons the abolition of the naval ratio system. What is the purpose of Britain's move? The abolition of the ratio system is welcomed by Japan but not by the United States. Now, Britain, in deference to Japan's wishes, has publicly announced the abolition of the ratio system, bringing the last vestiges of the Washington Five-Power Naval Limitation Treaty to its final demise. Is Anglo-Japanese cooperation about to revive?

Britain's declaration of abolishing the ratio system is enough to make the naval race among nations more active. This cannot be denied. According to recent news, the United States will build 68 warships in two years. Among those that began construction last year were two aircraft carriers, seven light cruisers, twenty-nine destroyers, and six submarines, totaling forty-four ships. This year, construction will begin on fifteen destroyers and six submarines, totaling twenty-four ships. Active construction of aircraft and the active development of trans-Pacific air routes are also noteworthy. At the same time, Britain's expansion of its navy will certainly not lag behind. Reuter's news reports that Britain plans to spend 150 million pounds to build new warships. The planned additions include fifty to seventy-two cruisers, eighty-four to one hundred destroyers, thirty-nine to fifty-two submarines, and eight to ten aircraft carriers. The naval competition between the two Anglo-Saxon nations, while their union is certainly sufficient to deal with their common enemies, their antagonism is equally sufficient to give ambitious individuals an opportunity to exploit. However, from the perspective of the facts, the situation of antagonism is far greater than that of union. Is this fortunate for Britain and the United States? Or is it unfortunate for the Far East? At present, it is not something we can foresee.

British Economic Expert Sir Arthur Salter to Visit China

(London) It is reported that Sir Arthur Salter will travel to China with an expert from the Bank of England. Salter's trip is without any preconceived notions. He has been studying Chinese affairs for several weeks, but does not wish to predetermine any plans before arriving in China. British individuals involved with China are continuing to study various methods to assist China. Public opinion generally believes that the necessary conditions include reducing military spending and reorganizing debt credit. Many emphasize the importance of seeking Japanese cooperation. Observations of the Japanese official stance on loans to China suggest that they believe it is neither necessary nor timely at present. (Reuter's Dispatch, 31st)

Yalu River Flooding: Extraordinary Disaster in Antung, Unseen in Sixty Years; Over 10,000 Houses Flooded; Refugees Wail for Rescue

Antung: The Yalu River's water level increased even further, reaching 28 feet at 9:00 PM on the 30th, a new record in sixty years. At 10:00 PM, 3,351 houses were flooded in Shin-Gishu. Emergency bells rang loudly across the river to both cities, their sound extremely mournful. (Domei News Agency Dispatch, 31st)

Antung: In Antung City, the water level was 24 feet at 6:00 PM on the 30th. Houses of all sizes collapsed one after another, with 15,000 houses flooded, causing losses of 10 million yuan. The city of Nakashima, between Antung and Shin-Gishu, was 21 feet under water. 1,500 residents have been rescued, but 4,500 remain in the area. The water level is gradually increasing, and houses are continuing to be washed away. Due to the rapid currents, rescue boats cannot operate. Refugees are wailing for help in the darkness, their situation extremely dire. (Japan United Press Dispatch, 31st)

(Shenyang) Thanks to the efforts of the garrison, the "Manchukuo" army, Japanese and Manchukuo police teams, and defense corps in Shenyang City, the embankments of the Hun River continue to be fortified, avoiding a flood. However, in the suburbs, over a thousand houses of Manchus have been flooded. (Domei News Agency Dispatch, 31st)

Bartholomew Appointed Commander of British Forces in China; Repeatedly Decorated During the European War; to Arrive in China at the End of the Year to Assume Office

(London) The War Office announced that it has appointed Lieutenant General Bartholomew as Commander-in-Chief of the British Forces in China, succeeding Lieutenant General Paget. He will assume office at the end of the year. Bartholomew joined the Royal Artillery in 1911 and was mentioned in dispatches six times for his merits during the European War. He is currently 57 years old. (Reuter's Dispatch, 31st)

Japanese Army Distributing Pamphlet; Attempting to Disrupt Control; Army Minister Hayashi Reports to Prince Kan'in; Decides to Strictly Enforce Military Regulations

(Tokyo) Army Minister Hayashi suddenly visited Hakone Mountain on the 30th to meet with Chief of Staff Prince Kan'in, and then went to Hayama to meet with the Emperor, reporting on internal army affairs, attracting considerable attention from various quarters. It is investigated that the content of the Army Minister's report concerns a pamphlet jointly written by Captain Kōtarō Muranaka and First Class Paymaster Asaichi Isobe, who were ordered to be suspended from their positions during the previous change of the Inspector General of Military Education. The pamphlet, entitled "Opinion on the Shaw Army," has been distributed to various quarters, with the army investigating its number to be over 3,000 copies. Army Minister Hayashi met with Inspector General Watanabe on the evening of the 29th to discuss countermeasures. Because the pamphlet exposes the contents of the so-called October Incident and March Incident, attempting to disrupt army control, it was decided to strictly enforce military regulations. Therefore, after determining the method of punishment, the Chief of Staff was reported. (Japan United Press Dispatch, 31st)

(Tokyo) Since the change of the Inspector General of Military Education, pamphlets and opinions on the army, drafted by the military or other names, have been distributed to various quarters. The content contains many inappropriate and distorted aspects of the army. The Army Central Department has investigated the actual situation and studied the aftermath. It has now been discovered that it was issued by a certain officer who was implicated in a certain incident last autumn. It has been decided to order the relevant authorities to confiscate the pamphlets in question and, within a day or two, punish the active duty officers involved. (Domei News Agency Dispatch, 31st)

Page 9

Page 10

League of Nations Council Meeting Filled with Tension; Britain and France Join Forces to Stifle East African Warfare; New Proposals to Italy Based on Treaties; Italy Opposes Placing Abyssinia Under League of Nations Trusteeship

(Geneva) Geneva is filled with tension this morning, as the League of Nations Council meeting, watched by the entire world, is scheduled to convene here today, possibly becoming the most serious meeting since the League's founding. Council President Litvinov arrived here last night from Carlsbad, followed by the Italian delegation led by Sir Aloisi, with only a few hours between them. Sir Anthony Eden and Prime Minister Laval are expected to arrive this morning, allowing sufficient time for preliminary talks before the meeting commences at 5:00 PM today. The League is paying attention to the attitudes of the various national representatives on procedural matters, namely, whether the Council should only mediate or directly intervene. The second method would likely cause the Italian representative to withdraw from the meeting. It is rumored that Britain will insist on discussing the root causes of the conflict. If a compromise cannot be reached, it can obtain the assistance of Austria, Denmark, Portugal, Spain, etc. However, the South American representatives will likely remain strictly neutral. Some quarters predict that Litvinov and the Turkish representative will suggest that both Italy and Abyssinia should reaffirm their commitment to the Kellogg-Briand Pact and Article 5 of the 1928 Italo-Ethiopian Treaty, which stipulates that all disputes should be submitted to mediation. (National Telegram, 31st)

(Geneva) This afternoon, French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval met with British Minister without Portfolio Anthony Eden. The two exchanged impressions gained from their talks with representatives from Italy and Abyssinia this morning. Laval and Eden seem to have reached an agreement on the attitude to be adopted at the League of Nations Council meeting at 5:00 PM today. (Havas Dispatch, 31st)

(Geneva) The representatives of the countries participating in the extraordinary meeting of the League of Nations Council, including the French delegation led by French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval, arrived here at 9:00 AM this morning. British Minister without Portfolio Anthony Eden also arrived at the same time. Prime Minister Laval immediately went to the offices of the French delegation to meet with representatives of the member states of the Council. These contacts were arranged in advance by the staff. The first meeting of the Council is still scheduled for 5:00 PM this afternoon, and it will be strictly private. (Havas Dispatch, 31st)

(Geneva) The representatives of the countries participating in the League of Nations Council meeting have arrived here together today, preparing to make a final effort to avoid an Italo-Ethiopian war. The representatives are also preparing to demand that Italy allow the process of peaceful negotiations to continue without resorting to armed attacks on Abyssinia. Currently, the greatest hope of the representatives is only to delay the final break, and they do not hope to resolve the fundamental issues. This is indeed noteworthy. (National Telegram, 30th)

(Rome) As a result of talks between British Cabinet Minister Eden and French Prime Minister Laval in Paris yesterday, there is now a new move to resolve the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. A method has been proposed to Rome today, advocating the establishment of a small committee of representatives from Britain, France, Italy, and Abyssinia to meet and study the overall situation based on the 1906 treaty. Italy would undertake not to take hostile actions while these talks continue. The above proposal may be welcomed by the member states of the League of Nations, as they can avoid involvement in the Italo-Ethiopian dispute and make the major powers take full responsibility. It is investigated that the 1906 treaty stipulated that Britain, France, and Italy were responsible for (1) respecting and seeking to preserve Abyssinia's territorial integrity; (2) industrial concessions obtained by any party should not harm the rights of other countries; (3) not interfering in Abyssinia's internal affairs; (4) acting jointly to protect each other's interests in territories bordering Abyssinia; (5) agreeing on the construction of railways within Abyssinia and equal treatment of the three countries' people in trade and transportation. (Reuter's Dispatch, 31st)

Eden's Behind-the-Scenes Activities; Hopes for Peace Remain Slim

(Geneva) British Cabinet Minister Eden visited Abyssinian representative Haile Haywarte, the Abyssinian minister to France, at 11:00 AM this morning, accompanied by a French advisor. At noon, Eden visited Italian representative Aloisi, and later had lunch with League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol. Although the Italo-Abyssinian dispute has not been formally discussed in meetings, there have been many talks behind the scenes. It is heard that the talks are progressing well, but it is too early to say that hopes are high. The idea that Italy would accept the League of Nations' assignment of an arbitrator to join the mediation committee is now generally disbelieved. Eden wants to do something to appease public opinion, letting them know that the League of Nations Council does not want to focus solely on unimportant border details and forget the main issues.

Rome Considers League of Nations Trusteeship of Abyssinia a Strange Tale

According to Rome dispatches, the League of Nations Council meeting today may be delayed, as it is heard that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has continued to work towards various peaceful solutions. According to the latest news from Rome, the Italian Prime Minister is now prepared to abandon his opposition to the League of Nations appointing a fifth arbitrator. However, if the mediation procedures ultimately fail, Italy reserves the right to detail its reasons when the Council meets. Italy will continue to refuse to make such statements at this session of the League of Nations Council. As for the idea of making Abyssinia a protectorate of the League of Nations, Rome does not welcome it, considering it a strange tale. The biggest reason for Italy's opposition is that Britain and France have great influence in the League of Nations and will have great power in the administration of the League of Nations' protectorate in the future, which cannot satisfy Italy. Moreover, this move is practically equivalent to the three signatory countries of the 1906 treaty establishing a mixed Anglo-French-Italian protectorate.

Regard the Treaty as Scrap Paper; Unwilling to Let Other Countries Share the Spoils

It is investigated that the Italian Prime Minister has long regarded this treaty as scrap paper. Italy has already progressed far in Abyssinia and is unwilling to let other countries share its benefits. Italy wants to control the raw materials it lacks, which is also one of its main ambitions for Abyssinia. Italy's *Tribuna* published an illustration today, expressing the feelings of hatred among Italians. The drawing depicts a barefoot Abyssinian under the Geneva negotiating table, befriending the leg of a trouser-clad Englishman. (Reuter's Dispatch, 31st)

Wartime Blockade of the Canal; Representatives Discuss

(Paris) According to sources here, the representatives attending the League of Nations Council meeting today actively discussed methods to block the Suez Canal and prohibit Italian or other countries' ships from transporting munitions after the outbreak of the Italo-Ethiopian war. It is likely that the Council will authorize Britain or various countries to organize a committee to prohibit munitions from any country heading to any location from passing through the Suez Canal. (National Telegram, 31st)

Britain and France's Stance Closer Than Before; Results of Talks Between Eden and Laval

(London) According to Reuter's dispatches from Paris, Britain and France's stance on the Italo-Ethiopian dispute is now closer than it was three weeks ago. This is the result of yesterday's one-hour talks between the two important figures, Eden and Laval. The two thoroughly discussed all aspects of the issue. Today, Eden has gone to Geneva to attend the League of Nations Council meeting. (Reuter's Dispatch, 31st)

(Geneva) It is heard that after the talks between Eden and Laval in Paris yesterday, there has been a change in Britain's position. Britain originally requested that the League of Nations Council immediately discuss the entire Italo-Ethiopian dispute to avoid the increasing danger of war. However, after Laval's advice, Britain's stance is no longer as firm as before. Laval believes that as long as there is still a glimmer of hope for a peaceful resolution, the procedure advocated by Britain is not necessary, as the Council's resolution of May 25th already stipulated that the Italo-Ethiopian dispute should not be discussed in its entirety until all conciliation procedures have completely failed. Although the British government has not completely decided to adopt the French view due to general public opinion at home, the fact that Britain and France can cooperate further makes the prospects for the Council meeting more optimistic. It is likely that Eden will make a final decision on Britain's attitude after holding talks with important representatives of the countries attending the Council. However, in any case, the postponement of discussion on the Italo-Ethiopian dispute without a guarantee to prevent war will be firmly opposed by Britain. Furthermore, the greatest difficulty at present lies in Abyssinia, as the Abyssinian government insists that the Council immediately discuss the entire issue and refuses to accept the resumption of the Italo-Ethiopian arbitration committee. However, although Abyssinia insists on this position, it is still generally believed that if Abyssinia's security can be guaranteed, the Abyssinian government may be expected to accept a conciliatory method, and the guarantee of Abyssinia's security is also what Britain hopes for. (Havas Dispatch, 31st)

Abyssinia Entrusted to League of Nations Governance; British and French Talks Consider This; London Official Statements Deny It

(London) Today, *The Times* published a Paris dispatch stating that Minister without Portfolio Eden and French Foreign Minister Laval had considered making Abyssinia a League of Nations mandated territory. Officials here have denied this claim. (Havas Agency Dispatch, 31st)

(London) According to *The Times*' Paris correspondent, Minister without Portfolio Eden and French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval have considered a solution to the Italo-Ethiopian dispute: not to have Abyssinia make sovereignty-damaging concessions directly to Italy, but rather to have the League of Nations, as the protector of Abyssinia's freedom and rights and the guarantor of European interests, accept Abyssinia's concessions. Britain and France intend to declare to the Abyssinian government that Abyssinia is a member of the League of Nations and has the obligations it should oversee. If the country cannot reorganize its internal affairs on its own, the League of Nations should step in to help. This concept is now being materialized, intending to make Abyssinia a mandated territory of the member states of the League of Nations, with a High Commissioner exercising governing power, whose position would be similar to the League of Nations High Commissioner to Danzig. Then, Abyssinia would grant Italy local concessions, but the power of governance would still be held by the League of Nations. At the same time, the League of Nations would act as Abyssinia's protector and provide financial assistance in exchange. (Havas Dispatch, 31st)

Page 11

(London) It is now suggested that the League of Nations should administer Abyssinia on its behalf, in order to resolve the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. This plan has been communicated to the Ethiopian King from undisclosed sources, advocating that the League of Nations grant Italy special economic concessions, with the understanding that it will protect Abyssinia from foreign aggression. According to the Reuter's correspondent in Addis Ababa, the Ethiopian King has only expressed gratitude. However, the King told a person who met with him that he had no objection to the principle of European power, as long as it was purely economic. The Ethiopian people would rather prosper under European guidance than be independent and impoverished.

British colonial expert Mr. Bell wrote to *The Times*, supporting this proposal, saying that the League of Nations should declare a temporary mandate over Abyssinia, allowing Italy's legitimate grievances and rights to be fulfilled. (Reuter's Dispatch, 31st)

(Paris) *Le Matin* received news from London stating that a new proposal has been made to the Abyssinian government, advocating that the League of Nations entrust European countries to jointly govern the country, while granting Italy economic interests but not granting it political or territorial privileges. The Abyssinian Emperor can freely select advisors from among the member states of the League of Nations to assist in governance. It is heard that the Abyssinian Emperor has replied that Abyssinia does not oppose the power of European countries, but that it should be purely economic. For Abyssinia's sake, it is better to prosper under the guidance of European countries than to be impoverished under complete independence. However, *Le Matin*'s correspondent did not indicate from whom this new proposal came. (Havas Dispatch, 31st)

Abyssinia Prepares for War

People with Guns Facing Outward; Strong Anti-Italian Sentiment

Addis Ababa: Abyssinia is currently in a state of war frenzy. One million Abyssinians are now preparing for war, sharpening their swords and cleaning their guns, ready to fight. Even children are learning to wield swords and fire guns, and women are also preparing to replace men in their duties when they go to war. Italian expatriates are leaving the country one after another. Several officials from the Italian legation returned home yesterday, escorted by guards from the legation, because the Abyssinians have extremely strong anti-Italian sentiments. There is currently only one Italian woman in Addis Ababa. The Italian envoy's refusal to attend the Ethiopian King's birthday celebration is seen as a major insult by the Abyssinians. Some quarters are now demanding a severance of relations with Italy. However, the Ethiopian King wants an honorable peace, and this strategy is supported by the masses. Therefore, as far as Abyssinia is concerned, the Ethiopian King is now the master of the situation. According to reliable sources, the entire Abyssinian territory unanimously supports the Ethiopian King's proposition that, in times of national crisis, all men and women, regardless of their religion, should defend Abyssinia against foreign aggression. People here currently know nothing about the views of the League of Nations and the great powers. (Reuter's Dispatch, 31st)

###

Italy Excludes Great Powers from Involvement in Abyssinia

Holds Firm Resolve to Military Occupation; Willing to Implement an Egyptian System of Governance

(London) Someone asked the Italian authorities for their opinion on the plan for a protectorate. The answer was that this is not enough to resolve the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. Mussolini recently stated that it is impossible for any country or great power to implement a protectorate over Abyssinia. The Italian view is that Italy must militarily occupy Abyssinia. (Reuter's Dispatch, 31st)

(London) Mussolini's newspaper *Il Popolo d'Italia* published an article suggesting that Abyssinia should implement a system of governance similar to that of Egypt, saying that this is honorable for Abyssinia, as Egypt is an ancient civilization, while Abyssinia was historically rife with barbarism. (Reuter's Dispatch, 31st)

Italy Busy Transporting Troops and Armaments; Over a Hundred Ships in May; Passing Through the Suez Canal

(Geneva) According to reliable sources, in the recent month of May, Italy transported troops and armaments to East Africa, with 179 ships passing through the Suez Canal. (National Telegram, 30th)

(London) According to Reuter's correspondent in Rome, General Graziani, the commander of the Italian forces in East Africa, issued a proclamation in Eritrea and Italian Somaliland, denouncing those who spread rumors, saying that if anyone expresses dissatisfaction with the colonial system, they will be immediately deported back to their country after being identified. At the same time, General Bōno, the Italian commissioner stationed in Eritrea, has established a special court and issued a declaration, stating that Italy has no issue of requisitioning land from the natives. The arrival of Italians there is solely for the development of the colony for the benefit of the masses. General Bōno has also established a bonus system, with the hope that those who serve diligently will be rewarded. (Reuter's Dispatch, 31st)

Representative Attending the League of Nations Conference Speaks by Telephone with Tokyo; What Was Said Is a Matter of Speculation

(Geneva) Haile Haywarte, the chief representative of Abyssinia attending the League of Nations Council meeting, spoke with Tokyo by long-distance telephone today before the Council meeting. What was said, Haywerte did not reveal. This matter has now aroused various speculations from the outside world, all saying that it is related to the recent discord and suspicion between Japan and Italy. (National Telegram, 31st)

East African War Inevitable; Britain Prepares to Protect Its Citizens; Will Also Send Troops to Protect Water Sources

(London) According to news today, Britain believes that the Italo-Ethiopian war is inevitable sooner or later. Therefore, in order to increase the security of the legation in Addis Ababa and protect the lives of British citizens in Abyssinia, it has been decided to send Indian troops to Addis Ababa. According to unofficial news from Egypt, once the Italo-Ethiopian war breaks out, Britain will send troops to protect the Lake Tana region in Abyssinia. (National Telegram, 31st)

(Paris) According to news from Egypt today, Britain is preparing to send troops into Abyssinia when Italy attacks the country, to protect British interests in the Lake Tana region. Lake Tana is the source of the Blue Nile River and is very important for the irrigation of Sudan. (National Telegram, 31st)

Egypt Grants Italy Permission for Aircraft to Fly Over; But Refuses to Issue Blank Permits

Cairo: Officials announced that 20 Italian military aircraft have flown over Egypt to date, each time with permission from the Egyptian government. (National Telegram, 31st)

(London) Foreign Secretary Sir Samuel Hoare replied to a question from a Member of Parliament, stating that in the past six months, Italy has requested permission from the Egyptian government for 11 Italian military aircraft to fly over Egypt. However, the Egyptian government has refused to issue blank permits without specifying the number of aircraft. (Havas Dispatch, 30th)

British Order Large Number of Reconnaissance Aircraft

(London) The Daily Telegraph reports that the government has recently ordered a batch of coastal reconnaissance aircraft, the largest number since the European war. Together with the existing ones, the British government will have a total of 200 aircraft. (Havas dispatch, 31st)

French Garrison Deploys Defenses

(Geneva) Today, the Associated Press correspondent traveled to Djibouti and passed through French Somaliland. He saw French troops unloading cannons and other equipment. When asked, they said it was to prevent Africans, due to the continuous activities of European countries in Africa, from attacking all white people. (National Telegram, 30th)

European Cooperation Faces Acid Test: French Newspaper Expresses Optimism

(Paris) "Le Temps" published a commentary studying the possibility of the League of Nations Council handling the Italo-Ethiopian dispute, stating that "The primary task of this Council meeting is to safeguard the future of the League of Nations and prevent the Italo-Ethiopian dispute from breaking down in Geneva. Keeping the green hills is more important than worrying about firewood. In this respect, the current trend seems quite optimistic. There seems to be a hope for compromise on the points of contention among the countries involved. Even if Britain believes that to maintain the authority and reputation of the League of Nations, it is necessary to expand the scope of the Council's discussion and conduct a comprehensive review of the Italo-Ethiopian dispute, it would be more appropriate for the League of Nations Council to first restore the work of the Italo-Ethiopian Arbitration Committee and then wait for the opportunity to make a final decision. Britain will soon understand this point. The League of Nations Council's gradual discussion of the entire dispute is not a deliberate delay or missed opportunity. On the contrary, only with ample time can a peaceful solution be sought. To what extent the Italo-Ethiopian dispute poses a danger to general peace will only be seen in the coming weeks. In summary, if all the countries involved have good will and a spirit of compromise, there is no difficult political problem that cannot be solved. This Council meeting may be a major test of cooperation and peace policies." (Havas dispatch, 30th)

International Court of Justice: List of Substitute Judges: Various Parties Compete for Adachi's Vacancy: League of Nations General Assembly to Vote in September

(Geneva) The League of Nations today released the list of substitute judges for the International Court of Justice in The Hague. There are 24 substitutes, all vying to succeed Japanese judge Adachi. Among them are three Japanese: Yamada, Sato, and Nagaoka; one Indian: Sapru; one Irish: Mulrahan; and one American: Scott. The new judge will be elected by the League of Nations General Assembly in September. (Reuters dispatch, 31st)

Germany Denies: Bombers Fly to East Africa

(London) This newspaper reports that a dispatch from the Romanian capital states that a very large German bomber plane flew over the city and then flew to Turkey, presumably to the capital of Abyssinia. (National Telegram, 31st)

(Geneva) A British news agency reports that a German bomber can carry 50 bombs, has a 700-horsepower engine and a machine gun. When it flew over Romanian territory, Romanian fighter planes forced it to land. The German Ministry of Aviation has denied this, saying that Germany has never had such a bomber, and that the story of the plane flying to Abyssinia is a rumor intended to provoke international ill will. Germany has neither sent planes to Abyssinia nor supplied that country with any arms. (National Telegram, 31st)

Japanese Naval Budget Swells: Totaling 700 Million Yuan: Implementing Second Replenishment as Foundation

(Tokyo) Regarding the next fiscal year's budget, the Navy convened a meeting of the ministry on the 9th and 10th of this month. After reviewing the outlines of the budgets submitted by various departments and bureaus, the figures were finalized yesterday, the 30th. The naval budget was submitted to the Ministry of Finance on the 31st. Of the total budget, the base budget is 402 million yuan, and the new requests total 310 million yuan, reaching a total of 712 million yuan. The keynote of the budget is to implement the second replenishment plan as its foundation and to fully consider the adjustment of finance and national defense, only including what is urgently needed. As for the third replenishment plan, which includes replacements and new construction, it will be separated from the next fiscal year's budget and will be handled flexibly according to the situation of the disarmament conference. The main points of the new requests are listed below:

Land and sea improvement costs: 72 million yuan

Naval administration improvement costs: 75 million yuan

Military supplies improvement costs: 45 million yuan

New warship maintenance costs: 13 million yuan

Research costs: 4 million yuan

Large-scale exercise costs: 8 million yuan

Repair costs: 35 million yuan

Manchurian Incident costs: 10 million yuan

Air Force equipment costs: 25 million yuan

Warship construction costs and other: 52 million yuan (United Press dispatch, 31st)

Japanese Four-Ministry Authorities Confer: Second Step in China Policy

(Tokyo) Regarding the resolution of the North China problem, the government is formulating a second-step policy toward China through consultations among the four ministries of Foreign Affairs, Army, Navy, and Finance. It is reported that the foundation is the stability and establishment of East Asia, namely Japan will strive to stabilize East Asia and resist all forces that hinder Sino-Japanese relations. It demands that the Chinese government absolutely prohibit anti-Japanese and anti-Manchukuo movements throughout China, prevent incitement by third countries, actively implement Sino-Japanese mutual assistance, and develop North China's industry. (China United Press dispatch, 31st)

Rumors of President Hayashi of South Manchuria Railway Resigning: Matsuoka Yosuke Highly Favored as Successor

(Tokyo) President Hayashi of the South Manchuria Railway visited Prime Minister Okada at 7:30 this morning, explained the recent situation of the South Manchuria Railway in detail, internal control, and his personal position on the Kwantung Army and "Manchukuo," and then requested to resign. Prime Minister Okada hoped that President Hayashi would take his position seriously. President Hayashi then visited Army Minister Hayashi at 8:30 a.m. and expressed his intention to resign. President Hayashi, having obtained the government's understanding, will return to Manchuria on August 2 to sort out unfinished business and formally submit his resignation at the appropriate time. (Dentsu dispatch, 31st)

(Tokyo) After Army Minister Hayashi met with President Hayashi of the South Manchuria Railway, he summoned the Vice-Director of the Manchurian Affairs Bureau to explain the content of the meeting. Within the government, there are opinions to replace the president of the South Manchuria Railway and reorganize the South Manchuria Railway. President Hayashi will resign after the government decides on the reorganization policy of the South Manchuria Railway. (United Press dispatch, 31st)

(Tokyo) President Hayashi of the South Manchuria Railway visited Prime Minister Okada and Hayashi of the Manchurian Affairs Bureau on the morning of the 31st. Later, according to what he told people, "My visit to the Prime Minister and the Army Minister this morning was entirely for personal matters. As for the rumors that I will resign or that Vice-President Hatta will also resign, I have no intention of leaving. Now that I have taken care of personal matters, I plan to return to my post in Manchuria on August 2 as scheduled." (United Press Agency dispatch, 31st)

(Tokyo) The government is currently looking for a successor to President Hayashi of the South Manchuria Railway, but the most promising candidate is Mr. Matsuoka Yosuke. It is heard that he is currently residing at his villa in Gotemba and will be contacted as soon as he returns to Tokyo. (United Press Agency dispatch, 31st)

Japanese Ambassador to Britain Matsudaira Expresses Intention to Resign: Hirota Decides to Persuade Him to Stay

(Tokyo) Ambassador to Britain Matsudaira is scheduled to return to Japan on August 8. It is heard that the ambassador will submit his resignation on the occasion of this return to make way for younger generations. However, Foreign Minister Hirota has decided to make every effort to persuade him to stay for the following three reasons: (1) No one has a relationship with the British royal family like Ambassador Matsudaira's reputation and family; (2) Ambassador Matsudaira has great credibility among all levels of British society, and replacing him would be a national loss; (3) He is only allowed to return to Japan on the condition that he resumes his post. (Dentsu dispatch, 31st)

(Tokyo) Since Foreign Minister Hirota took office, personnel changes at the ambassadorial level have been largely renewed. However, the middle ranks below the minister and consul-general levels are still quite stagnant. This time, Foreign Minister Hirota has decided to make a major change to create a new personnel structure. As a result, a considerable number of ministers and consuls-general will retire, and the scope of changes in bureau and section chiefs in the ministry will be broad. (Dentsu dispatch, 31st)

German Military Academy Principal Predicts Future War Scenarios: Mobilization Must Strive for Speed: Surprise Attack Without Declaration of War

German Sengcheng: Lieutenant Colonel Siebel, principal of the Sengcheng Military Academy in Germany, recently gave a speech to 2,000 university students, predicting the situation of future wars. He said: "Future wars will be wars of all-out struggle, and mobilization must strive for speed, so that once war is declared, all units are properly deployed, and even begin contact without waiting for a declaration of war. All fighter planes, bombers, motorcycle artillery, and long-range artillery will immediately begin fighting in the border areas, while using powerful radio stations to broadcast to the enemy to disrupt their morale. The main task of the war is to strike the enemy's heartland before the enemy country has fully mobilized the defense equipment prepared after the war, and to conquer it in one fell swoop. At the start of the war, the country should promulgate laws to concentrate all national power, solicit all scientific inventions and new technologies for war purposes, and conscript national scientists to assist the country in its operations day and night." (Havas dispatch, 30th)

New Dutch Cabinet Formed: Prime Minister Colin Concurrently Minister of Defense: Finance Minister Reelected, Economic Policy Unchanged

The Hague: Former Prime Minister Colin was ordered to reorganize the new cabinet and has now succeeded. The list of cabinet members is as follows: Prime Minister and Minister of Colonial Affairs, and Acting Minister of Defense, Dr. Colin (incumbent); Minister of Foreign Affairs, Graf (incumbent); Minister of Justice, Schneekluth (incumbent); Minister of Finance, Wood (incumbent); Minister of Interior, Vilter (incumbent); Minister of Agriculture, Dykeus (formerly Minister of Defense); Minister of Education, Brunner (newly appointed); Minister of Industry and Commerce, Grisen (formerly Minister of Economic Affairs); Minister of Social Affairs, Slingenberg (newly appointed). After the new cabinet attends Parliament for the first time, it is said that it will dissolve the Lower House. (Havas dispatch, 31st)

The Hague: Dr. Colin formed a new cabinet today, and its nature has completely broken the political party divide. The cabinet members from various factions in the two houses are even broader than his first mixed cabinet. However, the most important thing is the reelection of Finance Minister Dr. Wood, which is clear evidence that the new government will continue to maintain the Dutch currency and oppose devaluation. (National Telegram, 31st)

British-American Cooperation: Stabilize International Currencies: Morgan Visits Downing Street: Generally Believed to Be Related to This Matter

(London) The idea that the world's major financial countries will find ways to stabilize currencies is becoming more powerful here today, because American banker and former Treasury Secretary Morgan met with Prime Minister Baldwin. It is generally believed that the two men's talks are related to the hope of joint action by the British and American governments to stabilize currencies as soon as possible. Although Mr. Morgan currently holds no official position and his trip here is purely private, observers say that Mr. Morgan, in his position in the international banking community, occasionally contributes opinions on foreign financial situations to the U.S. Treasury Department. The idea of currency stabilization has been widely rumored here for weeks, and Mr. Morgan's visit to Downing Street today is the first indication that the British and American governments may take this step. After the two men finished talking, they both declined to announce the content of the discussion. (National Telegram, 30th)

Austria Completes Highway: Connecting Italian-Southern Transportation: Opening Ceremony Scheduled for Saturday

(Vienna) Austria's newly built highway passes through the Alps, connecting Salzburg and Carinthia provinces, so that the highways of Italy, Austria, and Yugoslavia can be directly connected. This highway has been completed and the opening ceremony will be held on the 3rd of next month, presided over by President Miklas and Prime Minister Schuschnigg. On that day, car and motorcycle races will also be held on the highway. Germany had originally sent representatives to participate, but recently withdrew, using poor highway construction as an excuse. It is rumored that Germany's non-participation is due to the Austrian authorities prohibiting German cars and motorcycles from displaying the Nazi swastika flag. (Havas dispatch, 31st)

International Commercial Telegram

——July 31, Reuters Special Business Telegram——

Gold and Silver: British Gold: The London gold price today is 140 shillings and 8 pence, up 31 pence.

British Silver: The London silver market is stable today. Spot prices are unchanged, remaining at 30 pence 1875. Futures rose 0.0625 to 30 pence 3125. The United States bought, and China both bought and sold. Transactions were average.

American Silver: The Mount Lyell silver market was quiet. At the opening, the September futures price was 67.85 to 68.10, the same as yesterday's closing price.

Exchange Rates: British-American: The London foreign exchange market was weaker this morning because the Dutch political situation has improved. The British-American exchange rate opened at $4.959375, down 0.0625 from yesterday's American-British closing price. It continued to fall by 25 in the first hour, unchanged at noon, and then rose by 0.0625 to $4.9575. This price remained unchanged until 2:00 p.m.

British-French: The opening price was unchanged, remaining at 74 francs 96. After the first hour, it fell by 14 pounds. At noon, it continued to fall by 3 pounds. In the afternoon, at 2:00 p.m., it rose by 3 pounds to 74 francs 82, down 14 pounds from the opening.

Cotton and Wheat: American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened higher due to reports of excessive rainfall in the eastern cotton belt. Later, due to the lack of new developments in the market, merchants waited and watched, and prices tended to loosen.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market rose sharply today. At 1:00 p.m., the October futures rose 1 pence 625 to 5 shillings 3 pence 25.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was quiet this morning. At 1:00 p.m., the October futures price was 6.19, the same as yesterday's closing price.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat and grain market opened firmer. Wheat was firm due to pro-long messages from Canada. At the same time, grain prices also rose. Opening prices were able to remain unchanged before noon.

Rubber: London: The rubber market opened stable and then turned sluggish. At noon, the trading price for October-December futures was 5 pence 875, the same as yesterday's closing price.

New York: The rubber opened higher due to improvements in the Dutch political situation. Later prices fell due to merchants holding and watching.

Securities: New York: The stock market was quiet today, and price changes were small. U.S. Steel stocks fell sharply due to poor business and disappointing dividend reductions. The Dow Jones 30 Industrial Average opened up 2 points to 125.59.

American Economic Observer, Dr. Buck, Has Lived in China for Over 20 Years

(Nanjing) Foreign news agencies reported that the U.S. government appointed Dr. Buck, the current head of the Agricultural Economics Department of Jinling University in Nanjing, as an observer of China's economic situation. The reporter visited Dr. Buck on the morning of the 31st, and learned that he had left Nanjing a few days ago to travel in South China and inspect the economic situation in Guangdong, Guangxi, and Yunnan. He is expected to return to Nanjing in the middle of next month. Dr. Buck has lived in China for over 20 years and has headed the Department of Agricultural Science at Jinling University for nearly ten years. He has conducted extensive research on China's rural economy and is familiar with other financial issues. He is the author of books such as "Chinese Farm Economics." Last year, when the silver problem occurred, he was hired as a member of the Silver Price Research Committee of our Ministry of Industry and Commerce. At the same time, the U.S. Treasury Department also hired him as a financial advisor and summoned him back to the United States to consult on everything. He was then sent back to China to investigate the currency system and general financial issues. After arriving in China this spring, Dr. Buck went to various places to investigate and is still carrying out the work. He originally planned to return to the United States recently to report his findings and opinions to the Treasury Department, but it is not yet known whether he will still need to return to the United States after receiving the new appointment, or whether he will continue his inspections in China. (Central News Agency dispatch, 31st)
