The Issue of Anti-Chinese Sentiment in the Dutch East Indies: The Progress of Negotiations by the Envoy. The Focus of Negotiations is on the Legal Status of Overseas Chinese and Restrictions on Entry. The Dutch Side Has Already Provided a Formal Response on the Issue of Legal Treatment.

Text of a Note to the Dutch Government: Our envoy to the Netherlands, Mr. Jin Wensi, sent a note to the Dutch Minister of Foreign Affairs, Graeff, regarding issues such as restrictions on Chinese immigrants in the Dutch East Indies, stating: (1) Regarding the matter of this note, concerning the recently submitted measures to the Dutch East Indies Parliament for restricting immigration, I, as the envoy of my country, hereby provide a more detailed explanation of the views of my government to Your Excellency the Minister. The Consul General of my country in Batavia has, under the instructions of my government, repeatedly met with the Secretary-General of the Dutch Governor-General. Furthermore, the Chargé d'Affaires of my country in the Netherlands also sent two letters to Your Excellency the Minister on June 29 and August 22 of this year, requesting that the government of your country consider the views of my government, hoping that the restrictive measures submitted to the National Assembly at that time would not be passed, or that, even if passed, other measures more favorable to the Chinese than the average quota could be used as the standard for restriction. To this end, I, as the envoy, have also held repeated negotiations with Your Excellency the Minister and the Director in charge of Your Excellency's Ministry. Moreover, during my meeting with Your Excellency the Minister on September 6 of this year, Your Excellency the Minister stated that a response would be provided immediately to the aforementioned two letters. A note was sent on November 18 of this year requesting Your Excellency the Minister to expedite the response. (2) I, as the envoy, have repeatedly received reports from various consulates of my country in the Dutch East Indies, learning that these restrictive immigration measures, after being passed by the National Assembly on September 6 of this year, have been submitted to the government of your country for approval, in the form of amendments and supplementary clauses to the Edict of October 15, 1915, as amended by the Edict of April 21, 1931. (3) I, as the envoy, hereby explain the views of my government on the following points: In recent years, the government of my country has not ignored the special difficulties encountered in the Dutch East Indies. On the other hand, it seems that one of the reasons for the new clauses passed by the National Assembly is to safeguard the existing economic interests of the Chinese residing in the Dutch East Indies, and that the implementation of these clauses will not unduly hinder the interests of the Chinese. This is another argument. (4) However, it must be pointed out that there is a long-standing and close relationship between the Dutch East Indies and the Chinese community. Any measures to restrict the subsequent migration of Chinese will inevitably have an unfortunate impact on the interests of the Chinese and the Dutch East Indies. For hundreds of years, the Chinese have worked hard to create enormous and important interests of an economic nature, which have become an inseparable part of the economic life of the Dutch East Indies since ancient times. This is an undeniable fact. It must also be pointed out that in several uncivilized areas of the East Indies, the Chinese have developed these areas through arduous efforts. If Chinese immigrants to the Indies are subject to restrictions, the freedom to choose hardworking young people from our country to assist in maintaining or improving existing businesses, or in establishing new businesses, will be stripped or diminished by these restrictions. Moreover, there are still many undeveloped areas in the Malay Archipelago. If Chinese immigration is restricted, it will inevitably hinder the development of these areas, which will be detrimental to the interests of China, the Netherlands, and the Dutch East Indies. (5) Moreover, the Chinese have never harbored any political intentions in migrating to the Dutch East Indies since ancient times. This restrictive immigration measure seems even more unnecessary for the Chinese. The Chinese who reside there support themselves and contribute to public happiness and prosperity, obeying local laws to live peacefully. Our interests are of the most important and purely economic or commercial nature. Moreover, it is sometimes said that our residence in the Dutch East Indies is in economic competition with the indigenous people, but this is not the case in reality. The Chinese do not own land in the Dutch East Indies. The agriculture of West Borneo has been improved through our efforts, which has greatly benefited indigenous landowners. (Omitted content) (6) In addition to the aforementioned practical points, this issue of immigration restrictions has also attracted the deep attention of the Chinese in the Dutch East Indies. Therefore, during the meetings of the National Assembly, respected members representing the interests of the Chinese strongly requested that the proposed measures be reconsidered. Even after the assembly passed the measures, thirty Chinese chambers of commerce in various ports of the Dutch East Indies, despite knowing that the case had passed, jointly submitted a petition to the Governor-General on October 28 of this year, requesting further consideration. This is sufficient to demonstrate the deep concern of the Chinese about this matter, which is shared by my government and the Chinese in my country and elsewhere. This is also what I, as the envoy, wish to add. (7) Regarding the section on the equal distribution of annual quotas for each ethnic group, while the purpose is to ensure equal and fair treatment for each ethnic group, it is feared that in practice, the situation of the Chinese will be much more unfavorable than that of other ethnic groups. This should not be ignored. From 1923 to 1932, the average number of Chinese immigrants to the Dutch East Indies accounted for 76% of the total number of immigrants from all ethnic groups. Now, 24% of foreign ethnic groups are being allocated the same annual immigration quota as the 76% of Chinese. The unfairness of this seems clear. Upon investigation, Section 1 of Article 18 of the new regulations stipulates that if the actual number of immigrants in any year is lower than the total number stipulated, each ethnic group may increase its immigration to one-tenth of the total number of immigrants from that ethnic group in the ten years prior to the implementation of the new regulations. Leaving aside the rarity of such circumstances, even the content of this provision is difficult to adapt to the needs of the Chinese. Moreover, there are difficulties in how to apply this provision. In my view, the shortfall in any year cannot be known until after that year has passed. Once it is known, there is no way to make up for it in other countries. Therefore, there must be a provision that allows the shortfall of one ethnic group in the previous year to be made up for by another ethnic group in the following year. (8) In view of the various reasons mentioned above, the government of my country cannot but hope that your government and the government of the Dutch East Indies will take a special attitude towards the issue of immigration. I, as the envoy, hereby invoke the various statements made by the representatives of the Dutch East Indies government at the meeting of the National Assembly on September 6 of this year. The main point of these statements was that people with assets or industrial knowledge and experience are welcome to enter the country, and that, for the sake of developing certain industries, a fixed number of workers may be allowed to enter the country, exceeding the prescribed annual quota. Furthermore, the new regulations are a pioneering undertaking, and the Dutch East Indies government is prepared to carefully examine the political and economic aspects of the implementation of these regulations. If, in practice, experience shows that it is necessary to adopt other methods, it will not hesitate to do so. (9) Therefore, I, as the envoy, hereby submit this note to Your Excellency the Minister to supplement the two previous letters from my embassy on June 29 and August 22. I, as the envoy, am convinced that regardless of the reasons for these new regulations, once these reasons no longer exist, the government of your country will change its attitude towards this matter. Therefore, I, as the envoy, request to reserve the right to raise this issue again at an appropriate time in the future. At the same time, I request Your Excellency the Minister to inform the government of your country in the East Indies of the contents of this note, hoping that the Governor-General of the East Indies will consider the views of the Chinese government when stipulating the annual quota for immigration, and will adopt measures deemed necessary to make the various provisions of Section 1 of Article 18 mentioned above practicable, or to facilitate their implementation, and to enable the various statements made by the representatives of the Dutch East Indies government in the National Assembly to be implemented. Respectfully requesting your consideration. Jin Wensi, Envoy of the Republic of China to the Netherlands, December 14, Year 23."

Reply Note from the Dutch Ministry of Foreign Affairs: The Dutch Ministry of Foreign Affairs replied, "Regarding the inquiry in Letter No. 769 from the Chinese Embassy on March 31 of last year, concerning the legal treatment of Overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies and elsewhere, the Ministry hereby respectfully responds to the aforementioned letter as follows: The legal status of Overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies can be said to be equal to that of Europeans. A portion of the laws there allows Overseas Chinese residing in the Dutch East Indies to be subject to the laws previously applied to Europeans, while another portion is completely newly established and applies to all ethnic groups without any discrimination. Therefore, the legal status of Overseas Chinese is similar to that of Europeans. For example, civil law, commercial law, civil procedure law, and the most important part, criminal law, do not differentiate between Europeans and Chinese. In addition, there are laws specifically for Chinese, and special circumstances among Overseas Chinese (such as adoption). Even Europeans in the East Indies once had such laws. From this, it can be seen that the government of the Dutch East Indies is now striving to ensure equal treatment for all people. On the one hand, the Dutch East Indies government will continue in this direction, striving to eliminate disparities that are unsuitable for the new era, while on the other hand, it will retain any remaining disparities between ethnic groups that are necessary. Based on the aforementioned principles, the Dutch East Indies government has been studying the improvement of criminal procedure for a long time, because there are still disparities between ethnic groups in this matter. This shows that the principles of peace repeatedly declared by the government are still being pursued. However, the complex nature of this endeavor and the technical (legal expertise) difficulties do not allow us to complete it all at once, but only in several stages. The order of priority and the timing must be determined by the local government according to the situation. One point that must be paid particular attention to as to why it must be done in stages is to avoid financial sacrifices. Progress on criminal procedure law has been shown in two ways: Firstly, not long ago, the criminal procedures for Europeans were simplified (as published in the Dutch East Indies Legal Gazette Nos. 460, 580, and 581 in 1932). Secondly, the criminal procedures of the local courts are non-discriminatory for all ethnic groups. The government hopes that it will be able to continue its efforts to improve criminal procedure in the future. The government is very pleased to be confident that improvements will be achieved in accordance with the above principles, which the government regards as its sole goal, to satisfy the desires of all the people of the Dutch East Indies. Graeff, Dutch Minister of Foreign Affairs, May 2, 1934." (End)

Flood Statistics in Anhui Province: Over 410,000 Mu of Farmland Flooded, Losses Estimated at Around 6 Million Yuan

Anqing Correspondence: Before the beginning of last month, Anhui Province had experienced a prolonged drought in various counties, with drought conditions reported in each county. However, in less than ten days, continuous rainfall caused the river water to rise sharply, flowing down torrentially, coupled with flash floods. The dikes along the river in various counties were in imminent danger. It is estimated that 78 dikes have collapsed due to the inability of manpower to resist. According to statistics from the Provincial Disaster Relief Committee, over 410,000 mu of farmland have been flooded, with the value of crop losses estimated at 15 yuan per mu, totaling around 6 million yuan. The number of houses, livestock, and sundries swept away is not included. Breaking it down by county, Huaining County had 11 dikes collapse, flooding over 86,000 mu, affecting over 55,000 people. Tongcheng County had 7 dikes collapse, flooding over 19,000 mu, affecting over 13,000 people. Wangjiang County had 21 dikes collapse, flooding over 111,000 mu, affecting over 88,000 people. Susong County had 6 dikes collapse, flooding over 14,000 mu, affecting over 9,000 people. Dongliu County had 5 dikes collapse, flooding over 15,000 mu, affecting over 7,000 people. Tongling County had 2 dikes collapse, flooding over 41,000 mu, affecting over 34,000 people. Fanchang County had 6 dikes collapse, flooding over 32,000 mu, affecting over 29,000 people. Nanling County had 6 dikes collapse, flooding over 8,900 mu, affecting over 9,000 people. Wuhu County had 9 dikes collapse, flooding over 33,000 mu, affecting over 13,000 people. Guichi County had 2 dikes collapse, and flash floods caused flooding of over 23,000 mu, affecting over 16,000 people. Dangtu County had 2 dikes collapse, flooding over 23,600 mu, affecting over 13,000 people. In Zhide County, farmland along the lake and river was flooded by tidal backflow, with the number of mu lost unknown. In Qianshan County, flash floods in Xingjiu Township along the two banks caused flooding of over 5,000 mu, affecting over 3,000 people. In total, 13 counties are affected, with over 300,000 victims. The survivors are extremely poor and have no one to turn to, and are only groaning and haggard under the scorching sun and hot wind, their suffering is unspeakable. To organize urgent relief, a minimum of three yuan per person is needed, requiring no less than eight or nine hundred thousand yuan. In addition, repairing dikes and organizing work relief will require over one million yuan. The Provincial Disaster Relief Committee has already consulted with the provincial government to finalize a work relief plan, and has also submitted a report to the Central Relief Committee, requesting that the disaster in Anhui Province be listed together with the provinces upstream, such as Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi, and that 800,000 yuan be allocated for urgent work relief to help the victims. The provincial government has also received an order from Chairman Chiang, instructing the three departments of civil affairs, finance, and construction to consult and form a General Anhui Flood Relief Association, modeled after the successful case of Jiangsu Province, first establishing a general affairs and flood control group, to be undertaken separately by the departments of civil affairs and construction, to save costs. The three departments of civil affairs, finance, and construction have jointly drafted the organizational regulations of the association and submitted them to the provincial government for approval and implementation. (July 29)

Jining: The Zhao Wang River Breached Again - The Water is Vast and Spreading North -

Jinan Correspondence: The Nanyang, Hunanwang, and Wanghu Lakes in Jining were unable to contain the continuous inflow from the He Yong Irrigation Canal. The Wang Guitun Dike in Xinian first breached, and the water has flowed to the Xin Tiao River. The lower reaches of the Grand Canal also cannot discharge the water due to the rising water level and rapid flow. At the breached area of the eastern dike near Xindian, the water has reached the base of the Jining-Yanzhou Railway branch line. Yesterday, the Zhao Wang River in Jining County suddenly breached again, and the entire Jining County was flooded. The water level of the Zhao Wang River had already reached the canal bank, and on the 28th, it suddenly rose another four inches. The surrounding area was all water, and there was no place to get soil for emergency protection. The dikes continued to collapse. On the 29th, the water level rose another two inches, and the water became even greater. The northern dike east of Tangjiakou and west of Liangqiao was breached in two places, each over ten feet wide. The overflowing water mixed with the sloping water from the Wang Guitun breach and passed through the Jining-Jiaxiang automobile road. The water level is now increasing continuously and there is a danger of it overflowing the road and continuing to spread north. Jining County Magistrate Zhen Guangyuan has telegraphed a report. The water levels in other counties are still high, and the houses have been completely collapsing after prolonged soaking. Inspector Wang Shaochang has telegraphed a report that over ten thousand victims have been continuously arriving in Jining waiting for trains to transport them to various counties for shelter. The provincial government allocated four more trains on the 29th for transportation. The fifth and sixth batches of victims who arrived in Jinan on the 28th were transported to Dezhou (1,200 people) and Pingyuan and Yucheng (750 people each) on the 29th. After the counties are filled with refugees, they will be transported to counties along the Jiaoji Railway for shelter and relief. (July 29)

Songjiang: Verdict on a Large Gambling Den in Songhui Village

The large gambling den at No. 8 Songhui Village in this city, after being raided by the Public Security Bureau, resulted in the arrest of thirteen gamblers, but the ringleader escaped and has not been apprehended. The county government has sealed off the ringleader's house, pending apprehension for further investigation. All thirteen gamblers and gambling money of 320 yuan were sent to the local court. After investigation by the prosecutor's office, a clear indictment was filed in the corresponding criminal court. Yesterday, the court convened, but the defendants did not appear in court and jointly appointed lawyer Zhu Shanqing to defend them. It was verified that the verdict would be announced on the 31st. The text of the announced verdict is now disclosed: Wang Yongsheng, also known as Li Hongsheng; Li Ersheng, also known as Lu ; Wang Benyuan, also known as Fang Benyuan; Wang Pinzhu, also known as Fang Pinzhu Da Dayuan; Wang Boyuan; Xu Erquan, also known as Ye Wenqing; Wang Sizhi, also known as Wang Shenlin; Wu Guisheng; Ye Baozhen, also known as Geng Haoqin, were all found guilty of gambling for money in a public place and were each fined 300 yuan. If they are unable to pay the fine, they will be sentenced to one day of labor for every three yuan. Gambling paraphernalia such as mahjong tiles, playing cards, chips, and dice were confiscated. Since the crackdown on this large gambling den, smaller gambling dens have successively disappeared.

Suzhou: Rioters in Shengze Smash the Business Tax Bureau

Due to dissatisfaction with the Business Tax Bureau's dispatch of personnel to investigate accounts, the rice industry in Shengze Town, Wujiang County, went on strike on the 29th. It is learned that on the morning of the 30th, dozens of villagers, unable to purchase grain, went to the town to petition. The town's Chamber of Commerce and district office and other agencies immediately summoned four representatives of the rice industry, including Yan Fu, to hold a meeting for investigation and mediation. The rice industry, considering the matter involved the people's food, accepted the mediation and agreed to resume business at 2 pm that afternoon. The villagers were also satisfied and dispersed. However, at noon that day, dozens of rioters suddenly rushed into the town's Business Tax Bureau, arbitrarily causing trouble and smashing objects. The responsible Public Security Sub-bureau immediately dispatched police to suppress them, but because the number of rioters was large, the police dispatched to suppress them were mostly beaten by the rioters. The rioters even rushed to the Public Security Bureau and smashed the doors and windows before leaving. Whether there is a background to this matter is still unknown. Afterwards, the director of the Business Tax Bureau, Gao Yuncheng, and the provincial commissioner, He Fuzong, both went to the province to request instructions. Wujiang County Magistrate Xu sent Section Chief Tang, together with Public Security Director Zheng and Security Team Captain Yang, leading a detachment of the Security Team, to Shengze at dawn yesterday (31st) to suppress the situation and investigate the truth of the rioters' riot. County Magistrate Xu also telegraphed the Department of Civil Affairs to request instructions.

Fugitive from the Xiansishan Restaurant Case Apprehended

In the case of Wang Ruilin and his family of three from Xiansishan being murdered by bandits last year and their bodies dumped in Cheng Lake, the perpetrators Gu Yunquan and Xu Shugao were subsequently captured and sentenced to death by the court. The remaining wanted fugitives, Cai Yiting, Zhuang Jinrong, and Wang Caide, were also captured by the Water Police Detective Team and sent to the district headquarters yesterday (31st). They will be sent to the court today (1st) for interrogation.

Wuxi: Journalists' Association Calls for Revision of New Publication Law

The Wuxi Journalists' Association, advocating for the Central Government to reconsider and revise the Publication Law, held its third special committee meeting yesterday (30th) at 4:00 PM. Committee members Sun Dexian, Yuan Hegao, Zhang Xiyin, Chen Hongjun, Hua E, Sun Chunpu, Shi Qinglin, Sun Xiangfeng, Yang Chusun, and eight others attended. Six lawyers, Zou Binghu, Zhou Beiwu, Tang Ying, Zhang Tong, Wang Tinghuai, and Zhou Jiapu, were invited to attend and provide preliminary advice. Chairman Sun Dexian reported that the Legislative Yuan had passed amendments to the Publication Law, restricting the industry and hindering its development. Two special committee meetings were held on July 10th and 16th, resolving to submit separate petitions to various central government departments, seeking relief, and issuing a declaration regarding the defamation charges against three newspapers in the Caoqiao murder case. A month had passed, and the draft petitions and declarations had been prepared, but they were repeatedly delayed due to seeking opinions from legal experts and revisions. Colleagues in Shanghai and other regions had already voiced their concerns. This association initiated the process early but has fallen behind. Today's meeting aims to discuss and research this matter together.

After discussion, the following resolutions were made: (1) Revise the petition: (a) (Omitted); (b) Regarding the points of non-punishment for defamation due to negligence and the triple penalty for one offense in the Publication Law and Criminal Law, request clarification and request that the implementing regulations of the Publication Law explicitly stipulate that journalists' negligent acts, in addition to being sanctioned by the Publication Law, should not be punished under the Criminal Law; (c) Still request the Central Political Council and the Legislative Yuan to reconsider and revise the Publication Law; (d) Publicly recommend Yang Chusun to draft a telegram, and distribute it to colleagues nationwide, urging them to advocate for a unified position (original text recorded below); (2) The petition will be released immediately, and representatives will be sent to Jingjiang, Jiangyin, Yixing, Liyang, Wuxian, Wujin, Zhenjiang, Jiangdu, Changshu, and other counties to seek signatures; (3) (Omitted); (4) The association will send letters to colleagues in various counties of Jiangsu Province, recommending representatives to jointly petition in Beijing, gathering in Wuxi on August 9th and departing early on the 10th; (5) (6) (Omitted). At approximately 6:00 PM, tea and snacks were served, and the meeting adjourned. The telegram is recorded as follows: To the Nanjing Central Political Conference, the Propaganda Committee of the Central Party Headquarters, the Legislative Yuan, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Interior: It is believed that the late Premier established the political program with freedom of speech and freedom of the press to proclaim to the world. This time, the Central Government has revised the Publication Law, presumably adhering to this principle with reverence and diligence. However, since newspapers published the full text of the revised Publication Law, the journalistic community across the country has been alarmed, rushing to tell each other, claiming that the Northern Warlords in the past controlled public opinion with stringent measures, and comparing them, there seems to be a distinction. Recently, the news industry in Beijing and Shanghai has telegraphed for reconsideration and submitted petitions. Although the authorities have agreed to provide relief in the implementing regulations, it is found that the implementing regulations can only be a transitional form of the old law and a supplement to the present law. Under the principle of not conflicting with this law, it can be relied upon for remedy. If the revised Publication Law has many points that are difficult to implement, most of them are related to principles. It seems that it is not enough to request a redefinition of principles and reconsideration of the revision. It is feared that it will still be difficult to eliminate implementation obstacles. Moreover, the news industry in the inland areas is particularly fearful of the amendment made by the competent official to the county government. The recent incidents of Jingjiang and Tongshan sealing newspapers and arresting people are not far away. From now on, when writing records, there will always be a shadow of imprisonment swaying before us, and we will have to avoid changing a single word to avoid guilt. Moreover, advertisements and announcements have responsible parties, and the revised laws are subject to the same restrictions. Then, in the future, the business operations of newspapers will also be in fear of being punished. The association believes that the interests are closely related and cannot remain silent. It is working with colleagues in neighboring counties to draft a detailed presentation. In addition to submitting it separately, we first send a telegram to present it respectfully, hoping for your examination and understanding. Wuxi County Journalists' Association.

Zhenjiang: Education Circles of Wujin Come to the Provincial Capital to Petition

The decision made by the 764th Committee Meeting of the Jiangsu Provincial Government last week to reassign Qian Hao, Director of the Wujin County Education Bureau, and appoint Sun Youguang to fill the vacancy has been reported in various newspapers. The education circles of Wujin were extremely indignant upon hearing this news. They petitioned on the previous day (29th). Secretary Yan received them and representatives, including Zhuang Quan, presented a petition and stated the reasons for the petition, earnestly requesting the reassignment of capable individuals to maintain education in Wujin. Secretary Yan found the reasons presented to be quite legitimate and promised to forward the petition to Chairman Chen. The representatives considered the reply satisfactory and left. Subsequently, they petitioned the Education Department. Director Zhou was in Shanghai for official business and had not yet returned to the province. Secretary Chen received the representatives, who stated their intentions. Secretary Chen replied that he would convey the representatives' opinions after Director Zhou returned to the department. The petition representatives, including Zhuang Quan, expressed satisfaction and left. According to the representatives of the Wujin education circles, the purpose of this petition was entirely because the new director, Sun Youguang, could not set an example for the education circles with his daily conduct. The entire county's education circles were unwilling to remain silent and expressed that they would not stop until their goal was achieved. The petition is as follows: Regarding the matter of petitioning, it has recently been reported that at the 764th meeting of your government, Qian Hao, Director of the Wujin County Education Bureau, was reassigned, and Sun Youguang was appointed to fill the vacancy. Upon hearing this, colleagues in the education circles were extremely shocked. Since Director Qian took office last June, he has reformed the bureau's affairs and reorganized education, sparing no effort in planning. Moreover, the early drought caused disaster, the rural areas collapsed, and the scenery was in ruins. The source of education funding was exhausted, and the primary schools had no rice to cook, already in a state of virtual stagnation. However, Director Qian, amidst hardship and distress, did not shy away from labor and complaints, making every effort to raise funds and distribute them monthly. His benefits to education are truly not insignificant. Recently, he handled private school advancement and displayed great ambitions. Unexpectedly, out of the blue, it was decided to reassign Director Qian and appoint Sun Youguang to fill the vacancy. Regarding the retention of Director Qian, the province and department naturally have the power, but Sun Youguang's selected conduct is vile, running to powerful figures, speculating in the revolution, and engaging in partisan strife, causing local disputes for years. In the seventeenth year of the Republic, the former provincial party department Minister Ni Bilai came to Changzhou to investigate the case. Sun knelt down in public to beg for forgiveness for failing to coerce. His personal corruption is extreme. Since then, he has been disdained by local people. Moreover, when Sun Youguang served as the county school supervisor in this county last year, he only inspected more than twenty schools in the first year of his term. In the half year of his successor, he did not inspect a single school. The Education Department has recorded two demerits. Knowing that he was uneasy in his position, he submitted his resignation. The records are all there and can be verified. Sun Youguang currently serves as an executive committee member of the county party department, concurrently as the director of the Dayou Seed Breeding Farm, and the manager of the Wuyi Road Automobile Company. With multiple positions and selfish motives, if he is appointed as the Director of the Education Bureau, he will inevitably repeat the same mistakes. Colleagues, learning from the past, for the sake of maintaining education in Wujin and considering the department's assessment, dare not avoid punishment and brave the summer heat to petition in the province, earnestly requesting your government to review the situation, swiftly propose a review, and reappoint capable individuals to maintain education and quell disputes, which is for the public good. Respectfully presented to Chairman Chen of the Provincial Government and Director Zhou of the Education Department.

Four Members of Opera Troupe Drown in Boat Accident

The Zhu Shengkang Opera Troupe, consisting of over fifty people, finished performing at the East Wharf and hired two boats to go to Pushu Bay for a performance. At 2:00 PM on the 30th, while sailing near Jiaoshan, one of the boats capsized due to wind and waves, causing fourteen male and female actors, as well as scenery and prop boxes, to fall into the water. The No. 8 red boat of the Jiaoshan Life Saving Bureau noticed this and immediately summoned the No. 3 and No. 10 lifeboats to rescue them. Ten people were rescued, but two of them could not be revived due to being in the water for too long. The bodies of the remaining two have not been recovered, and the losses are heavy.

Changshu: Soil Vendor Sun Meilin Arrested in Suzhou

Sun Meilin, a Shandong native residing in Jiaochang Bay of this county, has been making a living by selling soil. Yesterday morning, he purchased 51 taels of red soil, 17.5 taels of Yunchuan soil, and 16 taels of Teyun soil from the Hongchang Soil Shop in Tianbao Lane, Shanghai. While passing through Suzhou, intending to take a boat to Changshu to sell it, he was suddenly searched and arrested by the Suzhou Detective Team. Both the person and the goods were seized. After being sent to the Suzhou Public Security Bureau, Sun admitted to the crime without denial. He has now been transferred to the county's Anti-Smoking Association for investigation.

Nantong: Utilizing the Baojia System to Investigate Opium

The Nantong County Anti-Smoking Committee has been dispatching police teams and mobilizing all the Baojia heads in the county to investigate opium. After the offenders are forcibly detoxified, they are sent to the Xiaohai Town Opium Addicts Factory to learn skills after being tried by the county government.

The growth of cotton and rice in the counties of the Nantong area has been excellent this year. Although the coastal reclamation area suffered from insect pests earlier, they have been eradicated by two heavy rains. If there are no natural disasters in the next month, a good harvest can be expected.

Hangzhou: Distribution of 200,000 Loan

The financial difficulties in Zhejiang Province have reached an extreme point. The administrative expenses of various agencies are in arrears of about 1.6 million yuan, and the tax revenue is sluggish. The provincial treasury is insufficient to cope with the situation. A loan of 200,000 yuan has been borrowed from the Zhejiang Local Bank, with tax revenue as collateral. After deducting 45,000 yuan allocated for the previously announced notification, there is a surplus of 155,000 yuan. 40,000 yuan will be allocated for the food expenses of the military and police, and 115,000 yuan will be used to pay the administrative expenses of various agencies. The payment was completed yesterday and distributed without remainder.

The Hangzhou Municipal Government Public Security Bureau and other agencies believe that street light control is a necessary measure for urban safety. They have jointly implemented the street light control measures with various labor unions and will send personnel to inspect when necessary.

Nanyu Road Yushang Section Opens for Ticket Sales

The track laying project on the Nanyu section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, from Yushan to Shangrao, has been completed. It is scheduled to open for ticket sales starting today (1st). Three stations, Shaxi, Lingxi, and Shangrao, have been set up above Yushan. Passenger and freight transportation has already begun. Express trains No. 1 and 2 departing from Jiangbian Station in Hangzhou can reach Shangrao directly.

Xiaoshan: Three Families Robbed by Bandits in Pengshan One Night

Ni Xiaoyuan, a resident of Pengshan, near Linpu in the southern countryside of Xiaoshan, is a farmer. His family is reasonably well-off. His elder brother, Shi Lü, is a businessman in Shanghai. His family is also relatively prosperous. Recently, his eldest daughter returned home to spend the summer, bringing many suitcases with her, which attracted the attention of bandits. The previous night (28th), more than a dozen bandits armed with shotguns and flashlights, their faces painted black, broke into the house by digging through the wall. They then went upstairs and into the rooms, ransacking boxes and chests, and carrying out a major robbery. At that time, the family members were all tied up and did not dare to speak out. Fortunately, the neighbors heard the noise and sounded an alarm, and the bandits did not dare to stay long and left with a howl. As a result, three families were robbed, with losses exceeding 1,000 yuan.

Good Cotton Harvest Expected in Dongxiang

Dongxiang, Xiaoshan, has always grown cotton. This year, the weather has been sunny and clear, and rain has been frequent, so the cotton harvest is very good. Most of the cotton plants are now forming bolls, and new cotton will be seen after the beginning of autumn. After last year's drought and famine, when there was no harvest at all, the general farmers are now overjoyed and singing songs of harvest and prosperous years.

Industrial and Commercial Credit Loan to Begin Disbursement Today - Many People Have Been Crowding the Chamber of Commerce to Obtain Application Forms - Mortgage Loans to Be Negotiated Between Manufacturers and Various Banks

After the Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Loan Review Committee sent the industrial and commercial credit small loan forms to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for distribution, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce began issuing the industrial and commercial credit small loan application forms from the Industrial and Commercial Rehabilitation Committee on July 29th. The number of people going to obtain the forms, such as the Knitting Industry Association, the National Rubber Products Industry Association, the Electric Flower Manufacturing Industry Association, the Machine Flower Dyeing and Weaving Industry Association, the Electric Machine Silk Weaving Industry Association, the Lace Embroidery Industry Association, the Intestine Industry Association, the Clothing Industry Association, and national goods factories with smaller scopes of national goods stores, reached over 1,000 by noon yesterday. The time for obtaining the forms is stipulated to be from 9:30 AM to 11:30 AM and from 1:00 PM to 4:30 PM every day, excluding holidays.

Disbursement to Begin After Passing Review: Manufacturers of national goods, vendors of national goods, and transporters of national goods for export, after obtaining the credit small loan application forms, should fill them out and send them directly to the Industrial and Commercial Loan Review Committee for review. However, it is stipulated that the maximum application amount is 5,000 yuan in national currency. It is approved that loan disbursement will begin on August 1st. Those who have passed the loan review committee's review will be notified by the committee to receive the loan from the bank or money shop that approves the loan, and the applicant is responsible for the investigation fee of one yuan in foreign currency. Those who fail the review will have the fee returned. The interest rate and term are handled according to the loan regulations.

Major Factories Apply for Mortgage Loans: The major factories manufacturing national goods have applied for mortgage loans because the total amount of the industrial and commercial credit small loans is stipulated to be 5,000 yuan in national currency, which is a very small amount. They will negotiate directly with various banks and money shops in Shanghai for a loan according to the loan regulations, and then the mortgaging bank or money shop will submit it to the Loan Review Committee for review. Those who pass the review will be issued a national treasury certificate as the second guarantee. According to a reporter from Xinsheng News Agency, various banks and money shops have begun to negotiate separately with major factories for these mortgage loans.

Representatives of Various Countries Investigate China's Currency - British and French Representatives Scheduled to Arrive in China Next Month - Opinions of Our Financial Circles on the Investigation

According to the Central News Agency, the governments of five countries, Britain, France, the United States, Italy, and Japan, have jointly selected representatives to come to China to investigate the state of China's currency. The British representative has been appointed as Sir Otto Niemeyer, the financial advisor. The French representative is Mr. Renouvin, the financial deputy counsellor of the French embassy in Britain. The American representative has been appointed as Mr. Buck, a professor at Nanjing Jinling University. The Italian and Japanese representatives will also be decided soon. It is learned that the representatives of Britain and France are scheduled to depart from Britain in mid-August to come to China. According to the opinions of financial circles here, they all expressed their approval for the representatives of various countries to come to China to investigate China's currency. However, it is hoped that after the representatives of various countries arrive in China, they will carefully deliberate on everything at the beginning of the investigation and not base it solely on the position of each country (for example, Britain hopes that China's foreign currency will be related to the pound, France hopes to be related to gold, and the United States requires to be related to the US dollar), so as not to lose the original purpose of coming to China for investigation.

Ministry of Finance Orders Sichuan Province to Open Unified Tax - Scheduled to Start Today - Order Issued to Each District Unified Tax Bureau Yesterday to Comply

According to Shenshi News Agency, in order to reorganize Sichuan's finances and reduce the burden on the people, the Ministry of Finance has designated the province as a unified tax area and will open a unified tax office, scheduled to take effect today. The original text of the Ministry of Finance's instruction to each district's unified tax bureau is recorded as follows: Regarding the case of preparing to open a unified tax office in Sichuan Province, the Ministry has previously telegraphed the Sichuan Provincial Government and telegraphed the Sichuan Financial Commissioner to negotiate with the Provincial Government nearby to prepare. According to the Sichuan Financial Commissioner Guan Jiyu's telegram on the 29th, forwarded by the Sichuan Provincial Government on the 28th, it is briefly stated that the Ministry of Finance intends to open a unified tax office in Sichuan Province, and the Provincial Government expresses its strong support. Please ask the Ministry to deliberate and determine the implementation date and notify the Provincial Government so that the local tax bureaus can be informed. From that date, all goods entering the country that have been subject to the unified tax will be exempted from local tax. The goods within Sichuan Province that are subject to the unified tax will be handed over to the organs appointed by the Ministry of Finance to collect the unified tax from that date. It is found that the Sichuan Provincial Government has requested the Ministry to set a date for the implementation of the unified tax in Sichuan Province. The province should be designated as a unified tax area immediately, and the unified tax office should be opened on August 1st of this year. All duty-free transportation certificates for cigarettes shipped to Sichuan Province should be subject to the unified tax and affixed with sufficient stamps to obtain a unified tax transportation certificate from August 1st before they can be shipped. There should be no further double taxation upon arrival in the province. For unified tax goods such as cotton yarn and its woven products, matches, cement, wheat flour, beer, foreign wine, and fire wine, which were previously subject to the unified tax when transported to the province, if there is evidence of double taxation after being delivered to Sichuan Province, the Ministry will be requested to refund the tax. Now that the unified tax office has been opened in Sichuan Province, the double taxation should be stopped to comply with the tax policy. For various unified tax goods manufactured in factories within Sichuan Province, the Sichuan Financial Commissioner should send personnel to the factory to audit and collect the unified tax in accordance with the regulations before they are allowed to be sold. In addition to the distribution, the bureau chief and director are ordered to comply immediately and order all subordinates to comply. This order.

Special report from Xinsheng News Agency: Since Shanghai gentry Wang Yiting and others suggested to the Executive Yuan a method to stabilize finance, it has caused speculation among the general public, causing a considerable impact on the market. Chinese Red Cross Society Starts Membership Drive Today for Two Months; Over Four Hundred Branches Hold Simultaneous Events

Although the market is sluggish, the membership fee has already been reduced, and he requested everyone's assistance and support. Next, Secretary-General Cao Yunxiang reported on the organization's overview, noting that the American Red Cross Society has over ten million members, and Japan has over five million. The sponsorship certificate for this drive embodies this intention, and he hoped that all sectors would jointly support its success. Wang Xiaolai, Yu Zuoting, and others also delivered speeches successively, and the event concluded around 9 p.m.

Four Hundred Branches Hold Simultaneous Events. Simultaneously, all branches of the association across the country will also begin the membership drive today. Currently, there are branches in 72 locations in Jiangsu Province, 28 in Zhejiang Province, 31 in Anhui Province, 5 in Fujian Province, 78 in Henan Province, 20 in Hubei Province, 9 in Jiangxi Province, 10 in Guangdong Province, 7 in Guangxi Province, 2 in Shaanxi Province, 2 in Yunnan Province, 33 in Sichuan Province, 2 in Shanxi Province, 2 in Guizhou Province, 41 in Shandong Province, 41 in Hebei Province, 8 in Jehol Province, 15 in Liaoning Province, 18 in Jilin Province, and 11 in Heilongjiang Province. Haiyi Sails to Guangdong Today; Defense Route Temporarily Suspended

According to the Central News Agency, the Haiyi, a steamship of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company managed by Chinese merchants, after its maiden voyage to Qingdao and back to Shanghai some days ago, is scheduled to officially start sailing on the Shanghai-Guangdong line this afternoon. However, the section from Guangdong to Haiphong will be temporarily suspended due to pending navigation permits. Personnel are being sent to apply for port passenger licenses, and ticket sales are temporarily suspended. The details are as follows:

Sails to Guangdong Today. The Haiyi is scheduled to sail regularly between Shanghai and Guangzhou, stopping at Xiamen, Shantou, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou along the way. The round-trip voyages between Shanghai and Qingdao, and between Guangzhou and Haiphong, are once every two weeks, departing from Shanghai or Guangzhou in the afternoon every three days in alternating weeks. The ship cleared customs last night and is scheduled to sail from Shanghai to Guangdong at 2 p.m. today. The section from Guangdong to Haiphong is temporarily suspended because the navigation permit has not yet been obtained. Ye Chuanfang, manager of the company, has already gone to Beijing some days ago to liaise with the Ministry of Communications.

Cabin Fares. The ship's fares are set as follows: From Shanghai to Qingdao, special class is 12 yuan, first class is 18 yuan, and second class is 12 yuan. From Shanghai to Guangdong, special class is 40 yuan (now sold at a 30% discount for 28 yuan), first class is 24 yuan, and second class is 14 yuan. From Shanghai to Hong Kong, special class is 38 yuan (now sold at a 30% discount for 27 yuan), first class is 23 yuan, and second class is 13 yuan. From Shanghai to Shantou, special class is 36 yuan (now sold at a 30% discount for 25 yuan), first class is 21 yuan, and second class is 12 yuan. From Shanghai to Xiamen, special class is 34 yuan (now sold at a 30% discount for 24 yuan), first class is 20 yuan, and second class is 11 yuan. There are also third and fourth class cabins with very low prices. For special class passengers, Western food will incur an additional fee ranging from 1 to 5 yuan.

The meeting proceeded as follows: (A) Matters Reported (omitted); (B) Matters Discussed: (1) For the sake of commemorating Chairman Chiang, it is proposed to rebuild the Ningbo Xinjiang Bridge and rename it the Zhongzheng Memorial Bridge. The association will initiate a request for Ningbo native associations abroad to be initiating groups. Other organizations, businesses, or individuals may also join the initiation, but only those from the former Ningbo area are eligible. Postal Service Increases Weight Limit for Domestic Parcels

Shanghai Postal Administration Notice No. 1243: It has been found that for all domestic parcels mutually sent between bureaus that have rail transport and those specially permitted to use rail transport, except for parcels to and from Yunnan, the weight limit is temporarily permitted to be increased from 20 kilograms to 30 kilograms (60 market catties) from today. However, for weights exceeding 20 kilograms, additional postage will be charged as follows: (1) Basic fee: 10 cents per kilogram or fraction thereof; (2) Basic fee: 20 cents per kilogram or fraction thereof; (3) Basic fee: 30 cents per kilogram or fraction thereof, and so on. This is urgently notified for general information. This notice.

Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau to Inspect Imported Livestock Starting Today; Imported Cattle and Sheep Must Pass Inspection

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau's livestock inspection has previously only covered exported livestock products, not imported livestock. Following an order from the Ministry of Industry, stating that diseases previously unseen in our country's livestock have recently been introduced from abroad, spreading inland and causing significant harm, measures should be prepared to inspect livestock imports as soon as possible to prevent these diseases. The bureau decided to start with imported cattle and sheep, and drafted detailed implementation rules and supplementary measures, which were submitted to the Ministry of Industry and then to the Executive Yuan for approval. The ministry issued a decree for promulgation. Subsequently, to conduct this inspection, the assistance of the Customs was required, and consultations took some time. It is now reported that the bureau has agreed with the Jianghai Customs Superintendent on provisional measures for livestock import inspection, effective August 1st (i.e., today). From now on, cattle and sheep imported from abroad must pass the bureau's inspection before they can be declared for import. The bureau has officially announced this in newspapers for general knowledge.

The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway's Gongchen Bridge branch line passenger train, since it was changed to stop at the Gongchen Bridge Station's Dengyun Bridge freight platform, has had its timetable slightly altered due to the lack of a turning line facility at the platform, which made shunting time-consuming. Grain Exchange Resumes Auctions of Japanese Wheat Today

According to the Central News Agency, the case of the Grain Exchange resuming auctions of Japanese wheat has been decided by the exchange's board of directors to start from August 1st. A reporter learned the details from the exchange as follows:

Previously Suspended Auctions. Japan originally did not produce wheat. The so-called "Japanese wheat" is wheat that Japanese merchants transship to China for sale from wheat-producing countries. Previously, due to various reasons, the Grain Exchange decided to stop trading in wheat shipped to China by Japanese merchants or Japanese ships. Factories in our country used to order foreign wheat directly from wheat-producing countries.

Resumes Today. Recently, relations between China and Japan have improved, and the Yarn and Cloth Exchange first accepted the circulation of Japanese yarn on the market. The Grain Exchange is also resuming trade with Japanese merchants. It has been found that Japanese merchants ship foreign wheat to China from wheat-producing countries at lower freight costs, so the prices are also cheaper. From August 1st, foreign wheat transported by Japanese merchants will be officially auctioned on the market.

China National Goods Cigarette Maintenance Association Hosts Tobacco Dealers from the Entire City Yesterday

The China National Goods Cigarette Maintenance Association has been working quite intensively recently. Yesterday afternoon, it hosted tobacco dealers from the entire city at the Central Western Restaurant on Fourth Avenue, with over a hundred attendees, including Shen Qixiang, Jie Chengxian, Shen Dehua, and Chen Fuqi. Members of the association, Lao Dixiu and others, were in charge of the reception. The chairman of the association, Yuan Ludeng, Chen Liangyu, and Shen Weiting, delivered speeches. Teng Zhixiang, a representative of the tobacco dealers, expressed his opinions. Shen Weiting then spoke on behalf of the tobacco dealers, followed by individual talks by tobacco dealers present. They unanimously expressed their determination to rise up in cooperation and maintain national goods cigarettes. Tea and snacks were served, and the meeting adjourned. The speeches are listed below: (1) Member Yuan Ludeng stated, "I am deeply grateful that everyone has come despite the heat. The highest goal of our association is to maintain and then develop the city. The development of national cigarettes is also in the interest of tobacco dealers. Our association and the tobacco dealers are as dependent as arms and teeth. In these difficult times, our association deeply expects the tobacco dealers to make efforts to support us, and not just to go through the motions." (2) Member Chen Liangyu stated, "The gradual decline of Chinese cigarette factories is due to many reasons, and the encroachment of privately-made hand-rolled cigarettes on the market is one of them. I dare to hope that manufacturers will petition the tax bureau to strictly ban them, so that tobacco dealers can devote their full efforts to the sales of Chinese cigarette factories. Now, various industries related to national goods cigarettes, such as cigarette factories, tobacco leaves, and color printing, have organized maintenance associations, which can pool their wisdom and efforts. Tobacco dealers should not be an exception and should contribute their modest efforts, while also seeking to benefit themselves and others." (3) Member Shen Weiting stated, "Today, tobacco dealers have gathered together, with some coming from afar. Seeing this good sign, it is worthy of celebration for the future of our national goods cigarettes. Our association plans to conduct a large-scale publicity campaign to awaken the determination of compatriots across the country to smoke national goods cigarettes. I deeply hope that all tobacco dealers will assist in our association's publicity work and devote their full efforts to promoting national cigarettes, so that Chinese cigarette factories can have a chance to survive. I now ask everyone present to express their views, and all tobacco dealers are always willing to provide guidance to our association's work, so as to achieve speedy and great results. I cannot but hope for this." (4) Guest Teng Zhixiang inquired, "The Maintenance Association is hosting us tobacco dealers today, with high expectations for our industry to cooperate in promoting national goods cigarettes. It is believed that difficult times build a nation. Today, the national cigarette industry is also in a difficult situation. People are thinking of striving, so there is the organization of the Maintenance Association. If practical work is implemented, the difficult situation can be overcome. In my humble opinion, to seek the prosperity of national goods cigarettes, one is to research and refine the quality of the product itself, and the other is to resist and ban privately-made hand-rolled cigarettes. If the tobacco leaf industry can refuse to trade with them, and the tax bureau can severely punish them, the scourge of private cigarettes can be eliminated. As for the Maintenance Association's wish for our industry to assist in publicity, if there are practical measures, our industry will be happy to devote our efforts to running errands." (5) Representative Shen stated on behalf of the tobacco dealers, "Now, I, representing the tobacco dealers, have something to present. The tobacco dealers are happy to promote national goods cigarettes. Even small shop clerks have the same feeling. It is believed that everyone will share in the glory of seeing national goods come to light. The current business of tobacco dealers is also in a state of decline. Although the market is sluggish, the encroachment of tax-free private cigarettes on the legitimate retail business of tobacco dealers is one of the reasons. In summary, cigarettes and tobacco dealers are like arms and hands. If the two sides can exchange opinions at any time and jointly plan the development of the business, it will be twice the result with half the effort, and everyone will benefit. Just as the Maintenance Association needs our tobacco dealers to assist in its work, our tobacco dealers will also strive to move towards it."

China Merchants Bureau Sells Guangji Steamship for Scrap; Purchased by Hualun Foreign Firm; Sale Price 9,500 Yuan

The China Merchants Bureau's Wenzhou liner Guangji, due to its old age, was opposed by various public groups in Yongjia last year after the electricity department protested its navigation. The bureau was ordered by the Ministry to stop its northern sailings and was left idle in the Huangpu River for a year. The bureau has repeatedly tendered it for sale, but the bid prices were too low and did not meet the limit, so it was unsuccessful. Now the bureau has changed its approach and is selling the Guangji for scrap. The purchase is restricted, and it is not allowed to be repaired and sailed on any route. It can only be dismantled and sold for steel and machinery, distributed and sold separately, or converted into a hulk. The sale price has been reduced to the lowest amount. Now it has been purchased by Hualun Foreign Firm for 9,500 yuan, and the payment has been made. The bureau sent a letter to the firm yesterday, asking them to send someone to take over the ship. However, all other expenses will be borne by the firm. It has been found that although the Guangji is old, the quality of the hull is excellent and it is the oldest and most historical ocean-going vessel of the bureau.

Nanjing Red Swastika Society Raises Funds to Help with Rice Crust Porridge and Fried Indica Rice

Nanjing Red Swastika Society Raises Funds to Help with Rice Crust Porridge and Fried Indica Rice for Flood Relief: This year's floods are severe, and emergency relief is most important. However, for emergency relief, how can it be effective and how can it save lives? There must be in-depth research. The Swastika Society has handled floods for many years, and based on its experience, the most important thing is to go deep into the flooded areas at the time of the flooding, hire boats to rescue refugees, and distribute dry food and medicine. The most effective dry food for emergency relief and saving lives is rice crust porridge or fried indica rice. This is because the disaster victims are in the water, and they can chew on this rice crust porridge or fried rice at any time. Not only can it save lives, but it can also prevent epidemics. Because rice crust porridge and fried rice have a fragrant and dry taste and help with moisture and water, they are sufficient to treat diseases. Now, we loudly appeal to the public, hoping that all rice-eating areas in the north and south of the Yangtze River, provinces, counties, cities, and villages, will show great compassion and donate some rice crust porridge or fried indica rice, and hand them over to the Red Swastika Society in various places, or local organizations, to collect them, pack them into sacks, and transfer them to this society at any time for distribution in the disaster areas. In a very short time, millions of catties of dry food can be accumulated, saving the lives of millions of disaster victims. This kind of merit is easy to do, so why not do it? It is more beneficial than subsequent general relief. If you are willing to donate, please send it to our society at Xiaohuowa Lane in Nanjing for acceptance. Receipts will be issued according to the weight in catties to show trustworthiness. We bow our heads nine times to the disaster victims and ask for your consideration. Sincerely, the Nanjing Red Swastika Society.

Suffering Due to Public Service: Wang Bin'yan Bankrupt, Forced to Sell Home to Repay Debt; Third Trial Concludes with August 10th Auction of Residence

Wang Bin'yan, the head of the Zhabei Defense Corps, is known throughout Zhabei for his enthusiasm for public welfare and defense of the area. During the Jiangsu-Zhejiang War in the thirteenth year of the Republic (1924), Zhabei suddenly saw an influx of over 40,000 soldiers and 20,000 refugees. The people were panicked and order was disrupted. Fortunately, the then-Governor of Jiangsu Province and Superintendent of Military Rehabilitation, Han Guojun, repeatedly telegraphed Wang to take responsibility for maintaining local supplies and military provisions to prevent local devastation. Wang, in the name of the Zhabei Charity Association, sought to borrow money, totaling 228,649.70 yuan in advances. He submitted a register, and the Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, Zeng Pu, came to Shanghai to sign a contract. It was reported to the Ministry of the Army for record-keeping, with all the land of the state-owned Shanghai Manufacturing Bureau as collateral. Among these advances, the title deeds to Wang's private residence in Zhabei on Mei Road, Tongde Lane, and nine mu (approximately 1.5 acres) of land were mortgaged to the Guangdong Bank, the Hong Kong National Bank, and the Cunde Money Exchange for 30,000 taels of silver. Over the past ten years, the principal and interest have not been repaid, with a total debt exceeding 84,000 yuan. Repeated demands for payment from Wang have been unsuccessful, leading to a lawsuit in court, which has now been judged in a third trial, ordering full repayment. However, Wang, who has served as the head of the Zhabei Charity Association and the head of the Defense Corps, is known for his integrity and has no savings. Previously, the Hong Kong National Bank auctioned Wang's house on Hua Mu Land to settle the debt. Now, due to the Guangdong Bank's lawsuit and the third trial verdict, the Shanghai Local Court of Jiangsu Province has issued a summons for execution at 8:00 AM yesterday. Although Wang hired lawyers Wang Liangqing and Zhu Chengxun to request a temporary postponement of execution, it was denied, with a deadline of August 10th to auction Wang's residence to repay the mortgage debt. Recently, prominent figures such as Lin Kanghou, Fang Jiaobo, Chen Bingkun, Lu Bohong, Shen Lianfang, and Xu Qianlin, as well as Shen Huachen representing the Silk Industry Association, She Xipin representing the Timber Industry Association, Qiang Zisheng representing the Rice Milling Industry Association, and Fu Qiangeng representing the Bean and Rice Industry Association, have witnessed Wang's entire family facing bankruptcy due to public service. They have repeatedly requested the Local Association and Minister Kong to provide swift assistance. The Chairman of the Local Association, Du Yuesheng, as well as Qian Xinzhi, Wang Xiaolai, and Zhou, are making every effort to help, and have personally requested Minister Kong for relief. It is also reported that the Cunde Money Exchange at 316 Ningbo Road has also hired lawyer Wang Youling to sue Wang in the Local Court, with a hearing scheduled for August 10th.

Resolution of Rent Reduction Dispute in Hengmao Lane; Both Parties Sign Rent Reduction Agreement

The Hengmao Lane Branch of the Second Special District Rent Reduction Committee of Shanghai has been dealing with a dispute over rent reduction requested by tenants from the landlord, Sun Meitang, manager of Hengmao Real Estate Company, due to the city's economic downturn. After mediation by Fan Hengde, Xie Baosheng, and Jiang Wenzhang, a resolution has been reached. The details of the process are as follows:

Meeting Report

Yesterday afternoon, the Hengmao Lane Branch of the Second Special District Rent Reduction Committee of Shanghai held a general meeting of tenant members at the branch office at No. 53 Hengmao Lane. Over twenty people attended. Chairman Jin Zhizhi reported on the progress of the rent reduction request to the landlord, as well as the signing of an agreement on the 29th of last month. It was also publicly agreed to issue a notice to all tenant members to comply with the agreement. The meeting adjourned at 4:00 PM.

Negotiated Agreement

(1) Starting from October 1935, the original rent of 75 yuan for a single-unit house in the lane will be reduced to 70 yuan, and the original rent of 140 yuan for a double-unit house will be reduced to 130 yuan. Within two years (from October 1935 to the end of September 1937), both parties are responsible for ensuring that the rent is not increased or decreased. (2) For the two months of rent reduction from October to December of this year, the landlord will still collect the original amount due to other considerations. The tenants will deduct the amount of the two months' rent reduction when paying the rent in November 1936. (3) The landlord shall not sublet individual rooms in either the double-unit or single-unit houses in the lane. (4) This committee will, to the extent possible, dispatch personnel to assist in the collection of rent arrears owed by the tenants in the lane. (5) This agreement shall take effect after being signed by the responsible parties of both sides, and two copies shall be made, with each side holding one copy for record.

Traditional Chinese Medicine Doctor Zhu Shuping Found Not Guilty; Sun Hu's Family Also Found Not Guilty

Zhu Shuping, a traditional Chinese medicine doctor residing at No. 57 Changsha Road, prescribed medicine containing Ephedra and Aconite for the two-year-old child of the woman Sun Hu, who was suffering from lingering symptoms after being treated for measles. Unexpectedly, after taking the medicine, the child's condition deteriorated and death could not be averted. Sun Hu blamed Zhu, accusing him of negligence in his practice, and filed a criminal lawsuit against Zhu. However, Zhu argued that his treatment was proper and denied any negligence, and accused Sun Hu of false accusation and defamation, and filed a counterclaim against her.

Under the jurisdiction of the Special District Local Court, with both parties holding to their own claims and the question of whether Dr. Zhu was negligent only being determinable by those with specialized knowledge, it was agreed by both parties that the prescription written by Zhu would be sent to the National Medical Association for evaluation. The association replied to the court that the prescription was not improper. The presiding judge Liu summoned both parties for questioning, and yesterday afternoon announced the verdict: Zhu Shuping was not guilty, and Sun Hu's family was also not guilty.

Procedures for Repatriating Unemployed Hunanese

Due to the poor economic situation, the number of unemployed people is increasing daily. Since the Dragon Boat Festival, over 500 unemployed people from Hunan have been living in Shanghai without any means of support. They have gone to the Hunanese Association in Shanghai to request relief and assistance in returning to their hometowns. The association has specially dispatched Zhou Zhenlin to negotiate with the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, requesting them to provide preferential treatment as with the repatriation of refugees. It is proposed to charter a special ship starting today to transport all these unemployed Hunanese back to Changsha within half a month. The company stated that according to the regulations issued by the ministry for the repatriation of refugees, official documents must be provided by the competent authorities, such as the Relief Committee, the Provincial Government, the Municipal Government, or the Public Security Bureau, before the company can proceed accordingly. The relevant regulations have now been sent to the Hunanese Association, asking them to follow the procedures. As soon as notification is received from the competent authorities, a ship will be dispatched for repatriation.

Suicide Attempt Due to Poverty; Rescued and Given a New Chance

Yan Huaiqing, a 42-year-old from Jiaxing, used to work as a female laborer in a cotton mill in Nantong. Recently, due to crop failures and famine, she borrowed over ten yuan last month and came to Shanghai to look for her younger brother but was unsuccessful. Recently, her wallet was stolen by a pickpocket, leaving her penniless. Yesterday morning, she walked to Zhuanqiao Town, where, overwhelmed by resentment and hunger, she conceived the idea of ending her life. She hanged herself from a tree by the roadside. Later, a villager spotted her and managed to rescue her, giving her a new chance. She was immediately taken to the local police station, and the police chief arranged to purchase a train ticket to send her back to her hometown in Jiaxing to prevent her from becoming destitute in another place.

Double Suicide Attempt at the Great China Hotel; Truth Awaits Investigation

At around 3:00 PM the day before yesterday, a male guest checked into the Great China Hotel at the intersection of Fuzhou Road and Xizang Road. The hotel accountant led him to Room 431, where he stayed. The guest was wearing a white silk long gown and short shirt and pants, and identified himself as Zhang Mingfu, 22 years old, from Songjiang. He did not go out during the day and seemed relaxed. Until around 9:00 PM that night, a woman, claiming to be Ms. Zhang, 21 years old, from Songjiang, went to Room 431 to meet with Zhang Mingfu. They were very intimate. Shortly after, they closed the door and went to bed, with nothing else unusual happening. Until around 12:00 PM yesterday, a tea boy on the floor, seeing that they had not gotten up, went to knock on the door. He received no response for a long time, which aroused his suspicion. He managed to open the door and found the man and woman lying on the bed, both pale and unconscious. Remnants of poison were found beside the pillows, indicating that they had taken poison. He immediately reported to the police station, and the two were rushed to the hospital for treatment. However, due to the severity of the poisoning, they were unable to speak even late into the evening. Therefore, the truth remains to be investigated.

Ms. Xu Xue, a woman from Haimen residing at the Xu Xuefa teahouse at the Xiaomu Bridge on Longhua Road, and her younger sister, Zhang Xiuying (30 years old), were carrying coal ash on a coal boat in the Caohujing River in Longhua at 1:30 PM yesterday. Xu Xue reported the incident to the local police station. It was reported that Zhang Xiuying had been suffering from mental illness for over two months.
