Robbers Simultaneously Loot Three Businesses at the Intersection of Yangshupu Road and Linqing Road; Divided into Two Groups, Robbing in Different Directions, Then Converging to Continue the Robbery; Police Apprehend Three Robbers After Strict Pursuit

At approximately 8:35 PM last night, a robbery occurred at the intersection of Yangshupu Road and Linqing Road. The robbers were incredibly audacious, continuously robbing as many as three businesses. According to eyewitnesses, there were a total of eight robbers, six of whom were wearing black Guangdong silk shirts and pants, each carrying a handgun. The other two were wearing blue cloth shirts and pants and were unarmed. They spoke in various local, Shandong, and Jiangbei accents. All were of short stature. During the robbery, the robbers split into two groups. Four robbers robbed the Dachang Woolen Shop at No. 2061 Yangshupu Road. The robbers wearing blue cloth shirts and pants jumped over the counter and into the shop, snatching all the silver dollars and several hundred small coins from the cash register and fleeing. When one of the shop employees saw this and tried to run out to call for help, he was spotted by a lookout, who fired a shot into the air to scare him back. At the same time, the other four robbers had already broken into the Yuantai Chang Southern Goods Shop at No. 2057 Yangshupu Road. The shop was in the process of distributing salaries to the employees, so all the cash and banknotes, totaling about 300 yuan, were taken. The robbers quickly retreated and rejoined the robbers who had looted the Dachang Shop, and headed to the Hudong Shoe Shop at No. 15 Linqing Road, where they robbed again. However, the shoe shop did not have much money, so only 25 yuan in banknotes was stolen. Still not satisfied, the robbers smashed the display window and snatched two bolts of Guangdong silk and four pairs of slippers before shouting and fleeing north towards the Xiangyin Road area. By the time the patrolling police arrived, the robbers had long since fled. The three shops then checked their losses and reported the robbery to the local police station, requesting an investigation. It was learned that when the robbers were carrying out the robbery, the area had not yet closed for the day, and many residents and shop employees had witnessed the event. Some had followed the robbers secretly, intending to investigate their actions, but the robbers showed no concern. Their audacity was unparalleled. When the robbers retreated from the Hudong Lujiazhuang area, the crowds watching the robbers were unable to avoid each other, causing a girl to be knocked to the ground and break her nose. She has now been sent to the hospital for treatment. The fact that people, knowing it was a robbery, did not attempt to capture the robbers but instead followed them as if watching a strange and exciting event is truly incomprehensible. As of the time of this writing, it has been learned that the local police station has apprehended three robbers and is currently interrogating them.

Meeting of Creditors of China Industrial Bank; Creditors Refuse to Vote; Creditors Oppose, Meeting Adjourns Without Results; Xu Yongzuo Announces Assets, Liabilities

Since the China Industrial Bank went bankrupt on October 11th of last year, a lawsuit has been filed in the First Special District Local Court. The court appointed accountants Xu Yongzuo, Li Ding, and lawyer Qian Shusheng to conduct liquidation. Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, a meeting of creditors was held at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Because the creditors unanimously opposed the settlement plan proposed by Lu Xihou, the meeting adjourned without results. The details obtained by the China News Agency reporter are as follows:

Creditors Present: Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, a meeting of creditors of the China Industrial Bank was held to solicit the creditors' agreement to the settlement plan proposed by Lu Xihou. A total of 1,214 creditor representatives, including Xiang Xun, Luo Jiaheng, Tang Mingshi, Yu Zhongluo, Dong Yu, Wang Shuxun, Hu Yaocheng, and Zheng Zhaoding, attended, representing claims totaling 382,745.89 yuan. The debtor Lu Xihou was represented by lawyer Lu Ruizheng. The chairman group consisted of Li Jiashan, a clerk dispatched by the First Special District Court, and liquidators Xu Yongzuo, accountant Li Ding, and lawyer Qian Shusheng. Zhang Shourang served as the recorder.

Meeting Order: The order of the meeting was as follows: (1) Ringing the bell to open the meeting; (2) Reporting the number of attendees and the amount of debt; (3) Reporting the progress of the liquidation; (4) Reporting the asset and liability situation; (5) Electing supervisors; (6) Deciding on the settlement plan; (7) Other proposals; (8) Adjourning the meeting. However, when the chairman group took the stage to report, most of the creditors had already expressed their opposition, and discussions arose. The meeting became chaotic, and people began to shout. Li Ding reported on the meaning of the meeting, and Li Jiashan, a clerk from the court, explained that if the creditors opposed the settlement plan proposed by Lu Xihou, they could cast a negative vote. If they agreed, they could cast a positive vote. They were urged to calm down.

Refusal to Vote: During the meeting, creditor lawyers Yu Zhongluo, Tang Mingshi, and others raised questions to the chairman group, which can be divided into three points: (1) Is this liquidation truly a liquidation of the China Industrial Bank, or is it a liquidation of Lu Xihou and Lu Mengxiang, two people related to the China Industrial Bank? (2) The China Industrial Bank was established in 1923, with an authorized capital of 20 million yuan and a paid-up capital of over 2.5 million yuan. How was this 2.5 million yuan of capital used? (3) The shareholders, directors, and supervisors of the China Industrial Bank include many reputable or wealthy individuals, and they should all be responsible for repayment. Before the lawyers finished speaking, some creditors proposed to refuse to vote, and they all left one after another. The meeting adjourned without any results.

Total Liabilities: The China News Agency reporter went to the accounting firm of liquidator Xu Yongzuo to investigate the total liabilities of the bank. The Nanjing Road Head Office had 741,172.32 yuan, the Nanshi Branch had 106,872.81 yuan, the Tianzhutang Street Branch had 97,190.89 yuan, the Foch Road Branch had 148,411.33 yuan, the Songjiang Branch had 51,796.43 yuan, the Suzhou Branch had 122,309.75 yuan, and the Dongshan Branch had 25,446.20 yuan, totaling 1,293,769.74 yuan. After deducting outstanding payments, the actual liabilities were 812,981.90 yuan.

Total Assets: The estimated total assets were 694,760.47 yuan for the Nanjing Road Head Office, 61,727.70 yuan for the Nanshi Branch, 22,228.09 yuan for the Tianzhutang Street Branch, 6,676.03 yuan for the Foch Road Branch, 15,043.37 yuan for the Songjiang Branch, and 4,993.37 yuan for the Dongshan Branch, totaling 850,506.91 yuan. After deducting the amount of collateralized deposits and bad debts, the actual assets were only 193,199.38 yuan, which was far short. According to Xu Yongzuo, the creditors present did not reach the legally required three-quarters. He will have to consult with the court tonight.

Worsening Problem of French Concession Rickshaw Puller Registration; Rickshaw Pullers to Petition Today; Rickshaw Owners Unanimously Oppose

The issue of the French Concession periodically registering rickshaw pullers has been met with opposition from both rickshaw owners and pullers since the news came out. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce and other organizations have mediated, but to no avail. The situation is becoming increasingly serious. Rickshaw puller representatives launched a major petition yesterday. The details are as follows:

French Municipal Council: The registration of rickshaw pullers has been underway for a month, but rickshaw owners and pullers, considering their vital interests, have resolutely opposed it. To date, no one has registered at the registration office. The police department of the French Municipal Council plans to ban unregistered rickshaws from operating starting August 1st (today) and requested the assistance of the municipal government the day before yesterday.

Rickshaw Puller Petition: After the French authorities decided to ban unregistered rickshaws from operating starting today, rickshaw owners and pullers were extremely panicked, fearing that their livelihoods would be cut off. Rickshaw puller representatives, including Shi Changsheng, led over 40 representatives to the Nanshi Rickshaw Trade Association at No. 34 Sanmin Lane, Caoyudong Road, to petition, stating that the rickshaw pullers unanimously opposed registration. The association representatives promised to relay the message to the rickshaw owners. It is reported that a large-scale petition will be held again today.

Rickshaw Owner Meeting: The rickshaw owners, sympathizing with the demands of the rickshaw pullers, oppose registration. It is reported that the French police department will ban unregistered rickshaws from operating starting today, and the rickshaw owners, considering the importance of the matter, have decided to hold a meeting today to discuss how to respond.

Representative's Remarks: Yesterday, a spokesperson for the rickshaw owners stated, "The relationship between the rickshaw owners and the concession authorities is limited to paying taxes and operating. Regarding the rickshaw puller registration issue, the main stakeholders are the rickshaw pullers. Whether to register or not is up to the rickshaw pullers to decide, and the rickshaw owners have no need to make any claims. However, the relationship between the rickshaw owners and the rickshaw pullers is close, like lips and teeth. Most of the rickshaw pullers in Nanshi are ignorant and lack social experience. Not only do they not understand the true meaning of registration, but they also spread various unfavorable rumors. Previously, when registration was rumored, the rickshaw pullers fled back to their hometowns, as if a major disaster was about to happen. This caused a great blow to the rickshaw owners' business. Later, the situation calmed down slightly after the rickshaw owners provided firm guarantees that there would be no registration. Now that registration is actually being implemented, the rickshaw pullers will flee again, and the rickshaw owners' business will be hit hard first. To protect their own business, the rickshaw owners sympathize with the rickshaw pullers and oppose registration. As for the French Municipal Council, they previously allowed the rickshaw owners: (1) to register freely without time limit; (2) to hold registration procedures in batches. (All to be publicly announced by the French authorities in the newspaper.) Unexpectedly, the ink was not yet dry, and the French authorities broke their promise. Starting from August 1st, they immediately banned unregistered rickshaws and forced all rickshaws in the French Concession, whether they should register or not, to register, with all sorts of threats. This situation is regrettable. If the French authorities take drastic measures against the rickshaw pullers starting today, and provoke an unexpected incident, who will be responsible? Anyone with clear eyes can see it at a glance. We deeply hope that people from all walks of life will rise up and provide assistance so that the livelihoods of tens of thousands of rickshaw pullers can be preserved, which would be a great blessing for society."

——Grand Welcome Reception to Be Held at Shanghai World College on the Fourth

Mr. Mei Lanfang, having accepted an invitation from Soviet Russia this spring to perform Chinese symbolic drama arts, was warmly welcomed by the people there. Sir Robert Ho Tung originally intended to hold a grand welcome reception after the ship's arrival, but after consulting with the company, it was stated that due to the tide in Shanghai, the ship must set sail from Hong Kong at 11:00 AM sharp, and could not stay in Hong Kong for long. The company expressed its deep apologies, and therefore the welcome reception could not be held due to time constraints. It was decided to hold a small gathering at the Hong Kong Hotel at 9:00 AM on the second, with simpler arrangements and fewer people, in order to have a good meeting. All arrangements were made in advance via wireless telegraph to the ship, and the receptions along the way were very busy. It is also reported that prominent figures in Shanghai, including Li Shi Cao, Qian Xin Zhi, and Du Yue Sheng, will hold a grand welcome tea party at Shanghai World College on the day after Mr. Mei's arrival in Shanghai (the fourth), to welcome him back. It is anticipated that Mr. Mei will be very busy with banquets and appointments from all sides after his return to China.

Feng Zhiming and Liu Zhaokui, Chinese detectives of the General Inspectorate, and Wu Hanzhang, a detective's assistant, cracked down on a large-scale counterfeit silver dollar manufacturing organization and office at 806 Zhoujiazhui Road and 789 Dalianwan Road on the morning of the ninth of last month. Xie Wenyun, a 24-year-old native of Nanjing, works as a messenger at the Jian Da Silver Store in Ruyi Lane, Henan Road. He usually likes to frequent brothels and is familiar with the prostitute Liu Di, a former popular prostitute (Kresler), at No. 22 Huile Lane, Yunnan Road. They sing and drink together almost every night. On June 20th of this year, Xie invited many friends to have a banquet at Liu Di's brothel. Although Xie is a messenger at a silver store, his monthly income is limited, so how can he indulge in wine and women and spend money arbitrarily? However, with beautiful women in front of him, he cannot help but pretend to be a big shot. At that time, although Xie did not have cash on hand, he issued two Jian Da Silver Store promissory notes, one due on July 5th, for 100 yuan, and one due on July 10th, for 150 yuan, to Liu Di. The issuer of the notes was Xiang Kang Hao, and it was stated that Xiang Kang Hao was located at No. 17 Yong'an Street in the French Concession. On June 29th, Xie went to Liu Di's place again to drink and pay respects, and gave her another Jian Da Silver Store promissory note due on July 20th, for 80 yuan. However, Xie knew at the time that the three notes he had issued could not be cashed, and the first note was about to expire soon, so he used a perfunctory method and asked Liu Di's brothel to collect the second note on July 10th at the same time as the first note. At that time, the brothel did not know Xie's bottom line, so they agreed. When the time came, Shen Qiao, the manager of the brothel, instructed someone to take the note to the Jian Da Silver Store to find Xie, but he was not there. By July 13th, the Jian Da Silver Store had changed its name to Jin He Silver Store, and the manager had also been replaced by Guo Yun Gong. Because they did not see Xie, they could not negotiate. It was not until the 16th that they met Xie. After negotiations, Guo Yun Gong paid 40 yuan on behalf of Xie, and the remaining amount was to be paid later. Unexpectedly, Jin He Silver Store suddenly closed down a few days later, and Xie Wenyun also avoided meeting. Until the afternoon of the day before yesterday, when Xie was passing by Fuzhou Road, he was spotted by Bai Sheng, a rickshaw driver from Liu Di's brothel, who reported him to Chinese Constable No. 2359 and detective Xia Shikuai, who arrested Xie and detained him in the Zhabei Police Station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The police lawyer Zhang Shizhu filed charges of fraud and breach of trust under Article 339 of the Criminal Law, and presented the above situation, requesting legal action. According to Shen Qiao, the manager of Liu Di's brothel, the defendant had twice held banquets there and issued checks, but when they went to collect the money, they could not find it. When questioned, the defendant's testimony was vague. Judge Ye Shengchao verified the testimony and sentenced Xie Wenyun to one year and six months in prison for forging valuable documents.

Counterfeiting Whiskey: Four Bottles of Counterfeit Liquor Mixed into Each Dozen; Those Involved Sentenced or Fined

Lu Su Kui, Chief Chinese Inspector of the General Police Station, Detectives Feng Zhiming, Liu Shaokui, and Chen Yonggui, Detective's Assistant, etc., previously discovered that someone was secretly organizing the counterfeiting of "whiskey" for sale in the city. The method of manufacturing was to first collect hundreds of empty whiskey bottles, and then spend money to buy genuine whiskey, which was mixed with Chinese whiskey. Because according to market prices, each bottle of whiskey costs eight or nine yuan, while each bottle of Chinese whiskey costs one yuan, these people mixed eight bottles of genuine whiskey with four bottles of Chinese whiskey in each dozen for profit. Therefore, last month, they first purchased three dozen bottles of counterfeit liquor from Chen Heting in Room 305 of the Shenzhou Hotel on Zhejiang Road, at a price of 75 yuan per dozen (genuine whiskey costs 86 yuan per dozen). Chen was arrested, and then his accomplices Feng Jialuo and Gan Songlin were arrested at No. 27 Zhengde Lane, Zhaofeng Road, and Chen Qinshi and Xue Guisheng were arrested at No. 12 Houde Lane, Kunming Road. Jiang Baoheng was arrested at No. 44 Wufu Lane, Tangshan Road. Qin Baohua, Weng Qiaquan, and Chen Jingui were arrested at No. 67, 3-chome, Kitayongdori, Kobe City, Japan, and Nagoya Port, and transferred to Shanghai. A machine for manufacturing counterfeit liquor and other liquor materials and equipment were found in the upstairs of the Xindan Primary School at No. 373 Yuezhou Road. Three hundred empty bottles were seized at No. 50 Fengsheng Lane, Maohai Road, and taken to the police station and sent to the First Special Court. After several interrogations, the defendants hired many lawyers, including Chen Tingrui and Yan Yinwu, to defend them. The police lawyer Zhang Shizhu filed charges under Articles 339, 253, and 254 of the Criminal Law. After the interrogation was concluded, Judge Ye announced the verdict in Criminal Court No. 2 yesterday morning. The main text of the verdict stated: Qin Baohua was sentenced to four months in prison for jointly and continuously intending to deceive and counterfeit a registered trademark. Feng Jialuo and Weng Qiaquan were sentenced to a fine of 300 yuan each for the same crime. Jiang Baoheng was fined 240 yuan. Chen Heting and Zhao Songlin were each fined 200 yuan for continuously selling goods knowing that they were counterfeit trademarks. Chen Qinshi, Xue Guisheng, and Chen Jingui were each fined 100 yuan for helping others to counterfeit trademarks. If the fine is commuted to labor, it will be calculated at three yuan per day. Two dozen and twelve bottles of counterfeit whiskey, as well as machinery and other items, were confiscated. The remaining items, except for contracts and letters, were returned separately.

The Sad Story of a Woman, Lu Fengbao: Two Childhood Fiancés Died of Illness; Finally Married a Man Who Turned Out to Be a Bigamist—Failed Attempt to Become a Nun

Lu Fengbao, a woman from Anhui, is 25 years old this year and currently resides at No. 25 Pi Shao Nai Road, outside the Little North Gate of the French Concession. Her father died when she was only three years old. Because her family was poor, her mother had no way to make a living, so she lived with Wang A'lian (48 years old this year), a fellow villager from Anhui. Wang ran a Wang Gui Ji shoe store on Xinzha Road, Xujiazhai, in the International Settlement. At that time, because Fengbao was young, she was not allowed to work at the store, so she was introduced to the Zhang family in Zhenru Township as a daughter-in-law, and became a childhood fiancée. Before long, the Zhang family's son unfortunately died young. Wang A'lian returned eight yuan to the Zhang family as a refund for the betrothal gifts, and took Fengbao back. When the girl was 13 years old, she was once again engaged to the Liu family in Zhenru Township as a childhood fiancée. At the age of 17, her fiancé, the Liu family's son, fell ill and died again. Wang A'lian again returned sixteen yuan to the Liu family as a refund and took Fengbao back to the Wang Gui Ji shoe store he ran. Unfortunately, Fengbao's mother also died at this time. Wang ordered Fengbao to help take care of household affairs. Over time, in the spring of the 22nd year, Fengbao had an affair with Yang Zhaochang, a shop assistant. It was discovered by her de facto father, Wang A'lian. Since what's done is done, he gave his daughter to Yang Zhaochang as his wife. On the 19th day of the sixth lunar month of that year, he had Fengbao marry Yang and officially live together. At first, the couple's relationship was very close, but good times don't last forever, and the moon is not always full. Fengbao learned that Yang already had a wife living in his hometown. From then on, the couple often quarreled and their relationship broke down. Last month, Yang secretly had an affair with a concubine surnamed Someone and ran away with her, abandoning Fengbao and leaving her alone. At this time, Wang A'lian wanted to rape Fengbao and take her as his wife, but she refused. At this point, Fengbao thought about the hardships she had suffered from childhood to adulthood, and lamented her ill fate. At the end of last month, she went alone to the Tianzhu Nunnery in Hangzhou, intending to ask the head nun to take her in and shave her head to become a nun, wishing to spend the rest of her life with the ancient Buddha and a clear lamp. However, the nun demanded a filial piety fee of 200 yuan, otherwise she would refuse to take her in. Because Fengbao had no money to pay, she had to return to Shanghai and live with a little sister at No. 25 Pi Shao Nai Road. After all, the days are long, and she has no one to rely on. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit with the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court, accusing Yang Zhaochang and her de facto father Wang A'lian of bigamy, abandonment, and offenses against morality, requesting that they be investigated according to the law. She also filed a civil lawsuit, requesting that Wang A'lian be ordered to return the 200 yuan in betrothal gifts she gave to Yang Zhaochang, and the 300 yuan in cash and jewelry that her mother had accumulated over the years and deposited with Wang, for a total of 500 yuan. Based on the complaint, the court summoned the plaintiff Lu Fengbao to the Second Criminal Court for questioning at 10:00 AM yesterday, presided over by Judge Li Changnian. The plaintiff Lu Fengbao arrived on time and stated the above. The defendant Yang Zhaochang was on the run and did not appear. Wang A'lian appeared with his defense lawyer and denied all the allegations. After verifying the testimony in court, he ordered the debate to begin and announced the conclusion. He instructed that the trial of Yang Zhaochang be suspended, and the verdict on Wang A'lian would be announced on the morning of August 6.

The bandits were sent to the Second Special Court for prosecution. Tao Shuigen and Wang Fukang died of illness during the interrogation period. After the trial of Lin and others was concluded, Lin De was sentenced to life imprisonment and deprived of civil rights for life. Zhang Huizhi and Zhou Juqin were each sentenced to 15 years in prison. Li Shengxiao was found not guilty. The prosecution of Tao and Wang was dismissed. Later, Lin, Zhang, and Zhou appealed the original verdict to the Gao San Branch. These details have been reported in this newspaper. The Gao San Branch Collegial Panel concluded the trial. At 8:00 AM yesterday, Court President Guo, accompanied by Judges Fan and Li, went to Criminal Court No. 3 and ruled that Lin De would still be sentenced to life imprisonment and deprived of civil rights for life. The sentences of Zhang Huizhi and Zhou Juqin were each reduced to seven years of imprisonment. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be deducted from the sentence at a rate of one day for one day. The judge also explained the meaning of the verdict to the criminals. After the explanation was completed, he ordered them to be returned to the detention center. Upon hearing the ruling, Zhang and Zhou cried loudly and repeatedly protested their innocence. Lin suffered from insanity while in custody and was unable to walk on his own, so he was escorted back to the detention center by a bailiff.

Medical Doctor Liu Yongchun Returns to China

Liu Yongchun, a native of Jiangdu, Jiangsu, graduated from Aurora University Medical School in the eleventh year of the Republic of China (1922). He then went to Paris and Strasbourg in France to continue his studies, earning a doctorate and serving as the director of the clinical department of the Strasbourg Medical School for three years. In the seventeenth year of the Republic of China (1928), he returned to China and served as a member of the Sino-Belgian Gengkuan Health Construction Committee. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China (1929), the Chinese and French governments had a plan to establish a Pasteur Institute in Shanghai, and specially sent Dr. Liu to the Saigon Pasteur Institute to study microbiology. Dr. Liu saw that the Sino-French Pasteur Institute plan had no hope of proceeding during his three years in Vietnam, so he accepted the invitation of the Saigon Pasteur Institute and took charge of some of its affairs, and was relied upon by the institute. Now that the French Concession of Shanghai Health Experiment Institute has expanded its new buildings and added a vaccine department, Dr. Liu has been hired as the director of this department. Dr. Liu has returned to China by the Sicron Soso French mail ship, and will make a contribution to microbiology.

Zhu Wu Sets Up a Traditional Chinese Painting Studio in Shanghai

Mr. Zhu Wu, a famous painter from Shandong, courtesy name Fei Wu, alias Fei You, was skilled in painting at an early age. In his later years, his reputation became more and more prosperous. His landscapes initially followed Shigu, and later learned from Dong Ju, entering Yuan from Song, and has reached the realm of transformation, doing whatever he wants without losing the rules. He often said to his colleagues that it is biased to learn from people, things, and heart. He should take the image from nature, learn from the ancients, and use his heart. It is not easy to start after Mo Jie. His works are supernatural and consummate. Mr. Zhu has high character and appreciates himself. Free Talk

People, Works, and Criticism

— Qu Yi

Works are man-made. Therefore, every work, except for the stereotyped essays like official documents, is permeated with the author's personality. The deeper the author's personality is permeated in the work, the more the work touches people. At the same time, the greater the social nature of the author's personality, the higher the value of the work permeated by his personality. Therefore, I believe that a top-notch critic must be able to grasp the author's personality from his work. Reviewing a book is to review the person. There is no need to collect the author's irrelevant private life and add malicious attacks.

Of course, personality may have moments of division. Therefore, we can often see people with dual personalities in the world.

The elements that form a person's personality are probably what we call "words" and "deeds." But more precisely, they are "thought" and "behavior." With a certain thought, it is expressed in a certain behavior; that is where the person's knowledge and action are unified, and that is where the person's personality is unified. On the other hand, with a certain thought, but because of social obstacles, the person cannot and dares not express it in behavior; or even gives up on himself and goes with the flow, seeking only to survive. That is when knowledge and action cannot be unified, and the personality is split. That is what we call a person with a dual personality.

In other aspects, society also has its highest standards of specific morality and thought. In a specific society, it often requires the people living in this society to have its specific morality and thought. However, people who hold different kinds of morality and thought often do not blend with this specific society; but the pressure of that specific morality and thought is too great, so he has to express his submission in form. From the perspective of a specific society, this kind of person is undoubtedly a person with a split personality. At the same time, he has no ideals at all; living in this specific society, he takes its specific moral thought as his own moral thought. If this specific society changes, he will also change. From the perspective of this specific society, this kind of person is undoubtedly a person with a complete personality. In history, Cao Cao, who was judged as a traitor, still allows us to grasp the lovable side of his split personality when we read his short songs and other Yuefu poems. "The bright moon is like a mirror, when can it be picked? Sorrow comes from within, and cannot be cut off." It is always a very humane thing to say. Similarly, from the perspective of a specific feudal society, Chen Kongzhang, who fully expressed the complete personality of his loyal master, has had his檄豫州文 passed down and recited by thousands of people to this day because it embodies the highest standards of feudal morality and thought. But "Father Song begged for adoption, stealing Ding Si..., Cao was an ugly eunuch, and had no good virtue..." In our view, it is not enough to be Cao Cao's crime. Therefore, people with split personalities do not necessarily have good works; people with complete personalities do not necessarily have good works. But there is a limit to this, that is, people with split personalities are those who can realize the pain of their split in self-examination. In ancient times, there were probably many writers who produced their great works in this kind of pain.

Moreover, to go a step further, once a work has been typeset with lead type and appeared in front of the public; the work itself has existed as a social existence. This is not only the case for those works that permeate the author's personality, even stereotyped essays like official documents can be regarded as a "social existence." We readers can all find the social basis for its production through this work. Although this social basis of art can be mentioned very accurately and objectively in a complex and diverse society. The social basis for the development of Chinese essays now lies in the fact that the political unrest in society is deepening day by day, and it is more pleasant to express thoughts directly than to think about novels and engage in writing for this reason. If a critic can point out the social basis in his work, he has already given the author a fatal blow more deeply. There is no need to attack the author's private life any further.

I believe that a critic who can cause less unnecessary disputes and point out tendencies in the work itself to improve the literary world is the kind of critic that China needs at this stage. And I hope that such critics will appear!

Bai Pu's Golden Hairpin

— Zhao Jingshen

Yuan Sun Jichang's "Collection of Famous Yongqing Songs from Miscellaneous Dramas" has been carefully analyzed by Zheng Gong Ruihao. It contains 57 kinds of Yuan Dynasty Zaju, of which 55 kinds have been identified by me, and are detailed in my "Rhetoric Lectures" pages 111 to 115 (Beixin Edition). However, there are two kinds that have not been identified, namely "The golden hairpin is slanted in the temple" and "He is like the "Bamboo Forest Temple" with a shadow but no form."

In the Ming Dynasty, Shen Boying translated Wu Changling's words into "Collection of Famous Drama Names", which was published in the first volume of Tai She Xin Zou, pages 3 and 4 "Attached Drama Names", which listed the two drama names "Golden Hairpin" and "Bamboo Forest Temple"; it can be seen that these two names made by Sun Jichang are both Zaju. The source of "Bamboo Forest Temple" has not been identified by me, but "Golden Hairpin" has been resolved. Because today I accidentally flipped through the Beici Guangzhengpu, and unexpectedly found the arrangement of the "Golden Hairpin" set in the table of contents of Volume 3:

Dian Jiangchun Hun Jianglong Chuan Chuangyue

Jishengcao Yuanheling

Shangma Jiao Sha

Then I turned to the text and found two quwen of "Golden Hairpin". Page 29 (Beijing University edition) "Chuan Chuangyue" said:

"Remember the recklessness far away, how can you know that people are complaining about him? Singing and whipping drunk Qing Cong horse. Do not eat Qin Lou wine, thank the tea. Do not think about holding hands and parting."

The title is "Today's hairpin parting", which should be a mistake for "Golden Hairpin parting". Page 41 "Shangma Jiao Sha" said:

"Shangma Jiao has less joy, more troubles (pity), and the heart is chaotic like hemp. Accidentally walking to the east fence, Sha sighs and groans, cold Qing Qing and the moon face the yellow flowers."

Taihe Zhengyinpu Volume 2, page 6 (reprinted by Gushu Liutongchu) also contains "Chuan Chuangyue"; only "Yuan" is made "Zu", and the title is "Bai Renfu Santao". Taihe Zhengyinpu was published earlier than Beici Guangzhengpu, so it seems more reliable. But how could the Yuan Dynasty's Sun Jichang and the Ming Dynasty's Shen Boying both say it was a Zaju? It would be best to see the full text of the set. I then flipped through the scattered songs of Bai Pu compiled by Ren Ne (the three kinds of Yuan Dynasty scattered songs), and saw the full set of "Golden Hairpin Parting" compiled from "Yuefu Xinsheng", including the above-mentioned "Chuan Chuangyue" and "Shangma Jiao Sha":

(Xianlv Dian Jiangchun) Golden Hairpin Parting, Yujing people went to autumn Xiaosa. Coming late at leisure, needlework to tidy up. Leaning alone on the dangerous building, twelve beaded curtains hung. The wind Xiao is bleak, the rain is clear and the clouds are beginning, and the mountains are like paintings.

(Hun Jianglong) The place where the intestines are broken, the remnant sun in the sky, the sunset glow by the water. The withered lotus sleeps in shock, and the distant trees perch on crows. Fallen leaves are densely crowded with stone, and slender bamboos gently sweep the window screens. As dusk approaches, sorrow arises from the pestle, and resentment enters the pipa.

(Chuan Chuangyue) Remember the recklessness that is separated from the horizon, how can you know that people are complaining about him? Singing and whipping drunk Qing Cong horse. Do not eat Qin Lou wine, thank the tea, do not think about holding hands and parting?

(Jishengcao) Leaning on the railing for a long time, I went back to the embroidered curtain, and on the dangerous building I forcibly waved the golden lotus. The deep courtyard, the vermilion gate, stood on the green moss, and the cold penetrated the Lingbo socks. Counting the dates of return, I drew short Qiong hairpins in vain, and wiped away the tears and often wet the fragrant Luo handkerchief.

(Yuanheling) From the wild goose book, how many times did you make the turtle divination. Cui eyebrows are always locked with sorrow of parting, jade face is only haggard. Since the Lantern Festival, I have waited for the Chongyang Festival, why haven't I returned home?

(Shangma Jiao Sha) Less joy, more troubles, and the heart is chaotic like hemp. Accidentally walking to the east fence, sighing and groaning, cold Qing Qing and the moon face the yellow flowers.

The order of this set is completely the same as that of Beici Guangzhengpu; what Li Yu saw should be this set.

But according to my speculation, this set does not seem to be a Zaju, because:

1. Zaju uses Xianlv Dian Jiangchun, which usually follows Bazheng Ganzhou; but this set of Dian Jiangchun does not follow Bazheng Ganzhou.

2. The shortest set of Zaju using Dian Jiangchun is seven chapters, while this set is only six chapters.

3. The commonly used tunes in the Zaju Dian Jiangchun set include You Hulu, Tianxia Le, Nezha Ling, Qu Tazi, Jin Zaner, Houting Hua, Zui Zhongtian, Cunli Qiugu, Liuyao Xu, Qing Geer, Zhansha, Zhanshawei, and Weishi, none of which are in the "Golden Hairpin Parting" set.

4. Bai Pu's set is extremely coherent, just the old tune of boudoir grievances. It does not resemble the ever-changing plot of a drama.

With these four points as proof, I believe that Bai Pu's "Golden Hairpin Parting" is just the first sentence of the Xianlv Dian Jiangchun set, not a Zaju, which was mistaken by Sun Jichang as a Zaju and compiled into "Collection of Famous Zaju Names"; and Shen Boying, a later person, spread the error and also recognized the Golden Hairpin as a Zaju name.

Night at the Bailing Temple

— Yuan Chenying

In a yurt, serving as our temporary dining hall, our boys and girls all sat down. The fire in the stove blazed brightly. After two meals a day of stir-fried mutton, steamed buns, and white rice porridge, the smell of mutton still stung my nose, making me nauseous. These two meals were truly unappetizing; stir-fried mutton this, stir-fried mutton that... it all smelled of mutton. For someone as weak as me, it was truly a hardship. I don't know how the Mongols living in the desert manage to survive.

After the meal, the night began to envelop the Mongolian land. Candles were lit in the yurt, and the flickering light made the boys and girls inside fall silent. I, however, was worrying about sleeping at night; without being drowsy, how could I possibly fall asleep in the cold yurt!

Fortunately, at this time, four Mongolian musicians entered the yurt.

The yurt was instantly filled with more of our boys and girls. A group of lamas stood at the entrance, hanging the door curtain. In the wilderness, they were probably like us, rarely able to hear such tragic and magnificent Mongolian music.

The dim candlelight shone on the four young Mongolian musicians with ruddy faces. One was sucking on a flute, one was playing a four-stringed fiddle, one was playing an unknown ancient musical instrument, and the other was a young Mongolian man singing Mongolian songs.

The music began, at first long and slow. The sound was different from anything I had ever heard from any instrument. Gradually, the music became tighter, faster, and more urgent. In a daze, I seemed to hear the north wind outside the yurt harmonizing with the music, like a gust of wind, like a rainstorm. It made us, the boys and girls who had come from afar to this sparsely populated Mongolian land, all feel sad. But it wasn't entirely sadness; it was sadness mixed with heroism! I thought silently: if at this moment the Mongolian soldiers marched forward to the beat of this music, in the darkness of the night, what a magnificent and great scene it would be.

I was lost in wild thoughts. I didn't know where I was. Then the singing began, harmonizing with the unique flute sound, the four-stringed fiddle sound, and the ancient instrument sound. It seemed to be singing a farewell song, and also like singing a love song, but then it turned into an angry, heroic marching song. It made us sometimes sad, sometimes happy, and finally inspired, as if there were enemies ahead waiting for us to charge and kill...

As I was immersed in the atmosphere of music and song, a girl's voice, tinged with sadness, sounded softly in my ear. "What song is he singing?" I turned to look at the girl. Her eyes were moist. I looked again at the young singer. Struggle, despair, striving forward. A whole string of Mongolian songs I couldn't understand poured out of him. I shook my head; I didn't know either!

The singing and music stopped. The boys and girls applauded loudly. The four Mongolian musicians smiled, but soon became silent again. The young man who sang the Mongolian song sighed softly, and then, in the lamplight, silently walked out of the yurt together into the darkness.

Coming out of the yurt, the lamas had also dispersed. The night in the wilderness was a vast expanse. The sky was covered with dark clouds, and not a single star could be seen. The scattered yurts looked like round hills in the darkness. Most of the yurts had turned off their lights. Only a few yurts still leaked some dim light, and occasionally a flashlight shone, emitting a long beam of light, but it quickly went out.

I raised my head and looked around. I couldn't see what was ahead. The cold wind blowing from the north pierced my skin, which was covered by a woolen cloth gown (Note 1), like needles. The Mongolian land seemed to be completely dead. The Mongolian dogs barked, adding to my infinite loneliness.

I thought of the Japanese who came here to make a living during the day, and the post office director's complaints, the silent departure of the Mongolian musicians who had just played, and the young singer's soft sigh. I imagined the future of this Mongolian people and our fate, standing in the darkness for a long time. Suddenly, I remembered a friend saying that there might be wild animals coming out in this Mongolian place at night, so I staggered back to the yurt where I slept and quickly crawled into the quilt.

Note 1: A woolen cloth gown is made of woolen cloth and is unique to Suiyuan. The woolen cloth is woven from wool.

Farewell

— Ouyang Fanhai

Sending you back to your homeland,

How unbearable is your homeland to recall!

Tens of thousands of miles stained with the blood of the Jiao soldiers,

In the shell casing, may I ask the white bones,

Where is the loyal soul of my old friend?

Look at your body covered in dust,

Leaving only a desolate, thin frame!

You traveled alone overseas, and now return alone,

Where will you find the old friends who shared ten years of hardship?

Severe frost cannot tame your solitary pride,

Where is not a deserted island?

University Days (35)

— By German Storm, Translated by Chen Yinzhizhi

Then she went home. That night, and the next day, she sat and sewed until the valuable garment was completely finished.

"The next day was Sunday," the seamstress continued, after threading a line through the needle eye, "In the evening, when it was late, she inserted a few white May lilies into her black hair, and went to the dance hall.

"What follows, my nephew told me," he added, "He was also someone who wouldn't miss a chance to dance. – At first she sat for a long time, because the young artisans simply didn't dare approach her, and as for the university students, she rejected them one by one. It seemed like trouble was going to break out over her again. That pale-faced, noble university student, what do you call him?"—

"'Count Tu,'" I said. Translated by Chen Yinzhizhi

"Of course, he was also there. But he simply ignored her. Later, he had to come over, because she was dressed too beautifully that night; they said she looked like she was from the eastern Mediterranean coast. But when he walked up to her, her face turned red and her whole body trembled. But now she stood up and gave him her hand. My nephew said that he stared at her, as if he wanted to swallow her whole. She didn't dance with anyone else until the musicians packed up their violins, and then they both left the dance floor."

Lame Mary fell silent here; she only hummed twice, as if to give her story a conclusion. Then she continued her work more diligently than before.

I knew enough; so I decided to go to this "magician's gathering" tonight, in order to see with my own eyes how this story progressed.

In the suburban forest

It was already dark; as I searched for the mountain path in the bushes, the forest was filled with a depressing atmosphere.

I stepped onto the stone steps and couldn't help but stop. I saw several girls in white clothes walking back and forth through the woods, and then going into the house from the side. It seemed like it was time for a dance break; I heard the musicians tuning their violins inside the house, in the brightly lit hall. Students and girls were chatting lively as they passed through the open double doors. I couldn't help but want to go in right away. The little girl's lovely appearance appeared in my mind, and in my thoughts I saw her again hanging on her poor father's neck; I recalled how stubbornly she had rejected my innocent enthusiasm at that time. My heart suddenly felt a kind of pain, and I didn't know whether it was due to sympathy or jealousy?

Finally, I went up the two steps of the small portico and stood unnoticed next to the open door. The break was not over yet, but the inside was no less lively than during the dance. The students sat at tables along the wall or in side rooms, talking and clinking glasses; the girls walked around with smiling faces; and from time to time a dissolute shout echoed throughout the hall.

Among these girls were several lively and lovely faces, immature postures, and passionate, round eyes – emotions of carefree enjoyment or temporary annoyance further enhanced their charm. Although they were daughters of poor families, they were all dressed very cleanly, in uniformly light-colored, transparent clothes, with a flower or a fresh wreath inserted in their carefully woven hair.

But the male dance partners were not as neat and elegant as they were, especially those young students and a few so-called "leaders" of the club, who were simply not afraid to casually stretch their legs onto the tables or stools in front of their female dance partners.

I searched for Nali with my eyes, and soon found her. She was sitting across from the billiard room among several young girls: they were talking lively, but she was silent and looking straight ahead. She had a white rose in her hair, a rare flower in this season; but the rose season on her face had also passed: there was no blush left on her gentle, pale cheeks.

Education News

Children's Year Officially Opens Today, Implementing Children's Welfare, the National Government Issues a Special Notice on Two Matters: Implementing Free Education and Providing Relief to Children in Disaster Areas

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 31st) The first day of National Children's Year is the 1st. The National Government issued an explicit order on the evening of the 31st, instructing the entire country to earnestly implement matters related to children's welfare. The original order is as follows: Children are the foundation of national life. On the occasion of the beginning of Children's Year, matters related to children's welfare should be implemented according to laws and regulations. An examination of our country's matters regarding children's welfare reveals that school-age children should receive compulsory education, in-school children should receive excellent intellectual and physical training, pregnant women should receive new-method obstetrics, and infants and all children should have increased health and prevention of infectious diseases. Existing provisional laws and various educational regulations, health plans, and sports plans each have explicit provisions. The protection of children's right to life, the employment age and work hours of child laborers and apprentices, etc., have been detailed in special articles in the current criminal law and factory law. International conventions prohibiting the trafficking of women and children have also been signed by our country and various other nations. If they can be implemented, the benefits to children will be considerable. As for the improvement of children's clothing, food, housing, and transportation, the rescue of orphans and vagrants, the education of the disabled and mentally retarded, and the improvement of infant care institutions, either there are no laws and regulations to rely on, or although there are some provisions, there are still many omissions. Now, in order to enhance children's welfare and consolidate the foundation of national survival, where there are laws and regulations to rely on but the implementation is weak, all agencies should lead their subordinates, supervise the people of the country, and earnestly comply. Those that have not yet been stipulated or have omissions should be drafted by relevant agencies during the Children's Year and submitted for approval. Compulsory education is of great importance to children's welfare and wisdom and will be implemented starting this year. Currently, disasters are occurring frequently in various places, and the number of children displaced and in need of relief is undoubtedly not small. These two matters should be given special attention. The matter concerns children's welfare and the future of the nation. It is hereby ordered that the entire nation, from top to bottom, be informed and diligently comply. This order.

The National Children's Year Implementation Committee Held a Meeting Yesterday

(Nanjing, 31st) The National Children's Year Implementation Committee held a meeting at the Ministry of Education at 9:00 am on the 31st. More than ten people, including Pan Gongzhan, attended. Gu Shusen chaired the meeting. The following resolutions were made: 1. A draft of the Parents' Creed was proposed, and Gao Junshan and others were recommended to organize and review it. 2. The Minister of Education was requested to read the National Government's order on matters concerning children's welfare to be implemented during Children's Year at the opening ceremony. 3. The local Children's Year Implementation Committees were requested to subsidize the expenses of children's tour groups in various places. Separately, the committee will formulate principles for preferential treatment for children riding boats and trains and request the Ministries of Railways and Communications to formulate measures. 4. Artists will be invited to draw children's logos, which will be explained to the public at the opening ceremony. 5. Methods for various children's activities during Children's Year will be formulated, and a national children's painting exhibition will be held after the groups review them. 6. After a detailed plan is drafted, it will be submitted to the general meeting for discussion. 7. The national campaign to rescue homeless children will be combined with the previously drafted plan for discussion. 8. The Linzhuang Autonomous School should request funding from the local Children's Year Implementation Committee. 9. The three internal departments of the Ministry of Education will be requested to send additional staff to handle committee affairs. 10. Children's savings have been included in the children's activities and will not be discussed separately.

Capital Inauguration Ceremony

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 31st) The inauguration ceremony for National Children's Year in the capital will be held at the New Capital Theater at 8:00 AM on the 1st, which is the opening day of National Children's Year. At 7:00 AM, representatives from various schools will first pay their respects at the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum, then proceed to visit the heads of various central government agencies, and then return to participate in the opening ceremony. After the ceremony is presided over by Gu Shusen, Chairman of the Standing Committee of the National Children's Year Implementation Committee, Director Wang will read the order issued by the National Government regarding the earnest implementation of children's welfare matters during Children's Year. Next, the chairman will deliver an opening speech, and Vice President Kong will also deliver a speech. Following that, a children's representative will give a response, after which educational films for children will be screened and recreational performances will be held to add to the excitement. After the ceremony concludes, various child welfare organizations will be inspected in the afternoon, and Kong Xiangxi and Ye Chucang will give radio speeches in the evening.

Preparations

Xue Tianhan, Secretary-General of the Congress, wrote about the preparations for the National Children's Year as follows:

Formulation of the Outline of Implementation Measures for Children's Year

In October of the 23rd year of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Education drafted an outline of implementation measures for Children's Year and consulted the Ministry of Interior for approval.

In February of the 24th year, the Ministry of Education approved the Ministry of Interior's revised opinions on the outline of implementation measures for National Children's Year. After several consultations between the two ministries, the outline of measures was revised and jointly presented to the Executive Yuan. After receiving the joint presentation from the two ministries, the Executive Yuan convened the heads of the three ministries of Interior, Education, and Industry for detailed review, and also sent letters to the Central Propaganda Committee and the Mass Movement Guidance Committee to send personnel to participate in the discussion.

On March 8th, the two ministries of Interior and Education received instructions from the Executive Yuan: "The outline of implementation measures for National Children's Year presented by the two ministries of Interior and Education has been submitted to the 202nd meeting of the Yuan. It was decided that "the duration of Children's Year shall be from August 1, 1935, to July 31 of the following year, and the rest shall be passed according to the review opinions." The two ministries should promptly draft implementation procedures and submit them to the Yuan for approval."

After receiving the instructions from the Executive Yuan, the two ministries of Interior and Education immediately convened the heads of the three ministries of Interior, Education, and Industry to hold two preparatory meetings on March 16th and 19th to formulate implementation procedures for Children's Year and to pass the organizational regulations and budget estimates of the National Children's Year Implementation Committee.

On March 30th, the two ministries of Interior and Education jointly presented the revised outline of implementation measures for Children's Year and the organizational regulations of the committee to the Executive Yuan for record.

On April 12th, the two ministries of Interior and Education received instructions from the Executive Yuan: "The outline of implementation measures for Children's Year and the organizational regulations of the National Children's Year Implementation Committee have been submitted to the 206th meeting of the Yuan and resolved to be amended and passed. In addition to ordering the provincial and municipal governments to strictly abide by the outline of measures and to publicize the organizational regulations by the Yuan for notification and distribution, the ministry should comply."

The outline of implementation measures for Children's Year, from the drafting of the draft to its promulgation, took a total of seven months. The original draft stipulated that the implementation period would be from April 4, 1935—Children's Day—to April 3 of the following year. Later, due to the limited time and insufficient preparations, the Executive Yuan decided to revise it to be from August 1, 1935, to July 31 of the following year, which is in line with the academic year. In terms of organization, the original draft stipulated that "the implementation of Children's Year shall be jointly led by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education, together with the Ministry of Industry, to organize the National Children's Year Implementation Committee." The Executive Yuan revised it to "the implementation of Children's Year shall be jointly led by the Ministry of Education, the Ministry of Interior, and the Ministry of Industry, together with the China Child Welfare Association." There are no other major differences.

II. Establishment of the National Children's Year Implementation Committee

After the two ministries of Interior and Education received the instructions from the Executive Yuan approving the outline of implementation measures for Children's Year and the organizational regulations of the committee, they immediately followed the provisions of the regulations to start organizing the National Children's Year Implementation Committee, and drafted the committee's budget estimates - totaling 42,860 yuan - and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for review.

On April 26th, the two ministries of Interior and Education received instructions from the Executive Yuan: "The budget estimates for Children's Year have been submitted to the 209th meeting of the Yuan and resolved to be passed."

The budget estimates for the committee have been approved by the Executive Yuan, and the members and staff designated by the three ministries of Interior, Education, and Industry and the members proposed by the China Child Welfare Association have also been decided one after another. On May 14th, the committee announced its 21 members, one secretary-general, and five staff members. The members were appointed by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education, with five each, two appointed by the Ministry of Industry, three recommended by the China Child Welfare Association, and six appointed. The secretary-general and five staff members were jointly appointed by the two ministries of Interior, Education, and Industry, with two each from the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education, and one from the Ministry of Industry.

On May 15th, the two ministries of Interior and Education decided to appoint Gu Shusen, Wu Yanzhou, and Lu Xirong as standing members of the National Children's Year Implementation Committee. The staff meeting started working on May 30th, with Secretary-General Xue Tianhan responsible for presiding over it.

III. Meeting Process and Important Work of the National Children's Year Implementation Committee

(1) The Standing Committee held two meetings on June 6th and June 23rd. Its main tasks were to manage the work of the staff meeting, discuss the work plan, and formulate various measures and outlines to be drafted by the congress.

(2) The plenary session of the members held four meetings on May 20th, June 8th and 9th, July 5th and 6th, and July 31st. For the convenience of handling affairs, the committee was divided into four groups in accordance with the provisions of the committee's organizational regulations: the first group was responsible for children's education matters, the second group was responsible for children's health matters, the third group was responsible for children's protection and relief matters, and the fourth group was responsible for the organization of children's welfare groups. At each meeting, the important work that has been handled by the committee was carried out on time in accordance with the matters stipulated in the implementation procedures, as follows: (1) compiling Children's Year slogans and slogans, (2) compiling Children's Year songs, (3) formulating plans for compiling and printing publicity pamphlets, outlines of various activity measures for parents' associations, (4) formulating methods for newspapers and magazines to publish special issues or weeklys, Children's Year opening ceremonies, National Children's Book Exhibitions, National Teaching Aids and Toy Exhibitions, National Children's Health Exhibitions, etc., (5) holding the Capital Summer Children's Health Camp.

(3) The staff meeting is held once a week, on Tuesday mornings. Since its establishment, the committee has held six meetings. Its main tasks are to handle daily official documents, handle matters assigned by the Standing Committee and the Members' Congress. The committee is responsible for the general affairs of the opening ceremony in the capital, so the work has been extremely intense in the past two or three weeks.

(4) Organizational Situation of the Children's Year Implementation Committees in Various Provinces and Cities

Anhui Province: The committee was established on May 16th with seven members, served by the heads of the secretariat sections of various departments, one secretary-general, and five staff members, separately designated by various departments.

Henan Province: The committee was established on June 15th with seven members, separately appointed from the heads of the secretariat sections of various departments, editors, and personnel from relevant children's affairs organizations. One secretary-general was served by an official from the Department of Education.

Shandong Province: Established on June 14th. The committee has eleven members. The organizational regulations and the list of members have not yet been reported.

Chahar Province: The committee was established on May 30th with a total of five members, served by important officials from various departments and representatives from organizations related to children's affairs. The organizational regulations and implementation procedures have been formulated.

The organization of the committee includes two standing members, one secretary-general, five staff members, five members of the general affairs group, five members of the education group, five members of the social group, and five members of the health group.

Tianjin City: The organizational regulations of the committee have been formulated. The date of establishment and the list of personnel have not yet been reported.

Nanjing City: The organizational outline of the committee has been formulated. The date of establishment and the list of personnel have not yet been reported.

Shanghai City: The committee was established on June 21st. The organizational regulations have been formulated, but the list of members has not been reported.

Children's Year and Children's Welfare: Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education, Representing Ma Zongrong, Gave a Speech at the Central Broadcasting Station Last Night

Last night, on the eve of the opening of Children's Year, Ma Zongrong, a Senior Secretary of the Ministry of Education, representing Minister Wang Shijie, gave a speech at the Central Broadcasting Station entitled "Children's Year and Children's Welfare." The speech is as follows:

Ladies and gentlemen, the government has already declared that from August 1, 1935, to July 31, 1936, is the Children's Year of the Republic of China. Tomorrow is the day of the national Children's Year opening ceremony. This is a matter worth blessing for the children of our country and celebrating for our Chinese nation. Therefore, today, I would like to raise this issue—Children's Year and Children's Welfare—and discuss it with you.

What is called Children's Year? Simply put, it means striving for children's welfare movements during this year so that children's lives will be happier day by day in the future. This kind of movement is not a new invention unique to China. The United States government held a large-scale child protection movement in 1918. Around 1923, Japan also held a child protection movement. Other countries have also had similar movements.

Why do we want to hold a Children's Year? There are many reasons. Now, I will list four reasons for you.

(1) From the perspective of the inherent human desire, we want to hold a Children's Year. Because all living things have two desires: self-preservation and species preservation. The so-called desire for self-preservation means the desire for a long life. The so-called desire for species preservation means the desire for prosperous descendants. With these two desires, living things can continue to exist and develop infinitely. Both of these desires are important, but from a biological point of view, species preservation is more important than self-preservation. Since humans are one of the living things, they should engage in activities for species preservation. This is one of the reasons we hold a Children's Year.

(2) From the perspective of human ideals, we want to hold a Children's Year. Because humans are animals with ideals. The so-called ideal is the completion of the highest culture that humans can achieve. Human society should reach this ideal and always work hard. In order to achieve this goal, in addition to the hard work of the current people, we also need successors to inherit and strive. That is to say, we need excellent successors—children. This is the second reason why we want to hold a Children's Year.

(3) From the perspective of consolidating the foundation of the nation and society, we want to hold a Children's Year. Because the strength or weakness of the people is closely related to the rise and fall of their country. And the strength or weakness of the people is directly proportional to the health of the children. Therefore, when the United States held a large-scale child protection movement in 1918, its slogan was "Healthy children are the foundation of a great nation." Around 1923, when Japan held a child protection movement, its slogan was "The foundation of a healthy nation begins with children." Therefore, to establish a solid foundation for a healthy country, we must first seek the health of the children, who are its successors. This is the third reason why our country wants to hold a Children's Year.

In addition to the above three reasons, there is one more point to be explained. It is true that all parents in the world love their children. Therefore, some people think that the love of fathers and mothers does not need to be promoted with great fanfare. However, parents in the past mostly held the view that children are their private property. The idea of ​​raising children for the sake of the country and society is relatively lacking, and they cannot fully fulfill their duty of upbringing. Only recently have children enjoyed the right to be raised as members of the nation and society. If the family cannot fully fulfill its duty of upbringing, the nation and society should come forward and raise them personally. However, one thing that must be noted is that although the education of children is originally the primary responsibility of the nation and society, it is most natural and appropriate for families to raise children. Therefore, it cannot be said that the education of children must be directly provided by the nation and society. Only when the family cannot fully fulfill the care of children, or when the children do not have a suitable family, does the nation and society bear the task of educating them. Therefore, the meaning of our holding a Children's Year is, first, to strive to publicize the necessity and methods of child care, in order to deepen the awareness of child care among the people of the country, have a correct understanding, and know the way of upbringing. Second, we want to encourage families, society, and the nation to cooperate and engage in the construction of children's welfare undertakings. This is the fourth reason why we hold a Children's Year. The significance of the government's decision to designate the 24th year of the Republic of China as Children's Year lies in this.

In my previous speech, I used the term "children's welfare undertakings." What is meant by children's welfare undertakings? It can be broadly divided into two categories. First, striving for "the popularization of compulsory education for children." Second, striving to "promote children's protection undertakings."

First, let's talk about the issue of "the popularization of compulsory education for children." Eliminating illiteracy in China is a crucial task. However, to eliminate illiteracy, on the one hand, we must provide adult literacy education to adults who lost their schooling in childhood. On the other hand, we must ensure that all children receive compulsory education. And children's compulsory education is even more important than adult literacy education. Because the number of adults who lost their schooling in childhood is indeed large, but if the number of illiterate children no longer increases, then their number will naturally be limited. As for children, they are born continuously. If the compulsory education of children cannot be popularized, then the source of illiteracy cannot be cut off, hindering the cultural development of the nation and society, which is naturally very large. And the children themselves, because they are illiterate, suffer a lot of pain in their lives.

Therefore, the Executive Yuan's 214th meeting on May 28th of this year has revised and approved the Outline of Measures for the Implementation of Compulsory Education, which will be implemented starting from the 24th year of the Republic of China. The purpose is to gradually train school-age children across the country through one-year or two-year short-term primary schools, etc., to achieve compulsory education in four-year elementary schools. The implementation process is divided into three phases. The first phase is five years from August 1935 to July 1940. During this period, in addition to expanding four-year elementary schools, existing elementary schools will be converted into two-part systems, existing classes will expand enrollment, existing private schools will be reorganized and improved. Provinces and cities should also run one-year short-term primary schools so that all older out-of-school children and school-age children who have not yet entered school should receive at least one year of compulsory education. Funding has been strictly ordered to be prepared locally, and the central government may provide appropriate subsidies. It has been decided that a subsidy of 240,000 yuan will be allocated in the 24th year of the Republic of China. The training of teachers and the preparation of school buildings are also stipulated in corresponding plans, striving to popularize one-year compulsory education in all provinces and cities by the end of the 28th year of the Republic of China, and for the number of children receiving one-year compulsory education to reach 80% of the number of school-age children. If our ideals can be gradually realized, the benefits to children, society, and the country will be great. At the start of this Children's Year, I would like to plead for the children of the country, hoping that our elders, brothers, sisters, aunts, and uncles will directly and indirectly assist the government in completing the first phase of the compulsory education plan, widely establish one-year short-term primary schools, provide tuition-free education, provide books and school supplies, and continue to work hard to expand four-year elementary schools, so that children across the country have the opportunity to receive education, and illiteracy is eradicated, which will greatly benefit children, society, and the nation.

Next, let's talk about "children's protection undertakings." Children's protection undertakings include many things, which can be roughly divided into six types: (1) Maternal protection undertakings, (2) Infant and toddler protection undertakings, (3) Child labor protection undertakings, (4) Rescue undertakings for unfortunate children, (5) Nursing undertakings for weak children, and (6) Reform undertakings for delinquent children.

Maternal protection is to protect pregnant women and maternity women. Because the safe birth of the fetus is not only what parents hope for, but also what the entire society hopes for. Therefore, society should naturally fulfill the obligation to protect children's lives. However, according to statistics, there are often obstacles when children are born. The reason for this is that maternal protection undertakings have not been fully considered, and maternal education has not been thorough enough. Therefore, maternal protection is an indispensable part of children's protection undertakings.

Secondly, although infants and toddlers have been safely born, if they cannot grow up healthily, such as death or physical weakness, creating weak citizens, it is not only a loss for the parents of infants and toddlers. Therefore, infants and toddlers need to be fully protected.

Next, let's talk about the protection of working children. The so-called protection of child labor means not allowing children to engage in inappropriate labor. Whether it is engaging in their own family business or helping others with work, any labor that hinders the physical and mental development of children is prohibited.

Let's talk about the rescue of unfortunate children. The so-called unfortunate children, such as abused children, orphans, abandoned children, etc., have very poor environments. If they are ignored, it is not only intolerable from a humanitarian point of view, but also hinders the development of society. Therefore, the rescue of unfortunate children is a noteworthy children's protection undertaking.

Let's talk about the nursing of weak children. The so-called weak children are children with anemia, weak hearts, weak lungs, etc. Because of their physical weakness, these children cannot keep pace with ordinary children in all activities, and may even be in danger of dying young. Therefore, targeting these children and providing them with special care to restore their health and join ordinary children is also a necessary children's protection undertaking.

Finally, let's talk about the reform of delinquent children. Because the crime rate of children has been increasing in recent years. This is a common fact in all countries. Although punishment is imposed, the effect of reforming and doing good is very small. Therefore, for these children, it is better to protect them and actively reform and educate them, so that they know that crime is shameful, and cultivate their willpower to overcome bad temptations, in order to complete the ideal of educating everyone regardless of their background and making the best use of everything.

Other things such as the education of children with physical or mental abnormalities, such as blind children, deaf-mute children, disabled children, mentally retarded children, and idiotic children, can also be regarded as children's protection undertakings in a broad sense.

Based on the meaning of Children's Year mentioned above, after the opening of Children's Year, we must gradually work hard on the following practical facilities to promote children's welfare:

(1) Implement parental education to publicize the idea of ​​caring for children and to make their protection methods scientific.

(2) Popularize compulsory education for children so that children can have equal opportunities for education and welfare.

(3) Widely establish mother consultation centers, maternity hospitals, infant homes, milk supply stations, nurseries, children's health consultation centers, etc., to protect infants and toddlers.

(4) Formulate child labor laws, strive to protect the health of working children, widely implement apprenticeship education, and widely establish vocational guidance centers to protect child labor.

(5) Widely issue children's abuse prevention orders and establish orphanages for the blind, and formulate children's abuse laws to rescue unfortunate children.

(6) Widely establish summer health camps, forest schools, and seaside schools to care for weak children.

(7) Establish reformatories and formulate juvenile protection laws to protect delinquent children.

(8) Widely establish schools for the blind and deaf, schools for the disabled, etc., to protect children with abnormalities.

If the above-mentioned facilities can be gradually realized, children across China will enjoy boundless blessings. I would like to bless all the children in the country on the eve of the opening of the National Children's Year.

Little Men (1)

— Original by Ms. Alcott of the United States, translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)
