Voice of the Telegraph Industry

Respectfully Informing Agencies Handling Disaster Relief Telegrams

— Zhen

For the past two weeks, the weather in the Yangtze River basin has cleared up, and the water levels in various ports have decreased. The disaster-stricken areas can begin to provide relief, and the flood control areas have passed the critical period. Although the countryside has been destroyed, the cities have been preserved. Although it can be said that the will of heaven can be turned, it is ultimately due to human efforts. However, given the wide scope of the disaster, affecting almost both sides of the Yangtze River, and the large number of people affected, no less than hundreds of thousands of households, with wailing sounds spreading across the fields, and urgent relief needed! Therefore, the future policy should focus on relief in the short term and dredging in the long term, and the country relies on telecommunications to transmit the news of this policy.

In order to support disaster relief, the Ministry of Transportation has stipulated a type of disaster relief telegram that is transmitted free of charge. The definition of this telegram is summarized in the Disaster Relief Telegram Regulations, which applies to temporary or special urgent relief efforts handled by the National Government or Chinese and foreign relief organizations approved by the governments of various provinces. It does not apply to ordinary relief efforts of a permanent nature or telegrams sent by local charities and private relief organizations.

Relief agencies that wish to send this type of telegram must pay attention to the following points: (A) When applying for a license, they should first submit the following information to the Ministry of Transportation: (1) the name and address of the relief organization, (2) the name and occupation of the representative, (3) the agency that approved the establishment and the date of establishment, (4) the disaster-stricken location and its area, (5) the situation of the disaster area, (6) the purpose and method of the relief effort, (7) the estimated duration of the relief effort, (8) the place name of where the telegrams will be sent from, (9) the number of licenses requested. After being approved by the Ministry of Transportation, the license can be issued. (B) The effective period of the license is determined by the Ministry of Transportation and is limited to three or six months from the date of approval. If an extension is necessary due to the severity of the disaster, an application should be submitted to the Ministry of Transportation for approval to issue another license. However, this extension shall not exceed six months. If the relief effort has been completed, regardless of whether the license has expired, it should be immediately reported to the Ministry for cancellation. (C) The text of the disaster relief telegram is limited to the following urgent matters and must not be mixed with other matters: (1) matters concerning reporting the critical situation in the disaster area, (2) matters relating to the procurement of urgent relief supplies and their transportation, (3) matters concerning fundraising and urging the allocation of relief funds, (4) other urgent matters related to relief. The telegram should also be as concise as possible, limited to Chinese or English clear text. Each Chinese telegram must not exceed one hundred characters, and each English telegram must not exceed fifty characters.

The above is a general outline of the Disaster Relief Telegram Regulations. It is noted that disaster relief telegrams in other countries are not transmitted free of charge and are treated the same as ordinary commercial telegrams. Therefore, there are no restrictions on the provisions of disaster relief telegrams. Natural disasters are prevalent in our country, and relief is needed every year. Therefore, the Disaster Relief Telegram Regulations are promulgated for compliance. The purpose is to prevent agencies sending this type of telegram from abusing it, thus improving the efficiency of transmission, and to prevent the lines transmitting this type of telegram from becoming congested, thus increasing the difficulty of telegram service. It is hoped that relief agencies will strictly adhere to the scope and that all telegraph offices will be willing to receive and will never refuse to send disaster relief telegrams. If they disregard everything and send them indiscriminately, exceeding the capacity of the lines of each office, making it impossible to transmit them, it may be difficult to maintain the implementation of these regulations.

Telecommunications and Transportation Amidst the Flood Disaster

— Qinghua

In the past two months, floods have occurred in the Yangtze River and Yellow River basins, and low-lying counties and cities have been turned into wetlands. The severity of the damage can be described as unprecedented. The sacrifice of people's lives and property is in the millions, which is truly a great misfortune for the Chinese nation!

Among the state-owned enterprises, the most affected by the flood disaster are telecommunications and transportation. The telecommunications and transportation equipment in inland provinces in our country mostly use land lines, followed by wireless communications. The telegraph offices in the disaster-stricken counties and cities along the Yangtze River and Yellow River were either washed away, or the poles and lines were broken, or the poles were submerged in water, causing severe leakage and preventing the transmission of telegrams, which greatly threatened domestic telecommunications and transportation. Fortunately, the transportation authorities made every effort to maintain and properly manage the situation, and communication and transportation in various places were maintained without interruption, or were restored shortly after being interrupted. The process is described as follows:

The Ministry of Transportation has four approaches to deal with telegraph poles and lines washed away by floods: (1) dispatching workers for emergency repairs. Whenever telegraph poles are broken due to strong winds, rain, or water flow, a large number of linemen are dispatched to risk their lives for emergency repairs. Even in flooded areas, they must find ways to support the poles in order to restore communication; (2) constructing temporary lines to bypass and reconnect the communication to maintain communications. For example, the water level in the vicinity of Hanyang and Shashi in Hubei Province is very high, and almost all of the original poles and lines are submerged in water, making repairs impossible for the time being. However, the telecommunications and transportation between Sichuan and Hubei are extremely important, so they had to find ways to bypass the disaster-stricken area and construct temporary telegraph lines in order to reconnect the original lines and restore communication; (3) scheduling lines to maintain communication. For example, the direct lines between Shanghai and Hankou and between Beijing and Hankou were interrupted by water several times, so they found ways to use the lines from Nanjing, Xuzhou, and Zhengzhou to Hankou to maintain communication between Shanghai and Hankou and between Beijing and Hankou without stopping work due to the interruption of the original lines. This is the most economical and effective method; (4) increasing wireless telegraph machines and working hours. For example, the Shanghai-Hankou line was once interrupted because the lines between Zhengzhou and Hankou were washed away by water at the same time, so there was no way to travel by wire. Therefore, they had to increase the number of wireless machines, with Shanghai and Hankou working day and night on dual machines to avoid the backlog of telegrams. In other places where wired telecommunications could not be maintained due to the floods, the daily working hours were also increased to clear telegrams. In addition, the land line between Hankou and Chongqing was interrupted between Shashi and Yichang, and there was no hope of repair for the time being. In addition to the Hankou-Chongqing dual-machine wireless communication, the Nanjing and Wanxian radio stations were also ordered to communicate day and night, and a portion of the telegrams between the downstream of the Yangtze River and Sichuan Province was transmitted via the Beijing-Wanxian route. The land line was still used to the west of Wanxian (because the dual machines of the Hankou-Chongqing wireless line could not handle the huge amount of telegrams). In this way, the telegrams from Nanjing to Chongqing could still be transmitted via two routes, one via the Beijing-Hankou and Hankou-Chongqing wireless lines, and the other via the Beijing-Wanxian wireless line and the Wanxian-Chongqing land line, so that the telegram service would not be severely delayed.

The significance of the Ministry of Transportation's efforts to maintain telecommunications and transportation in the disaster area is very significant. Those who benefit from it are not only the convenience of flood control and disaster relief communications, but also the telegrams of merchants who have stopped purchasing and transporting goods due to the flood disaster, as well as the communications of condolences and reporting disaster situations, which can be transmitted quickly, so they do not suffer from the inability to communicate. Moreover, the military suppression of bandits in Sichuan Province has been tense recently, and the communication between the central government and the military authorities is extremely important. In the midst of this flood disaster, the ability to maintain telecommunications and transportation, so as not to hinder the progress of the military suppression of bandits, is even more gratifying.

Talking About "Special Delivery Telegrams"

— Zhongming

...Please pay attention to the sender and receiver...

If the place where the sender sends the telegram, although there is a telegraph office or radio station, is far away from the location of the receiver, then this telegram must be delivered to the receiver by a special messenger hired by the receiving office. This type of telegram is a special delivery telegram. This telegram is marked with the fee identification of "Special Delivery" or "Express". When delivering the telegram, the receiving office must collect the special delivery fee from the receiver in accordance with the special delivery charter established by the Ministry of Transportation. If the sender is willing to pay the special delivery fee for the receiver in advance, they can use "(Special Payment...or XP...)" as the fee identification, and the dotted lines in the parentheses represent the silver dollars for domestic telegrams or the francs for international telegrams. As for the small amount of special delivery fee collected, the regulations are as follows:

No special delivery fee is charged if the receiver's address and the telegraph office or radio station (hereinafter referred to as the office) are within the same city. No special delivery fee is charged if they are not in the same city but are within five li from the office. From five li to ten li, the fee is 15 cents. From ten li to fifty li, the fee is increased by 15 cents for every ten li. Beyond fifty li, the fee is increased by 20 cents for every ten li. For example, for sixty li, the fee should be 95 cents, and so on. Beyond ten li, the remainder less than ten li is also calculated as ten li. The above regulations for collecting special delivery fees are intended to provide a basis for the office and to make it easier for the receiver to check. As for the reason why the office wants to collect a special delivery fee from the receiver for delivering a special delivery telegram, it is very simple, because the number of messengers hired by the office is fixed, and their main task is to deliver general telegrams. If this type of special delivery telegram is also delivered by the office messenger, it will inevitably delay other telegrams due to the long distance and time-consuming round trip. Also, if the office bears this special delivery fee, it is very unreasonable because the telegram fee is often smaller than the special delivery fee, and the office will have to pay a lot of compensation. Therefore, the special delivery fee for special delivery telegrams must be paid by the receiver or sender, as stipulated in the international telegram business regulations.

As for the convenience that the office can provide to the public on special delivery telegrams, it is to regulate the special delivery fee, prevent the messenger from demanding extra money, and thus increase the burden on the receiver. It is also stipulated that all special delivery telegrams delivered to the same receiver at the same time will be charged as one delivery, regardless of the number of telegrams. The Ministry of Transportation has seen this and specially made a special delivery envelope and a special delivery fee receipt, and all offices must use this special envelope when delivering special delivery telegrams, and must fill in the special delivery fee amount in the special delivery fee receipt and hand it over to the special messenger to deliver to the receiver as proof. If this envelope and receipt are used up or have not been sent, the ordinary envelope can be used for delivery, but the office must issue a formal special delivery fee receipt separately to collect the special delivery fee from the receiver to show caution.

Finally, we sincerely hope that the receiver will pay attention to the following four points when receiving a special delivery telegram and paying the special delivery fee:

(1) Be sure to ask the special messenger for a special delivery fee receipt before paying the special delivery fee;

(2) Whether there is (XP...) in the telegram bottom;

(3) Whether the special delivery fee receipt issued is consistent with the stipulated amount and distance;

(4) Whether the special delivery fee receipt is stamped with the office seal and signed or stamped by the handler.

If the receiver has any questions about this receipt, they can send a detailed account of the matter, along with the receipt, directly to the Telegraph Administration Department of the Ministry of Transportation in Nanjing for verification. The Telegraph Administration Department will definitely verify and handle it strictly and give a satisfactory reply upon receiving this letter of request.

The Significance of the Ministry of Transportation's Crackdown on Privately Established Radio Stations

— Hua

Recently, major daily newspapers have often carried advertisements from the "Ministry of Transportation offering rewards for reporting privately established radio stations," which has caught our eye. What is the nature of privately established radio stations? What is the reason for the crackdown? The general reader does not seem to have paid close attention to this or have a correct understanding of it. The reporter is not talented and would like to use the pages of this publication to elaborate on it.

Telecommunications and transportation are the lifeline of a country, and without unified management, it is difficult to achieve the effectiveness of using arms and fingers. Therefore, the telecommunications regulations promulgated by the National Government stipulate that the telecommunications equipment established by public and private organizations or individuals must be approved by the Ministry of Transportation or its entrusted agency. And when necessary, personnel may be sent to inspect the telecommunications or the equipment may be purchased at a price. If this is not the case, it is inevitable that unscrupulous people will use telecommunications equipment as a tool for plotting wrongdoing, causing great hidden dangers to the country and society. In order to comply with national laws and maintain public security, the Ministry of Transportation must strictly crack down on illegal privately established radio stations to maintain the integrity of telecommunications management. This is one reason.

The transmission of wireless telecommunications relies on the oscillation of radio waves. The receiving and transmitting sides must have harmonious oscillation frequencies in order to receive clearly. Therefore, the frequencies of each station must be different in order to avoid interference, otherwise, the noise will be chaotic and it will be impossible to work. Therefore, maintaining spatial order is a necessary condition for wireless telecommunications. Recently, the Ministry of Transportation stopped issuing licenses for the establishment of stations because there were too many private broadcasting stations in this city and all frequencies had been distributed, which is one example. Those privately established radio stations that only know how to operate for personal gain and disregard the public interest are not subject to the supervision of the Ministry of Transportation, and the frequencies they transmit cannot be regulated, and spatial interference will inevitably become more serious. In order to maintain the efficiency of wireless communications, the Ministry of Transportation must severely punish privately established radio stations that disregard the overall situation. This goes without saying. This is the second reason.

In addition to plotting wrongdoing, which is punished by law, most privately established radio stations communicate privately to solicit commercial reports and eavesdrop on public radio stations' telegrams for profit. This type of illegal behavior not only causes losses to the telegraph office, but also poses a serious threat to the financial and news circles. According to the criminal law, "electricity is considered a property," and these privately established radio stations constitute the crime of theft and occupation. In the case of the privately established radio station of the Tianjin Yongli Yongzeng Joint Silver Company last year, the Tianjin Procuratorate filed a public prosecution for theft. All relevant parties should jointly report them and make sure that the unscrupulous people are completely eliminated. This is not only a matter of the Ministry of Transportation's crackdown. This is the third reason.

We have observed that in all advanced countries in the world, regardless of their political system, the laws and policies promulgated by the government must be implemented without obstruction with the sincere cooperation of the people. Therefore, the government can exercise its powers and seek welfare for the people. The crimes of privately established radio stations, such as operating for personal gain, theft, and illegality, have been described above. We believe that the people of the country will definitely support the Ministry of Transportation's crackdown policy, jointly seek ways to implement sanctions, and the people's interest and efforts in serving the public will also be reflected in this.

Provisional Measures for Domestic Chinese Cipher News Telegrams

— Chu Hao

——Effective Today, Please Note, News Media——

In recent months, news organizations or their reporters in various locations, transmitting news telegrams via wireless circuits, have frequently experienced eavesdropping and publication by other newspapers, resulting in significant losses of rights. They have appealed to the transportation authorities to take measures to stop this. The Ministry of Communications, upon request, immediately issued orders to all bureaus and stations to pay close attention. If any local news organization is found to be copying and publishing news, it should be dealt with according to the law. Furthermore, it has been stipulated that wherever wired circuits are available, news telegrams should be transmitted via wired circuits as much as possible. A provisional measure for domestic cipher news telegrams has also been promulgated, allowing for transmission in cipher, making it impossible for others to understand the text. In addition, plans are underway to select important wireless circuits and convert them to high-speed automatic wireless transmitting and receiving machines, greatly increasing the speed of transmitting and receiving electrical signals, making it virtually impossible for outsiders to eavesdrop. (It is noted that international radio stations all use high-speed automatic transmitting and receiving equipment, which is extremely secure and reliable.) The aforementioned cipher news telegram measure is scheduled to take effect today. Excerpts of its main content are listed below for the reference of the news media:

(1) Cipher news telegrams are limited to those transmitted via domestic wireless circuits of the telegraph bureaus in Peiping, Nanking, Shanghai, Hankow, Changsha, Tientsin, Tsinan, Nanchang, Foochow, Canton, Amoy, Tsingtao, Chefoo, Chengdu, Ba County, Kweiyang, Kunming, Chang'an, Kalgan, and Lanzhou. Except as specifically stipulated in these measures, all other matters shall be handled in accordance with the regulations for ordering news telegrams.

(2) Any news agency, periodical publisher, news management office, or its reporter (hereinafter referred to as news organization or its reporter) wishing to send cipher news telegrams shall, in accordance with Article 2 of the News Telegram Regulations, fill out an application form, together with a copy of the cipher codebook, and submit it through the receiving news organization to the local telegraph bureau for forwarding to the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Communications for approval. Once approved and a certificate issued, the news organization shall prepare another identical copy of the cipher codebook and send or deliver one copy each to the receiving and transmitting telegraph bureaus for record before being allowed to send such telegrams. If the cipher codebook is used for a long time or there are other reasons for replacement, the original news organization or its reporter shall prepare an identical copy of the cipher codebook and send or deliver it to the receiving and transmitting bureaus for record, and report it to the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Communications for filing.

(3) In addition to writing the text of cipher news telegrams in cipher, the original text shall be listed next to the code to facilitate review. The cipher code used shall be limited to four digits representing one Chinese character, and the fee shall be the same as for plain language news telegrams.

(4) The name and address of the receiving organization for cipher news telegrams shall be written in plain language, unless already registered. The word "Copress" shall be added before the name and address of the recipient as a paid identifier, counted as one word for billing purposes.

(5) If the cipher code of a cipher news telegram is found to be inconsistent with the deposited cipher codebook, or if there is any impropriety, the receiving and transmitting bureaus shall detain it and report it to the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Communications for cancellation of the news telegram transmission certificate.

According to the promulgation of the Provisional Regulations for Wireless Transmittal of Cipher News Telegrams issued by the Ministry of Communications in June of the eighteenth year of the Republic (1929), the content is not much different from the current measures. However, after the promulgation, very few news organizations utilized it, so the regulations were explicitly abolished in August of the twenty-second year of the Republic (1933). It is unexpected that after two years, domestic wireless news telegrams sent by the news media are often eavesdropped on, proving that cipher news telegram measures are indeed needed by the news industry, and the news media's initial failure to utilize them was a miscalculation. It is hoped that gentlemen of the news media will make full use of this meticulous and secure cipher news telegram measure in the future to protect their own interests!

Advantages of the Newly Revised Regulations for Paid Official Telegram Fees

— Bao Zhen

If senders or recipients have any questions, corrections, supplements, or cancellations regarding any part of a telegram received or sent, they can request the telegraph bureau to send a paid official telegram according to the regulations. However, senders and recipients often do not know how to use the paid official telegram method and instead directly telegraph the other party for inquiries or request corrections, supplements, or cancellations of any part of the original telegram, resulting in the loss of telegram fees. They then negotiate with the telegraph bureau to refund the fees for the original telegram or the inquiry telegram sent. From the telegraph bureau's perspective, according to the regulations, there is no obligation to refund the fees for such cases. However, from the sender's or recipient's perspective, they believe that the telegraph bureau's service is inadequate and does not provide sufficient convenience to the public, which inevitably leads to various misunderstandings. Recently, the Ministry of Communications revised and standardized the regulations for paid official telegram fees, which will take effect on August 1, 1935. I would like to explain the advantages of this measure in detail so that the public can thoroughly understand and fully utilize the paid official telegram method.

(1) If the recipient has any doubts about any part of the received telegram (including the address, text, signature, etc.) and believes that there is an error in transmission, they can take the telegram to the telegraph bureau and request the sending of a paid official telegram to inquire with the original sending bureau or forward the inquiry to the sender. All official telegrams back and forth are free of charge, except when the text of the original telegram was provided by the sender. The implementation of this free inquiry method for questionable words in incoming telegrams has been praised by all sectors.

(2) If the incoming telegram does not have the sender's signature and the recipient does not know who sent it, or if the recipient does not know the sender's current address and cannot send a reply telegram, they can request the telegraph bureau to send a paid official telegram on their behalf to inquire with the sending bureau. This official telegram is free of charge, and the requester only needs to prepay the fee for a six-word reply telegram. (If the original telegram is a domestic Chinese or foreign language telegram, regardless of the type or text, the reply telegram fee is calculated according to the domestic Chinese plain language or foreign commercial telegram rates. If the original telegram is an international telegram, regardless of the type or text, the reply telegram fee is calculated at the full rate for international commercial telegrams. However, if the requester does not want the sending bureau to reply by telegram and only needs a postal reply, the domestic postage is only the cost of a registered letter, and the international postage is only 80 centimes for registered mail). According to the old regulations, the requester had to pay the official telegram fee word by word, but with the implementation of the new regulations, the requester can save a telegram fee.

(3) If the sending bureau informs the sender that the telegram could not be delivered because the recipient's name and address are incomplete or incorrect, the sender can immediately request the telegraph bureau to send a paid official telegram to notify the receiving bureau to supplement or correct the recipient's name and address in the original telegram and then resend it. The words added for supplementation or correction are charged word by word. For example, supplementing the recipient's address with five words only costs the fee for five words. Correcting the recipient's name or address by one word only costs the fee for one word. According to the old regulations, the sender had to pay for the entire telegram based on the total number of words it contained. With the implementation of the new regulations, the sender can also reduce part of the telegram fee.

Development of International Wireless Telephony

— Guang

This article only covers the wireless telephone network centered on London, the capital of England. Other countries are not mentioned.

The beginning of international long-distance wireless telephony dates back to 1923 in the Western calendar. At that time, the British Post Office and the American Telegraph and Telephone Company cooperated in research, planning to build wireless telephone services on both sides of the Atlantic. At that time, the propagation characteristics of short waves had not yet been clarified, so it was decided to use long-wave communication.

After this plan was decided, both parties began to observe the propagation characteristics of radio waves in this line to determine the applicable wavelength and the power of the transmitter, so that it could be smooth and unobstructed throughout the year, regardless of season, day or night. The observation results showed that a transmitter with a power of 200 kilowatts, using a single-sideband suppressed carrier system, and a directional antenna on the receiving side, could realize commercial operations. Therefore, the United Kingdom and the United States worked hard to achieve success as soon as possible to benefit commerce. On the British side, the transmitting station was installed in Rugby, and the receiving station was initially installed in Wionghton and later moved to CuparEfei. The control components were all installed in the international exchange in London. On the American side, the transmitting station was installed in Rocky poin long Island, and the receiving station was installed in Houlton Maine. The control machine was installed in the New York exchange. In January 1927, commercial wireless telephone service was officially opened between London and New York, so residents of the two places could talk to each other on ordinary telephones, which shows its convenience.

The Anglo-American wireless telephone service was opened not long ago and achieved very satisfactory results. The lines were immediately expanded to both ends. The British end expanded to the entire United Kingdom and the European continent, while the American end connected to countries such as Canada, Mexico, and Cuba. As a result, business increased sharply, and the original long-wave lines were insufficient. At this time, short-wave radio developed extremely rapidly, and its applicability to long-distance communication was a very obvious fact. The United Kingdom and the United States conducted short-wave wireless telephone experiments on both sides of the Atlantic Ocean to obtain appropriate short-wave wireless telephone equipment.

In June 1928, the short-wave wireless telephone experiment was successful, and the commercial line was officially opened for communication. In June and December of the following year, two more short-wave telephone lines were added to meet commercial needs.

In February 1930, the British wireless telephone business with ships was officially opened. In April, communication with South America also began.

Between 1932 and 1933, the United Kingdom successively opened wireless telephone services with South Africa, Canada, Egypt, and India. In March of this year, communication between London and Tokyo was also officially opened.

Observing the above-mentioned development of wireless telephony, it can be seen that London has become one of the centers of the world's wireless telephone network. The original receiving station was not sufficient, so it was moved to Baldcck in 1930. The new station covers an area of 900 acres, with more than 30 directional antennas, which shows the scale.

In addition to being the center of the world's wireless network, London also has submarine cables connecting major European cities. Therefore, major cities in the world that communicate with London, whether wireless or submarine cable, can be connected through London, making global electrical communication more convenient.

The technical difficulties of wireless telephony have been resolved by the efforts of manufacturers in the United States and other countries over the past few years. The clarity of wireless communication is now no different from that of urban telephones.

It is generally recognized that submarine cable telephony is only suitable for shorter distances due to the difficulty of loading. Therefore, radio is the exclusive product of long-distance telephones (over thousands of miles). With its low cost and clear communication, its future development is limitless.

Although the development of my country's radio business is later than that of Germany and the United States, the communication with European and American countries is being actively prepared by the relevant authorities of the Ministry of Communications and will soon be a reality. The development of international communication can be foreseen.

Revenue and Expenditure Report of the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Communications for the Twenty-Third Year of the Republic (1934)

— Yun

In the past year, the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Communications has been rectifying various businesses, striving to commercialize the telecommunications industry. The reorganization of financial aspects, such as improving revenue and expenditure methods, repaying domestic and foreign debts, and paying interest on telegraph fee deposits (i.e., the telegraph fee deposit guarantee system), have also been implemented one by one. Among them, the implementation of unified revenue and expenditure has been particularly effective. The details of the process and the revenue and expenditure report for the past year are briefly described below:

The unified revenue and expenditure method was implemented on July 1 of last year. The Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Communications signed an agency payment contract and a method for collecting telegraph and telephone fees with the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau. All telegraph and telephone bureaus and radio stations under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Communications, totaling more than eighty locations, should remit their telegraph and telephone fee revenue to the local Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for temporary deposit into the Telecommunications Department's unified account in the Shanghai Savings and Remittance Bureau. The bureaus and stations make a request form based on their actual monthly operating expenses and submit it to the Telecommunications Department for detailed review. After verification, the Savings and Remittance Bureau is notified to instruct the local Savings Bureaus to disburse the funds on schedule. The Savings and Remittance Bureau receives the telegraph and telephone fees remitted from various places, fills out a daily report form, and compiles a monthly summary of revenue and expenditure, which is sent to the Telecommunications Department for mutual verification with the reports from various bureaus and stations and for timely accounting. The auditing method is extremely strict, and the previous abuses of excessive withdrawals, fraudulent reporting, misappropriation, and arrears have been almost completely eliminated. This is the most significant benefit for the Telecommunications Department. The Postal Bureau can also use these deposits as various investments, and the benefits obtained are also considerable. Since the implementation of this method, the personnel involved on both sides have been able to cooperate sincerely and deal with all difficulties. The original contract period was set for a trial period of six months. The trial period expired in December of last year, and both parties agreed to extend it for another six months. The period expired again at the end of June of this year, and it was agreed to extend it for another year.

From July of last year to the end of June of this year, the total revenue was over 8.134 million yuan, and the expenditure was approximately 9.355 million yuan. The difference between revenue and expenditure was actually a deficit of 1.22 million yuan, with an average monthly deficit of 100,000 yuan. This deficit was temporarily overdrawn from the Savings and Remittance Bureau in accordance with the contract. All overdrawn principal and interest have been paid in full from time to time. The detailed figures for the annual revenue and expenditure are listed below.

Answering Mr. Kang Dingji from Zhenjiang's Question

— Zhong Xian

I recently received your letter, inquiring about the charging method of using telephone numbers to replace the recipient's address. I will provide a summary of the answers as follows:

Answer (1) Telegrams using telephone numbers instead of the recipient's address, such as "Peiping telephone East 2105 Wang Cheng" or "Shanghai telephone concession 94013 Tu Xiaochao," are charged as four words. However, if the receiving bureau needs to transmit the telegram to the recipient by telephone, the sender should add the word "telephone transmission" or (TF) in the fee identification column, which is counted as one word along with the telephone number book. The writing format is as follows: "TF telephone concession 8123311 Shanghai Gao Bingjun." Charged as five words. According to the above examples, if the telephone number is used to replace the recipient's address and the receiving bureau uses the local telephone bureau number to find the recipient's address and then delivers the telegram by messenger, the location and recipient's name are counted as four words. If the receiving bureau needs to transmit the telegram to the recipient by telephone, an additional "telephone transmission" or (TF) fee identification is added, and the telephone number, location, and recipient's name are counted as five words. As for the telephone number replacing the recipient's address, along with the TF fee identification, it can be counted as one word in foreign language telegrams. However, the recipient's name and location must be charged separately word by word. For example, TFSettlement 79542=Smith Shangbai should be charged as three words.

Answer (2) Article 5 of the method for using telephone numbers to replace the recipient's address is somewhat ambiguous. The Telecommunications Department has already telegraphed all bureaus on September 10, 1934, instructing that "the format of the location and recipient's name and address written in accordance with the first example of item A of Article 4 of the method for using telephone numbers to replace the recipient's address, that is, "Peiping telephone East 2105 Wang Cheng," should be charged as four words, and the second example should still be charged as five words." After the above telegram was clearly explained, the various telegraph bureaus should no longer have any misunderstandings. Although the writing format of the above examples is different, the distinction is very clear regarding the method and there is no contradiction.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Discussions

Written on the Opening Day of Children's Year

— Meng Ruo

Ellen Key said: "The 20th century is the century of children." All civilized countries in the world have long had regulations for Children's Day. They all pay close attention to children's causes, so that children can obtain full happiness in the embrace of society. Even our backward China has a four-year history of holding Children's Year. Until this year, the Central Government, in order to expand children's activities, has stipulated that from August 1 of this year to July 30 of next year, it will be Children's Year, engaging in various promotions. This meaning is even more significant. Today is the opening day of China's Children's Year.

Chinese children have never been valued by society. Their position is only the private property of the family. How do we know that children are the masters of society, the country, and the nation? The future progress of society, the strength of the country, and the prosperity of the nation are all entrusted to the children of today. The 20th century society takes children as the center, which is humanity's greatest realization.

The expectations of Children's Year for children, in general, are nothing more than wanting Chinese children to become healthy citizens in the future so that they can seek welfare for society, the country, and the nation. But how can children become healthy citizens? This is to pay attention to the education of children. We should give each Chinese child a considerable education so that their body and mind can develop freely.

Regarding the education of children, China has always placed this responsibility on the family. Originally, family education was most suitable for children. But Chinese families treat children as private property. Therefore, parents in the family arbitrarily mold them into a model according to their own wishes. Wealthy families can only raise some pampered and lazy children, while ordinary families only produce a batch of ignorant children. This is detrimental to society.

Therefore, children in the future should be liberated from the family so that they can become social members instead of being private property of the family. The realization of Children's Year must first raise the status and rights of children. Then, society should teach and nurture them in the best way so that they can become healthy citizens with full wisdom, vibrant life, full spirit, strong physique, rich thought, and pure character.

But my proposition does not mean that the education of children should be borne entirely by society and that the family should not be involved at all. What I mean is that since children are the core of social organization, society should guide and handle all issues related to the education of children. And the family needs to change its original concept, take the welfare of the people as a prerequisite, and fulfill its due obligations to its children.

As for society to educate children, there should be sufficient facilities for various social undertakings, such as children's parks, children's libraries, children's sports fields, children's training institutions, nurseries, and juvenile reformatories. These undertakings have become commonplace in foreign countries, but they have not yet been held in our country. This is what we should pay attention to.

There is one thing that must be specially mentioned here, that is, Children's Year should be universal, not partial. Society should educate children, not only a few special classes, but also the children of most poor families. This is the happiness of Chinese children, and it is also the true meaning of the government's Children's Year this year.

Today's China has fallen into a crisis-ridden situation, and the future disasters may be even worse than today. Therefore, adults cannot shirk their responsibility for the work of saving the country, and children should also strive hard. Because the important task of revitalizing the nation in the future is waiting for the children of today to shoulder. On this opening day of Children's Year, we expect this from our beloved children in China.

Faded Story

— Er He

The story is about loquats, but the loquat season has long passed, and the story took place a distant ten years ago, so I think this story must be faded.

When I first came to Shanghai, my family wanted me to return home once during the loquat season. At first, I agreed wholeheartedly. My original intention was not to perfunctory, but I really wanted to return home to eat a big meal of loquats. But after arriving in Shanghai, I really lived a muddled life. Watching baskets and baskets of golden loquats go on the market, my heart really wanted to fly over the Yangtze River to the loquat courtyard in the north. My family wrote several times, saying that the loquats were about to ripen, saying that the loquats were full of trees, but I was lazy and couldn't muster the interest to go back.

Recently, the scorching sun is in the sky, and I am determined to return to the countryside. Knowing that I will not be able to eat loquats anyway on this trip, I still think of loquats day and night, and even in my dreams I see golden loquats hanging on the branches...

Ten years ago, when I was still a child, from the time the loquats bloomed, I cared about their growth every day. At that time, my grandmother had not yet passed away. The old lady had nothing to do all day long, and she cared about the loquats every day like a child. From the time the loquats turned yellow, she used all her strength to deal with the loquat trees. During the day, she lay sideways on a bamboo chair that was so ripe it was red, and watched the loquat trees all day long. At night, she didn't even light the kerosene lamp, and she still lay sideways on a bamboo chair that was so ripe it was red, guarding the loquat trees. Originally, there was no need to guard them, but we children were too wild. We still wanted to eat green loquats, and of course the yellow loquats were in danger. So grandmother had to guard them, and if necessary, use her only weapon - a cane - to beat the children who stole loquats.

Of course, I was extremely afraid. Although I wanted to steal them, I pretended to be very docile in front of my grandmother.

Page 26

a very obedient child. Therefore, grandmother especially treasured me among the children, but the so-called treasure was only said verbally, and I could not get golden loquats because of it. In desperation, I still had to resort to "stealing." Because I was too tired at night, I fell asleep deeply as soon as I got into bed. When I woke up, everything was silent, and of course it was still late at night. So I secretly got up and climbed up the loquat tree. At that time, everything was quiet except for the dog who knew me well wagging its tail at me. I picked big and yellow loquats and ate them under the stars. One by one, I ate until my jaw was sore before climbing down, falling on the bed, and sleeping soundly. The next day, in front of my grandmother, I was still a very docile and obedient child.

My father and mother were too frugal, so buying fruit was not allowed. That's why I could only satisfy my only desire in a moment of the night.

Grandmother picked the golden loquats and hid them inside, not even willing to eat them freely herself. Of course, I didn't understand this at the time. When the loquats turned color and were about to rot, she beckoned me and gave me five or six, which was a great gift in her eyes, because she treasured me. As for the other children, they didn't even get the rotten ones.

Now my grandmother has passed away, and the story has long faded, but I chew on this story every time I see golden loquats every year. If I go back during the loquat season in recent years, of course I can eat loquats to my heart's content. But as I get older, my interest fades. The irretrievable childhood is just like the irretrievable setting sun going west... I am anxious to return home, the weeds on my grandmother's grave are probably green again, and soon, the hot summer will pass and the clear autumn will come, and the green weeds should be withered and yellow again.

Gambling Rush

— Ding Weinan

Turning a corner, the deep, long alley was left behind. My footsteps stretched my shadow long, the vast, dark square covered my vision, and in the distant woods, dogs howled.

Bright light shone from the town over there.

It was still two or three li to get there!

"Old Three, pick up the pace, it's getting late! Maybe some stalls are already closed, and we need to try our luck too!" The one calling out to Old Three reeked of alcohol. He was staggering and waving his hand. Although it was dark and his face couldn't be seen clearly, the outline of his shadow was visible. He kicked a small stone, and with a thud, he stumbled, as if in slight pain.

"Hey, drunkard, Old Huang's 'Azure Dragon' game last night, I really predicted it accurately. There really was a 'way' to win! One bet, and I overturned the whole stall! I really have the skill. If you weren't with me, you'd surely lose money!" Old Three's voice echoed in the darkness, and you could see him gesturing with his big fingers.

"Stop bragging! Are you really that accurate? If you were so rich, why does your wife still scold you like a dead pig?" The dark shadow behind Old Three interjected, indistinctly. It sounded like he was tilting his head a few times, and perhaps making a mocking sound, shrugging his shoulders.

"How could I not be accurate? You useless fool, I've been hustling outside longer than all of you... As for my wife scolding me, hah, she wouldn't dare!"

"Stop running your mouth, we can all see it!"

"The drunkard is actually afraid of his wife," Old Three teased. "He secretly drank some wine tonight. When I passed his door, he secretly winked at me. Of course, his wife was eating beside him, but I knew he was telling me to wait for him. Drunkard, isn't that right?" He turned his head to look back, leading the way.

"Isn't that the truth? Last night was really noisy. Luckily, he hadn't lost any money and was able to show her some, which calmed things down. She really keeps a tight rein on him. He's definitely a wife-dominated man! Haha, Drunkard, you!"

The drunkard didn't respond, walking with his head tilted to the side.

The sound of gongs and drums reached their ears. The stars hid in the high sky, squinting their eyes. The Earth was watching, the moon had not yet rolled out.

They strode forward, the darkness kept at bay by the circle of light. In front of the Kang Wang Temple, many small vendors had set up stalls on the ground, with a scattering of melon seed shells and the suffocating, dizzying smell of fried oil. Countless faces, old, young, male, and female, were all facing the gambling tables, turning their backs to the bodhisattvas in the temple. The atmosphere was strangely murky.

The three men's heads were squeezed into the crowd around the gambling stalls. Bright gas lamps hung high above, so bright you could see a fallen needle on the ground. Dice jumped around in the treasure box, clanging and tinkling. With a cry of "Azure Dragon" or "Tiger," the gamblers' faces turned either flushed or pale.

Like foam merging into the sea, their shadows disappeared, everything lost in the shouts and cheers of the gambling game!

The Bamboo Buzz (Part 1)

— Tian Hu

One afternoon, a few days after returning home, I was fanning myself with a palm leaf fan under a large locust tree, enjoying the cool. Suddenly, I saw my fourth younger brother in the threshing ground, flapping his arms and energetically spinning a bamboo buzz toy.

"Buzz... buzz..." The continuous sound gradually broke the silence of the meadow. Behind my fourth brother, many children watched the bamboo buzz, which seemed like a strange object, with envious expressions.

My fourth brother was very proud. After he stopped spinning the toy, his companions surrounded him with flattering expressions, talking to him. He used an assertive tone to tell his companions about the origins of the bamboo buzz.

Indeed, in our village, this bamboo buzz was still a rare object. My fourth brother's was bought from Old Kunhe's teahouse in Saint Hall. I don't know why, but Old Kunhe had a flash of inspiration this time and ordered this item from the city. Yesterday, I took my fourth brother to the teahouse and happened to see it, so I bought one for him.

My fourth brother seemed tired of playing. He tied the two bamboo sticks and a bamboo rod into a ball shape with a drawstring, held it on his head, and went into the house with a very proud expression, while his companions watched with envy.

The scene made me feel somewhat disgusted. I saw my fourth brother and said to him, "Just because you have a bamboo buzz, you act like you've found a treasure and show off in front of others. You have one, and they don't. Be careful of making others unhappy; they might not want to play with you!"

"They don't have one, they're all jealous of me, especially Little Fire Root..." My fourth brother quickly turned his head. He seemed to know that if he said too much, I would scold him, so he ended his sentence with a gentle smile, ending what he wanted to say.

Two days later, in the afternoon, I was sitting by the west window reading a book when suddenly, a loud buzzing sound and children's chatter filled the air. Disturbed, I strolled to the threshing ground and saw eight or nine children from the village, who usually gathered together, all with bamboo buzz toys, having a great time spinning them with the drawstrings. My fourth brother was also among them, jumping around the busiest. But ten steps away from the group, stood a very ugly child, sticking out his thumb, watching the lively group with a silly grin. As soon as I saw his left eye drooping, I recognized him: it was Little Fire, the son of Bing Sheng, who sells salty soup in the village. (To be continued)

News

There are excerpts from Yu Yuxing's "To Harmonica Lovers," Zhao Qi's "Practice Method of Polyphonic Accompaniment," Bao Mingshan's "Knowledge of Harmonica," Zhao Xiaodong's "Harmonica Repair Method," "Evaluation of Music Performance Technology by All Reporters," Harmonica Famous Songs, Beginner's "Past Spring Dreams" (Love Overture), Advanced "Boy Ma" (Decomposed Chord Playing Method), and Mr. Bao Mingshan, the editor and publisher of this magazine, will personally teach the music language symbols and playing methods of this song at Huamei Radio Station from 11:00 am this Sunday. In addition, this issue of the magazine "Youth Supplement" contains Gu Xingyan's article on movie star Chen Boer, Zhang Qingbo's "Talking about Women's Clothing," the Outdated Society's "Masterpiece of Photography," etc. A sample copy will be mailed immediately with postage from other provinces. This magazine is sold in newspapers and magazine companies and bookstores in other provinces. The annual subscription including postage is one yuan and two jiao.

"Suppressing Bandits' Great Achievements" Public Screening

"Suppressing Bandits' Victory" is the bloody history of the US government's declaration of war against bandits and their victory. In the attack of justice against evil, I don't know how many loyal and brave soldiers sacrificed their lives for the country. This film faithfully engraves the entire struggle and hand-to-hand combat of the so-called secret detective team on the screen. Iron and blood are the components of the film's organization, and intelligence and power are the artistic expressions of the film. If the reader looks at the stars participating in this film, they can understand the true value of the film. The leading actors are Ang Balimua, the head star of the Pa Brothers, Qian Yashan, the heroine of "Scandal in the City," Jishi Malis, the protagonist of "The Truth Comes Out," and Joseph Garia, Paul Keller, and Louis Stone. At the same time, the most valuable masterpiece of MGM's five-color American art music film "Walking Chicken" is added. It is truly rare and valuable to open the summer with such a good film.
